Taharah — Purification
beginner
6 min
Intention in Tayammum vs Wudu: Distinct Rulings
Ruling on the status of intention in tayammum and wudu.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on intention in wudu and tayammum and identify the Quranic proof for this distinction.

Core Idea
Intention is obligatory in tayammum but only recommended in wudu — a unique Hanafi distinction.

The Hanafi school treats intention differently in wudu and tayammum. While most schools require intention for both, the Hanafis make a distinction based on the nature of the act. This lesson examines the ruling and its Quranic evidence.

Guided Path
1
State the two rulings
From the passage, identify that intention is fard (obligatory) in tayammum and mustahabb (recommended) in wudu.
2
Identify the proof
The author cites the Quranic verse Al-Ma'idah 5:6, which commands tayammum. Note how the imperative indicates obligation.
The verse reference is commonly given as Al-Ma'idah 5:6, though the source text writes 'Surah an-Nisa 5, verse 6'.
3
Understand the rationale for tayammum
Tayammum is a substitute (badal) for wudu. Intention is required to distinguish it from ordinary wiping of the face and hands.
Hanafi usul: a substitute inherits the ruling of the original if it requires distinction.
4
Understand the rationale for wudu
Wudu is a clear physical act of washing specific limbs. Intention is not needed for validity because the act itself indicates the purpose.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) require intention in both wudu and tayammum. The Hanafi position is a minority view but well-established.
The passage does not elaborate on the ikhtilaf, but it is important for context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالنِّيَّةُ فَرْضٌ فِي التَّيَمُّمِ مُسْتَحَبَّةٌ فِي الْوُضُوءِ . د وجه: (ا) الآية لثبوت وَالنِّيَّةُ فَرْضٌ فِي التَّيَمُّمِ مُسْتَحَبَّةٌ فِي الْوُضُوءِ \ ﴿فَلَمْ تَجِدُوا مَآءَ فَتَيَمَّمُوا صَعِيدًا طَيِّبًا فَأَمْسَحُواْ بِوُجُوهِكُمْ وَأَيْدِيكُمْ﴾ (سورة النساء5 ، آيت نمبر 6) اصول : وضو اور تیم کی نیت کی حیثیت الگ الگ ہے ، وضو میں نیت مستحب، جبکہ تیم میں نیت فرض ہے۔
And intention is obligatory (fard) in tayammum, recommended (mustahabb) in wudu. Evidence (1) The verse for the proof: '...so perform tayammum with pure soil...' (Surah an-Nisa 5, verse 6). Principle: The status of intention in wudu and tayammum is different; intention in wudu is mustahabb, while in tayammum it is fard.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage establishes that the ruling of intention (niyyah) differs between wudu and tayammum. In wudu, intention is mustahabb (recommended) according to the Hanafi school, meaning wudu is valid even without explicit intention. In tayammum, however, intention is fard (obligatory); without it, the tayammum is invalid. The proof cited is the Quranic verse '...fa-tayammamu sa'idan tayyiban...' which commands the act of tayammum. The Hanafi interpretation is that since tayammum is a substitute for purification, it requires intention to distinguish it from mere wiping. For wudu, the default understanding is that it is a physical act of cleanliness, and intention is not a condition for its validity. The usul note at the end reiterates this distinction.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): Intention; in tayammum it is fard (obligatory), in wudu mustahabb (recommended).
فرض (fard): An obligatory element; omission invalidates the act.
مستحب (mustahabb): Recommended; omission does not make the act invalid but one loses reward.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling of intention (niyyah) in wudu according to the Hanafi school?
A) Fard (obligatory)
B) Mustahabb (recommended)
C) Sunnah mu'akkadah
D) Makruh

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes intention in wudu and tayammum: fard in tayammum, mustahabb in wudu, based on the nature of the acts.

Nullifiers of Tayammum and the Condition of Pure Soil
Ruling on nullifiers and condition of tayammum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the nullifiers of tayammum and state the requirement of pure soil with its evidence from the Quran and hadith.

Core Idea
Tayammum is nullified by all wudu nullifiers plus seeing water; only pure soil is valid.

This passage is a concise ruling on what invalidates tayammum and what substance is required for it. It establishes two key principles: first, that tayammum shares all nullifiers of wudu, with the addition of seeing water when one is able to use it; second, that tayammum is only valid with pure soil (sa'id tahir). The ruling is supported by the Quranic verse commanding tayammum with pure soil and the hadith of Abu Dhar. Understanding these rules is essential for maintaining valid purification in the absence of water.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main rulings
The passage begins with the nullifiers of tayammum and then states the condition of pure soil. Identify both parts clearly.
2
Recognize the nullifiers of wudu
Recall the nullifiers of wudu (e.g., urination, defecation, wind, sleep, loss of mind). The passage states that all of these also nullify tayammum.
This is based on qiyas: tayammum is a substitute for wudu.
3
Understand the unique nullifier: seeing water
Tayammum is also nullified specifically by seeing water when one is able to use it. This is because tayammum is a temporary substitute – when water becomes available, the substitute ends.
Hanafis hold that mere sight nullifies, not just actual usage.
4
Note the condition of pure soil
The passage requires that tayammum must be performed with pure soil (sa'id tahir). 'Pure' means free from najasah (impurity).
The Arabic term 'tayyib' in the Quran is interpreted as 'tahir' (pure) by Hanafis.
5
Examine the evidence
The passage cites the Quran (Al-Ma'idah 5:6) and the hadith of Abu Dhar. Understand how these texts prove the requirement of pure soil and the nullification upon finding water.
The hadith explicitly states that when water is found, it should be used, implying tayammum ends.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَنْقُضُ التَّيَمُّمَ كُلُّ شَيْءٍ يَنْقُضُ الْوُضُوءَ وَيَنْقُضُهُ أَيْضًا رُؤْيَةُ الْمَاءِ إِذَا قَدَرَ عَلَى اسْتِعْمَالِهِ وَلَا يَجُوزُ التَّيَمُّمُ إِلَّا بِالصَّعِيدِ الطَّاهِرِ . د وجه : (۱)الأية لثبوت وَلَا يَجُوزُ التَّيَمُّمُ إِلَّا بِالصَّعِيدِ الطَّاهِرِ \ ﴿فَلَمْ تَجِدُوا مَاءً فَتَيَمَّمُوا صَعِيدًا طَيِّبًا فَأَمْسَحُوا بِوُجُوهِكُمْ وَأَيْدِيكُمْ) (سورة النساء5 ، آيت نمبر 6) وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ لَمْ يَجِدْ الْمَاءَ وَهُوَ مُسَافِرٌ \ فَقَالَ: أَبُو ذَرٍ... فَقَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: " يَا أَبَا ذَرّ: إِنَّ الصَّعِيدَ الطَّيِّبَ طَهُورٌ ، وَإِنْ لَمْ تَجِدِ الْمَاءَ إِلَى عَشْرِ سِنِينَ، فَإِذَا وَجَدْتَ الْمَاءَ، فَأَمِسَّهُ جِلْدَكَ ابو داؤد ، بَابُ الْجُنُبِ يَتَيَمَّمُ، غبر 333)
And tayammum is nullified by everything that nullifies wudu, and it is also nullified by seeing water when one is able to use it. And tayammum is not valid except with pure soil. Evidence (1) The verse for the proof: '...so perform tayammum with pure soil...' Evidence (2) The hadith for the proof: Abu Dhar said... The Prophet said: 'Indeed pure soil is a purification, even if you do not find water for ten years, and when you find water, let it touch your skin.' (Abu Dawud).
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage states two things: (1) The nullifiers of tayammum are the same as those of wudu (e.g., urination, defecation, wind, loss of mind, sleep, etc.), with the additional nullifier of seeing water when one is able to use it. This is because tayammum is a substitute for water; when water becomes available, the substitute is no longer valid. (2) The condition for tayammum is that it must be performed with pure soil (sa'id tahir). The Quranic verse commands 'tayammamu sa'idan tayyiban' (pure soil), and the hadith of Abu Dhar emphasizes that pure soil is a purification even if water is unavailable for years. The Hanafi school emphasizes that the soil must be pure (tahir), free from najasah.

Key Terms
ينقض (yanqud): Nullifies; makes the purification invalid, requiring a new tayammum.
رؤية الماء (ru'yat al-ma'): The sight of water; when a person sees water and is able to use it, tayammum is nullified.
صعيد طاهر (sa'id tahir): Pure soil; soil that is free from any impurity (najis).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a nullifier of tayammum according to the passage?
A) Passing wind
B) Seeing water while able to use it
C) Sleeping
D) Entering a mosque

Key Takeaway
Tayammum shares all nullifiers of wudu, plus seeing water ends it; only pure soil is valid.

The Recommendation to Delay Prayer When Hoping for Water
Ruling on delaying prayer for hope of water

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on delaying prayer for one who hopes to find water and explain its mustahabb status using the athar from Alqamah.

Core Idea
Delaying prayer is recommended, not obligatory, when hoping for water; it reflects optimism and reliance on Allah.

This lesson focuses on the first part of the passage: the recommendation to delay prayer if one does not have water but hopes to find it before the time ends. The ruling is based on the practice of the early Muslims, as transmitted by Alqamah. We will explore why it is mustahabb and not wajib, and how this balances practicality with religious devotion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal category
The act is delaying prayer to the end of its time for one who lacks water but hopes to find it. Determine its hukm level: is it obligatory, recommended, or permitted?
Look for the term 'yustahab' in the text.
2
Locate the proof
The text cites an athar from Alqamah about a junub traveler waiting until the end of the time. Identify this as a qawl sahabi (statement of a companion) and understand its authority in Hanafi fiqh.
Alqamah was a tabi'i, but the report reflects companion practice.
3
Understand the rationale
Why delay? The hope of finding water allows performance of prayer with water, which is superior. Delaying is a way to seek the better option without neglecting the prayer obligation.
It is not obligatory because the primary obligation is to pray within the time, and tayammum is a valid substitute.
4
Contrast with other positions
Consider that some schools may view delaying as obligatory if water is expected, or as impermissible if it risks missing the time. The Hanafi view is the middle path.
No explicit dispute is mentioned in the passage, but awareness of ikhtilaf is useful.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيُسْتَحَبُّ لِمَنْ لَمْ يَجِدْ الْمَاءَ وَهُوَ يَرْجُو أَنْ يَجِدَهُ فِي آخِرِ الْوَقْتِ أَنْ يُؤَخِّرَ الصَّلَاةَ إِلَى آخِرِ الْوَقْتِ وَهُوَ يَرْجُو ١٠ وَيُصَلِّي بِتَيَمُّمِهِ مَا شَاءَ مِنْ الْفَرَائِضِ وَالنَّوَافِلِ د. وجه: (ا)قول الصحابي لثبوت وَيُسْتَحَبُّ لِمَنْ لَمْ يَجِدْ الْمَاءَ \ عَنْ عَلِقٍ, قَالَ: «إِذَا أَجْنَبَ الرَّجُلُ فِي السَّفَرِ تَلَوَّمَ مَا بَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَ آخِرِ الْوَقْتِ, فَإِنْ لَمْ يَجِدِ الْمَاءَ تَيَمَّمَ وَصَلَّى»(سنن الدار قطنِي، بَابٌ فِي بَيَانِ الْمَوْضِعِ الَّذِي يَجُوزُ التَّيَمُّمُ فِيهِ ، نمبر 720 / السنن الكبري للبيهقي، بَابُ مَنْ تَلَوَّمَ مَا بَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَ آخِرِ الْوَقْتِ رَجَاءَ وُجُودِ الْمَاءِ، نمبر 1101) ١٠ وجه : (۱) الآية لثبوت وَيُصَلِّي بِتَيَمُّمِهِ مَا شَاءَمِنْ الْفَرَائِضِ وَالنَّوَافِلِ \ ﴿مَا يُرِيدُ اللَّهُ لِيَجْعَلَ عَلَيْكُم مِّنْ حَرَجٍ وَلَكِن يُرِيدُ لِيُطَهِّرَكُمْ وَلِيُتِمَّ نِعْمَتَهُ عَلَيْكُمْ ﴾ (سورة المائدة 5 أيت نمبر 6) وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَيُصَلِّي بِتَيَمُّمِهِ مَا شَاءَمِنْ الْفَرَائِضِ وَالنَّوَافِلِ \ إِنَّ الصَّعِيدَ الطَّيِّبَ طَهُورٌ، وَإِنْ لَمْ تَجِدِ الْمَاءَ إِلَى عَشْرِ سِنِينَ، ابو داؤد، بَابُ الْجُنُبِ يَتَيَمَّمُ، غير (333)
And it is recommended for one who does not find water, and he hopes to find it at the end of the time, to delay the prayer to the end of the time while he hopes (to find water). And he may pray with his tayammum as many obligatory and voluntary prayers as he wishes. Evidence (1) statement of a companion for the proof: From Alqamah, he said: 'When a man becomes junub on a journey, he should wait until the end of the time; if he does not find water, he performs tayammum and prays.' Evidence (1) the verse for the proof: 'Allah intends ease for you, not hardship...' (5:6). Evidence (2) the hadith for the proof: 'Indeed pure soil is a purification, even if you do not find water for ten years.'
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage addresses two practical rulings for the traveler without water. First, it is mustahabb (recommended) to delay the prayer until the end of its time if one hopes to find water before the time expires. This is based on the practice of Alqamah (a tabi'i) as reported in the hadith, showing the teaching of the Companions. Second, once a valid tayammum is performed, one can pray multiple obligatory and voluntary prayers with that same tayammum until it is nullified (by seeing water, etc.). This is supported by the Quranic verse indicating ease and the hadith that pure soil is a purification even for ten years, implying continuity of purification. The Hanafi position is that tayammum lifts the state of impurity until something nullifies it, so multiple prayers are valid without renewing tayammum.

Key Terms
يستحب (yustahab): It is recommended; doing it is rewarded, omitting it is not sinful.
يرجو (yarju): He hopes; expects with a reasonable basis.
تلوّم (talawwama): He waited, delayed, tarried.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the hukm of delaying prayer for one who does not find water but hopes to find it?
A) Fard (obligatory)
B) Mustahabb (recommended)
C) Haram (forbidden)
D) Makruh (disliked)

Key Takeaway
Delaying prayer is recommended only when one hopes to find water; it is not obligatory, and the proof is the practice of early Muslims.

Multiple Prayers with One Tayammum
Ruling on multiple prayers with one tayammum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling that one tayammum suffices for multiple prayers, citing the Quranic and hadith proofs.

Core Idea
Tayammum purifies until nullified; one tayammum allows multiple prayers, showing Islam's ease.

The second ruling in our passage addresses a common question: when a traveler performs tayammum, can he pray more than one fard prayer with it? The text explicitly says 'he may pray as many obligatory and voluntary prayers as he wishes.' This lesson examines the proofs from Quran and hadith that support this position, and contrasts it with the view of other schools that require a new tayammum for each fard prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is performing multiple prayers with a single tayammum. The ruling is that it is permissible (ja'iz) and valid as long as the tayammum remains intact.
The phrase 'ma sha'a' indicates unrestricted number.
2
Examine the Quranic proof
The text cites Quran 5:6: 'Allah intends ease for you, not hardship.' Understand how this verse supports the permissibility of multiple prayers: requiring a new tayammum for each prayer would be hardship.
The verse is a general principle of ease (yusr), applied here.
3
Examine the hadith proof
The hadith 'Pure soil is a purification, even if you do not find water for ten years' is used. This implies that tayammum remains valid as a purification for an extended period, thus multiple prayers are valid.
The hadith is from Abu Dawud and is considered strong by Hanafis.
4
Understand the underlying principle
Tayammum, like wudu, is a state of purification. Once performed, it is not exhausted by one prayer; it remains until something nullifies it (e.g., finding water, breaking wudu, etc.).
This differs from the Shafi'i view that tayammum is a 'rukhsah' for a specific prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيُسْتَحَبُّ لِمَنْ لَمْ يَجِدْ الْمَاءَ وَهُوَ يَرْجُو أَنْ يَجِدَهُ فِي آخِرِ الْوَقْتِ أَنْ يُؤَخِّرَ الصَّلَاةَ إِلَى آخِرِ الْوَقْتِ وَهُوَ يَرْجُو ١٠ وَيُصَلِّي بِتَيَمُّمِهِ مَا شَاءَ مِنْ الْفَرَائِضِ وَالنَّوَافِلِ د. وجه: (ا)قول الصحابي لثبوت وَيُسْتَحَبُّ لِمَنْ لَمْ يَجِدْ الْمَاءَ \ عَنْ عَلِقٍ, قَالَ: «إِذَا أَجْنَبَ الرَّجُلُ فِي السَّفَرِ تَلَوَّمَ مَا بَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَ آخِرِ الْوَقْتِ, فَإِنْ لَمْ يَجِدِ الْمَاءَ تَيَمَّمَ وَصَلَّى»(سنن الدار قطنِي، بَابٌ فِي بَيَانِ الْمَوْضِعِ الَّذِي يَجُوزُ التَّيَمُّمُ فِيهِ ، نمبر 720 / السنن الكبري للبيهقي، بَابُ مَنْ تَلَوَّمَ مَا بَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَ آخِرِ الْوَقْتِ رَجَاءَ وُجُودِ الْمَاءِ، نمبر 1101) ١٠ وجه : (۱) الآية لثبوت وَيُصَلِّي بِتَيَمُّمِهِ مَا شَاءَمِنْ الْفَرَائِضِ وَالنَّوَافِلِ \ ﴿مَا يُرِيدُ اللَّهُ لِيَجْعَلَ عَلَيْكُم مِّنْ حَرَجٍ وَلَكِن يُرِيدُ لِيُطَهِّرَكُمْ وَلِيُتِمَّ نِعْمَتَهُ عَلَيْكُمْ ﴾ (سورة المائدة 5 أيت نمبر 6) وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَيُصَلِّي بِتَيَمُّمِهِ مَا شَاءَمِنْ الْفَرَائِضِ وَالنَّوَافِلِ \ إِنَّ الصَّعِيدَ الطَّيِّبَ طَهُورٌ، وَإِنْ لَمْ تَجِدِ الْمَاءَ إِلَى عَشْرِ سِنِينَ، ابو داؤد، بَابُ الْجُنُبِ يَتَيَمَّمُ، غير (333)
And it is recommended for one who does not find water, and he hopes to find it at the end of the time, to delay the prayer to the end of the time while he hopes (to find water). And he may pray with his tayammum as many obligatory and voluntary prayers as he wishes. Evidence (1) statement of a companion for the proof: From Alqamah, he said: 'When a man becomes junub on a journey, he should wait until the end of the time; if he does not find water, he performs tayammum and prays.' Evidence (1) the verse for the proof: 'Allah intends ease for you, not hardship...' (5:6). Evidence (2) the hadith for the proof: 'Indeed pure soil is a purification, even if you do not find water for ten years.'
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage addresses two practical rulings for the traveler without water. First, it is mustahabb (recommended) to delay the prayer until the end of its time if one hopes to find water before the time expires. This is based on the practice of Alqamah (a tabi'i) as reported in the hadith, showing the teaching of the Companions. Second, once a valid tayammum is performed, one can pray multiple obligatory and voluntary prayers with that same tayammum until it is nullified (by seeing water, etc.). This is supported by the Quranic verse indicating ease and the hadith that pure soil is a purification even for ten years, implying continuity of purification. The Hanafi position is that tayammum lifts the state of impurity until something nullifies it, so multiple prayers are valid without renewing tayammum.

Key Terms
تيمم (tayammum): Dry ablution using pure earth as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or harmful.
صعيد (sa'id): Pure earth, soil, or dust that can be used for tayammum.
فرائض ونوافل (fara'id wa nawafil): Obligatory and voluntary prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is a proof for performing multiple prayers with one tayammum?
A) The statement of Alqamah about delaying prayer
B) The Quranic verse 'Allah intends ease for you' (5:6)
C) The hadith about covering the head
D) The verse on fasting

Key Takeaway
One tayammum suffices for an unlimited number of prayers, supported by the Quranic principle of ease and the hadith on tayammum's lasting purification.

Tayammum for Funeral and Eid Prayers for a Healthy Person
Ruling with proof for tayammum when fearing loss of funeral/Eid prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tayammum for funeral and Eid prayers for a healthy resident and identify the proofs from the Companions and Successor.

Core Idea
Tayammum is permissible for a healthy resident when missing the funeral or Eid prayer is feared.

This lesson addresses a practical scenario: you are a healthy person in a city attending a funeral or Eid prayer, but you have no wudu. If performing wudu would cause you to miss the prayer, what should you do? The Hanafi school provides a dispensation: tayammum suffices. We will examine the ruling from al-Quduri's matn and the evidence that supports it, primarily from the statements of Ibn Abbas, Ibn Umar, and Ibrahim al-Nakha'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what action is being ruled upon and its legal classification. The act is tayammum performed by a healthy person in a city for funeral or Eid prayer when fearing loss of the prayer. The ruling is permissibility (jaiz/mubah).
2
Locate the evidence (dalil)
The author cites three proofs: (1) a general statement that tayammum is performed for every prayer; (2) a direct instruction from Ibn Abbas to perform tayammum if one fears missing the funeral; (3) a statement from Ibn Umar that the funeral prayer must be done in purity. For Eid, a statement from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i permits tayammum for the two Eids and funerals.
These are qawl sahabi (Companion's statement) and qawl tabi'i (Successor's statement), which are considered valid evidence in Hanafi usul.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (how the evidence proves the ruling)
The imperative 'tayammam' in Ibn Abbas's statement indicates permission. The general hadith 'tayammum is performed for every prayer' shows that tayammum is not restricted to specific conditions. The principle mentioned in the Urdu usul is that tayammum is allowed for any act that has a deputy or substitute.
The Hanafi school accepts these narrations as zanni al-thubut, but they are sufficient to establish permissibility.
4
Note the scope and conditions
The ruling applies only when: (1) the person is healthy and in a city (i.e., not on travel), (2) the funeral or Eid prayer is imminent, (3) performing wudu would cause missing the prayer, (4) the person is not the guardian (wali) of the deceased. For Eid, no guardian condition exists.
This is a specific exemption from the general rule that tayammum is only for travel or illness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ التَّيَمُّمِ ال وَيَجُوزُ التَّيَمُّمُ لِلصَّحِيح فِي الْمِصْرِ إِذَا حَضَرَتْ جِنَازَةٌ وَالْوَلِيُّ غَيْرُهُ فَخَافَ إِنَّ اشْتَغَلَ بِالطَّهَارَةِ أَنْ تَفُوتَهُ الصَّلَاةُ فَإِنَّهُ يَتَيَمَّمُ وَيُصَلِّي ١٢ وَكَذَلِكَ مَنْ حَضَرَ صَلَاةَ الْعِيدِ فَخَشِيَ إِنْ اشْتَغَلَ بِالطَّهَارَةِ أَنْ تَفُوتَهُ صَلَاةُ الْعِيدِ . ال وجه : (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَيَجُوزُ التَّيَمُّمُ لِلصَّحِيح فِي الْمِصْرِ إِذَا حَضَرَتْ جِنَازَةٌ «يُتَيَمَّمُ لِكُلِّ صَلَاةٍ» (سنن الدار قطني، بَابُ التَّيَمُّم وَأَنَّهُ يُفْعَلُ لِكُلِّ صَلَاةٍ ، نمبر 707/ السنن الكبرى للبيهقي، بَابُ التَّيَمُّم لِكُلِّ فَرِيضَةٍ، غمبر 1054) وجه: (٢)قول الصحابي لثبوت وَيَجُوزُ التَّيَمُّمُ لِلصَّحِيحِ فِي الْمِصْرِ إِذَا حَضَرَتْ جِنَازَةٌ «عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسِ ، قَالَ: «إِذَا خِفْتَ أَنْ تَفُوتَكَ الْجُنَازَةُ، وَأَنْتَ عَلَى غَيْرِ وُضُوءِ، فَتَيَمَّمُ وَصَلِ» (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، فِي الرَّجُلِ يَخَافُ أَنْ تَفُوتَهُ الصَّلَاةُ عَلَى الْجَنَازَةِ وَهُوَ غَيْرُ مُتَوَفِّي، 11467 ، كِتَابُ الْجَنَائِزِ) وجه (۳)قول الصحابي لثبوت وَيَجُوزُ التَّيَمُّمُ لِلصَّحِيحِ فِي الْمِصْرِ إِذَا حَضَرَتْ جِنَازَةٌ عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ، أَنَّهُ قَالَ : " لَا يُصَلِّي عَلَى الْجَنَازَةِ إِلَّا وَهُوَ طَاهِرٌ ( السنن الكبري للبيهقي، بَابُ الصَّحِيح الْمُقِيمِ يَتَوَضَّأُ لِلْمَكْتُوبَةِ وَالجَنَازَةِ وَالْعِيدِ وَلَا يَتَيَمَّم ، نمبر 1093) ۱۲ وجه (۱) قول التابعي لثبوت وَكَذَلِكَ مَنْ حَضَرَ صَلَاةَ الْعِيدِ فَخَشِيَ \ عَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ، قَالَ: يَتَيَمَّمُ لِلْعِيدَيْن وَالْجِنَازَةِ» (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، الرَّجُلُ يُحْدِثُ يَوْمَ الْعِيدِ، مَا يَصْنَعُ، غمبر 5868) اصول : جس عبادت کا خلیفہ یا نائب ہو اس کے لئے تمیم کرنا جائز ہے، جیسے جنازہ اور عیدین کی نماز۔
Chapter of Tayammum. And tayammum is permissible for a healthy person in a city when a funeral is present and the guardian is someone else, and he fears that if he occupies himself with purification he will miss the prayer, then he performs tayammum and prays. And similarly, one who attends the Eid prayer and fears that if he occupies himself with purification he will miss the Eid prayer. Proof: (1) Saying of a Companion for establishment: 'Tayammum is performed for every prayer' (Sunan al-Daraqutni...); (2) Saying of a Companion... from Ibn Abbas: 'If you fear missing the funeral and you are without wudu, perform tayammum and pray' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah); (3) Saying of a Companion... from Ibn Umar: 'One should not pray over the funeral except in a state of purity' (al-Bayhaqi). Proof for Eid: Saying of a Successor... from Ibrahim: 'He performs tayammum for the two Eids and the funeral' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah). Principle: For an act that has a substitute or deputy, performing tayammum for it is permissible, such as the funeral and the two Eid prayers.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi matn of al-Quduri regarding tayammum for specific prayers. The ruling states that a healthy person residing in a city may perform tayammum for the funeral prayer if he fears that performing wudu would cause him to miss the prayer. This applies when the guardian of the deceased is someone else (i.e., the person is not the primary guardian responsible for the funeral). The same ruling applies to the Eid prayer. The author then provides proofs: a narration that tayammum suffices for every prayer, a direct instruction from Ibn Abbas to perform tayammum for fear of missing the funeral, and a statement from Ibn Umar emphasizing the necessity of purity for funeral prayer. For Eid, the proof is from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, who permits tayammum for the two Eids and funerals. The Urdu usul notes that tayammum is permissible for any act that has a deputy or substitute, like funeral and Eid prayers, because they can be performed without full ablution in necessity.

Key Terms
تيمم (tayammum): Dry ablution using pure earth as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or harmful.
جنازة (janazah): Funeral; the body of the deceased or the funeral prayer.
ولي (wali): Guardian of the deceased, typically a close relative responsible for the funeral.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Only during travel

Key Takeaway
Tayammum for funeral and Eid prayers is permissible for a healthy resident when performing wudu would cause missing the prayer.

Tayammum for Friday Prayer and Shortened Time
Ruling that one must do wudu, not tayammum, for Friday and when time is short

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that wudu is obligatory even if it means missing jumu'ah or the prayer time, and explain the proof from Al-Hasan al-Basri.

Core Idea
Wudu is obligatory even at the cost of missing the congregation; tayammum is only for absence of water.

In both situations – fear of missing Friday prayer and fear of time running out – the Hanafi school emphasizes that taharah with water (wudu) must be performed. Tayammum is not a permissible shortcut because the prayer can still be performed later as qada or as zuhr. This lesson presents the ruling and the proof from the tabi'i Al-Hasan al-Basri.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage covers two cases: (1) fear of missing the Friday prayer due to wudu, and (2) fear of the prayer time expiring due to wudu. Recognize that both involve a conflict between purification and catching the prayer.
In both cases, the person has access to water.
2
State the ruling in each case
In both scenarios, the ruling is the same: the person must perform wudu, not tayammum. The text explicitly says 'he does not perform tayammum but performs wudu'.
Tayammum is only permissible when water is absent or harmful.
3
Determine the consequence if the prayer is missed
If he misses Friday, he prays zuhr (four rak'ahs) because the original obligation is zuhr. If he misses the time for an obligatory prayer, he prays it as qada (make-up). The default obligation remains.
Friday is a substitute for zuhr; missing it reverts to zuhr.
4
Analyze the proof from Al-Hasan al-Basri
The proof is the statement of Al-Hasan al-Basri: when a man performed wudu on Friday and missed the imam, he said 'he prays four rak'ahs' (i.e., zuhr). This shows that wudu is prioritized and the obligation of wudu is not sacrificed for congregation.
This is a qawl tabi'i, considered a proof in Hanafi fiqh when not contradicted by stronger evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ خَافَ مَنْ شَهِدَ الْجُمُعَةَ إِذَا اشْتَغَلَ بِالطَّهَارَةِ فَاتَتْهُ فَإِنَّهُ لَا يَتَيَمَّمُ وَلَكِنَّهُ يَتَوَضَّأُ فَإِنْ أَدْرَكَ الْجُمُعَةَ صَلَّاهَا وَالْأَصْلُ الظُّهْرُ أَرْبَعًا وَكَذَلِكَ إِذَا ضَاقَ الْوَقْتُ فَخَافَ إِنْ تَوَضَّأَ فَاتَ الْوَقْتُ لَم يَتَيَمَّمْ وَلَكِنَّهُ يَتَوَضَّأُ وَيُصَلِّيهَا فَائِتَةً وَجْه : (۱) قول التابعي لثبوت وَإِنْ خَافَ مَنْ شَهِدَ الْجُمُعَةَ إِذَا اشْتَغَلَ بِالطَّهَارَةِ فَاتَتْهُ \ سُئِلَ الْحَسَنُ، عَنْ رَجُلٍ أَحْدَثَ يَوْمَ الْجُمُعَةِ، فَذَهَبَ لِيَتَوَضَّأَ فَجَاءَ وَقَدْ صَلَّى الْإِمَامُ، قَالَ: «يُصَلِّي أَرْبَعًا» (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه الرَّجُلُ يُحْدِثُ يَوْمَ الْجُمُعَةِ ، نمبر 5580)
And if one who attends the Friday prayer fears that if he occupies himself with purification it will pass him by, then he does not perform tayammum but performs wudu. If he catches the Friday prayer, he prays it; the origin is zuhr, four rak'ahs. Similarly, when time is short and he fears that if he performs wudu the time will pass, he does not perform tayammum but performs wudu and prays it as a missed prayer. Proof: (1) Saying of a Successor: Al-Hasan was asked about a man who had an event on Friday and went to perform wudu, and came back after the imam had prayed; he said: 'He prays four rak'ahs.'
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling for two situations: fear of missing Friday prayer and fear of time running out for any obligatory prayer. In both cases, the Hanafi position is that one must perform wudu even if it means missing the Friday prayer or the time for the current prayer. For Friday, if he misses it, he prays zuhr (four rak'ahs) as the original obligation. For a prayer whose time is short, he performs wudu and then prays the prayer as qada (make-up). The proof is a narration from al-Hasan al-Basri that if someone misses the Friday prayer due to performing wudu, he prays four rak'ahs (i.e., zuhr). This shows that wudu is prioritized over catching the congregation or time.

Key Terms
جمعة (jumu'ah): Friday congregational prayer, which is a substitute for zuhr.
ضاق الوقت (daqa al-waqt): Time for prayer is short, i.e., only enough for a minimal required acts.
فائتة (fa'itah): Missed prayer performed after its time as qada.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) They must perform wudu even if they miss Friday, and pray zuhr instead
C) They may pray without wudu due to necessity
D) They should skip the prayer altogether

Key Takeaway
Wudu is obligatory even if it means missing the Friday congregation or the prayer time; tayammum is only for when water is absent or harmful.

Forgetting Water Before Tayammum: When Repeat is Not Required
Ruling and intra-Hanafi dispute on repeat of prayer after forgetting water

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the validity of prayer performed with tayammum when water was forgotten, and explain the intra-madhhab dispute with Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Forgetting water in your luggage does not invalidate tayammum – the prayer stands, no repeat required.

This lesson examines a specific scenario from al-Quduri: a traveler forgets water in his luggage, performs tayammum, prays, and later remembers. The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold the prayer valid without repetition, while Abu Yusuf requires repetition. We will analyze the basis of each position and identify the relied-upon ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Read the Arabic text: 'wa l-musafiru idha nasiya l-ma'a fi rahl...' The scenario involves a traveler, forgotten water, tayammum, prayer, then remembrance. Note the key term 'rahl' meaning luggage.
2
Spot the key phrase 'عندَهُمَا'
This indicates the opinion of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Note the ruling: 'لم يعد صلاته' (does not repeat).
Abu Yusuf is the dissenter.
3
Understand the opposing view
Abu Yusuf says 'يعيد' (he repeats). Think about why he might consider the tayammum invalid.
Possible basis: water was present, so tayammum was not justified.
4
Consider the practical consequence
The difference matters for a traveler: does he need to make up the prayer? The mufta bihi (operative fatwa) is no repetition.
This ruling eases burden on the traveler.
5
Link to usul: forgetfulness as excuse
The majority view treats forgetfulness as a valid excuse that makes water effectively absent at the time of prayer.
This involves the usul principle that actions are judged by circumstances.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالْمُسَافِرُ إِذَا نَسِيَ الْمَاءَ فِي رَحْلِهِ فَتَيَمَّمَ وَصَلَّى ثُمَّ ذَكَرَ الْمَاءَ بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ لَمْ يُعِدْ صَلَاتَهُ عِنْدَهُمَا. وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ يُعِيدُ
And the traveler, if he forgets water in his luggage, performs tayammum and prays, then remembers the water after that, he does not repeat his prayer according to the two of them. And Abu Yusuf said: he repeats.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on a specific scenario: a traveler who forgets that he has water in his luggage, performs tayammum, prays, and then after the prayer remembers the water. According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the two, indicated by 'عندَهُمَا'), the prayer is valid and does not need to be repeated. However, Abu Yusuf holds that he must repeat the prayer. The default position in the Hanafi school is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, which is the mufta bihi as per the matn. Abu Yusuf's view is based on the idea that the tayammum was invalid because water was available, even though forgotten, while the majority consider that forgetfulness excuses the lack of search.

Key Terms
رحل (rahl): Luggage or baggage of a traveler, containing his belongings including water.
عندَهُمَا (indahuma): According to the two of them, i.e., Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad, what is the ruling for a traveler who forgets water in his luggage, performs tayammum, prays, and later remembers the water?
A) His prayer is invalid and must be repeated
B) His prayer is valid and need not be repeated
C) He must repeat only if he remembers during the prayer
D) He must perform both wudu and repeat the prayer

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school relies on the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: prayer with tayammum after forgetting water is valid and does not require repetition.

Searching for Water and Asking a Companion Before Tayammum
Rulings on obligation to search for water and ask companion before tayammum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions that trigger the obligation to search for water before tayammum and explain the ruling when a companion has water.

Core Idea
Search is only obligatory when you have a strong assumption that water is near; you must ask your companion first.

Tayammum is a dispensation for when water is unavailable, but it is not a free pass. The Hanafi school sets clear conditions: you must have a genuine belief that water is absent, and if you are traveling with a companion, you must request water from them. This lesson unpacks these rulings from the matn of Al-Quduri and the proofs cited by the commentator, including actions of the Companions and hadiths.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios regarding search for water
Read the first part of the Arabic text: 'وَلَيْسَ عَلَى الْمُتَيَمِّمِ إِذَا لَمْ يَغْلِبْ عَلَى ظَنِهِ أَنَّ بِقُرْبِهِ مَاءً أَنْ يَطْلُبَ الْمَاءَ فَإِنْ غَلَبَ عَلَى ظَنِهِ أَنَّ بِقُرْبِهِ مَاءً لَمْ يَجُزْ تَيَمُّمُهُ حَتَّى يَطْلُبَهُ'. Distinguish between when search is not required and when it is obligatory.
Key term: ghalabat al-zann (prevalent assumption).
2
Understand the ruling on asking a companion
Examine the sentence: 'وَإِنْ كَانَ مَعَ رَفِيقِهِ مَاءً طَلَبَهُ مِنْهُ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَتَيَمَّمَ فَإِنْ مَنَعَهُ منْهُ تَيَمَّمَ'. Note that requesting water is obligatory; if refused, tayammum becomes valid.
3
Analyze the proofs cited
The author provides four proofs: (1) Action of Ibn Umar (tayammum without searching), (2) Hadith of the Prophet entering Madinah without repeating prayer, (3) Statement of 'Aliq about waiting until end of time, (4) Hadith of Aisha about seeking water before tayammum. Understand how each supports the ruling.
These proofs are from Muwatta Malik, Bukhari, Daraqutni, and Bayhaqi.
4
Apply the rule to a scenario
Given a hypothetical traveler in a desert with no strong assumption of nearby water, and a companion who has water, determine the steps before tayammum.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ التَّيَمُّمِ ها وَلَيْسَ عَلَى الْمُتَيَمِّمِ إِذَا لَمْ يَغْلِبْ عَلَى ظَنِهِ أَنَّ بِقُرْبِهِ مَاءً أَنْ يَطْلُبَ الْمَاءَ ١٦ فَإِنْ غَلَبَ عَلَى ظَنِهِ أَنَّ بِقُرْبِهِ مَاءً لَمْ يَجُزْ تَيَمُّمُهُ حَتَّى يَطْلُبَهُ عَل وَإِنْ كَانَ مَعَ رَفِيقِهِ مَاءً طَلَبَهُ مِنْهُ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَتَيَمَّمَ فَإِنْ مَنَعَهُ منْهُ تَيَمَّمَ ۱۵ وجه (۱) عمل الصحابي لثبوت وَلَيْسَ عَلَى الْمُتَيَمِمِ إِذَا لَمْ يَغْلِبْ \ عَنْ نَافِعٍ، أَنَّهُ أَقْبَلَ هُوَ وَعَبْدُ اللهِ بْنُ عُمَرَ (1)، حَتَّى إِذَا كَانَ (2) بِالْمَرْبَدِ، نَزَلَ عَبْدُ اللهِ، فَتَيَمَّمَ صَعِيداً طَيِّباً، فَمَسَحَ بِوَجْهِهِ وَيَدَيْهِ إِلَى الْمِرْفَقَيْنِ، ثُمَّ صَلَّى ) موطأ مالك، الْعَمَلُ فِي التَّيَمُّمِ، برقم 176) وجه : (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَلَيْسَ عَلَى الْمُتَيَمِّمِ إِذَا لَمْ يَغْلِبْ \ ثُمَّ دَخَلَ المَدِينَةَ وَالشَّمْسُ مُرْتَفِعَةٌ فَلَمْ يُعِدْ» (بخاري بَابُ التَّيَمُّم في الحَضَرِ، إِذَا لَمْ يَجِدِ الْمَاءَ، وَخَافَ فَوْتَ الصَّلَاةِ ، نمبر 337) ١٢.وجه: (ا)قول الصحابي لثبوت فَإِنْ غَلَبَ عَلَى ظَنِهِ أَنَّ بِقُرْبِهِ مَاءً لَمْ يَجُزْ تَيَمُّمُهُ \ عَنْ عَلِقٍ قَالَ: «إِذَا أَجْنَبَ الرَّجُلُ فِي السَّفَرِ تَلَوَّمَ مَا بَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَ آخِرِ الْوَقْتِ فَإِنْ لَمْ يَجِدِ الْمَاءَ تَيَمَّمَ وَصَلَّى» (سنن الدار قطني، بَابٌ فِي بَيَانِ الْمَوْضِعِ الَّذِي يَجُوزُ التَّيَمُّمُ فِيهِ،نمبر720/مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، مَنْ قَالَ لَا يُتَيَمَّمُ مَا رَجَا أَنْ يَقْدِرَ عَلَى الْمَاءِ، نمبر 1701) وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَإِنْ كَانَ مَعَ رَفِيقِهِ مَاءً طَلَبَهُ مِنْهُ \ عَنْ عَائِشَةَ، ... ثُمَّ إِنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ اسْتَيْقَظَ وَحَضَرَتِ الصَّلَاةُ فَالْتَمَسَ النَّاسُ الْمَاءَ فَلَمْ يَجِدُوا... (السنن الكبري للبيهقي ، بَابُ إِعْوَازِ الْمَاءِ بَعْدَ طَلَبِهِ، نمبر 1062) اصول : پانی تلاش کرنا واجب نہیں ، بشر طیکہ غالب گمان یا علامت ظاہرہ موجود ہو۔
Chapter of Tayammum. And it is not upon the one performing tayammum, when his assumption is not prevalent that water is near him, to search for water. If his assumption is prevalent that water is near, his tayammum is not permissible until he searches for it. And if a companion has water, he asks him for it before performing tayammum; if he prevents him from it, he performs tayammum. Proof: (1) Action of a Companion: Nafi' reported that he and Ibn Umar came until at al-Marbad, Ibn Umar descended, performed tayammum with pure earth, wiped his face and hands up to the elbows, then prayed (Muwatta Malik). (2) Hadith: Then he entered Madinah while the sun was high and he did not repeat (Bukhari). (3) Saying of a Companion: 'Aliq said: 'When a man becomes junub on a journey, he delays until the end of the time; if he does not find water, he performs tayammum and prays.' (al-Daraqutni, Ibn Abi Shaybah). (4) Hadith: From Aisha... then the Messenger of Allah woke up and the prayer became due, and the people sought water but did not find... (al-Bayhaqi). Principle: Searching for water is not obligatory unless there is a prevalent assumption or apparent sign.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage provides detailed rulings on the obligation to search for water before tayammum. It distinguishes two cases: if a person has no strong assumption that water is nearby, no search is required. If he has a strong assumption (ghalabat al-zann) that water is near, then tayammum is not permissible until he searches for it. Additionally, if a companion has water, one must ask for it before performing tayammum. If the companion refuses, then tayammum becomes permissible. The author supports these rulings with multiple proofs: the action of Ibn Umar (he performed tayammum without searching because he had no assumption of water), a hadith from Bukhari where the Prophet did not repeat a prayer after entering Madinah (indicating no search obligation), a statement from 'Aliq that one should wait until the end of the time if hoping to find water, and the hadith of Aisha where people sought water before tayammum. The Urdu usul concludes that searching for water is not obligatory unless there is a prevalent assumption or apparent sign.

Key Terms
غالب الظن (ghalabat al-zann): Prevalent assumption or strong probability that water is nearby.
رفيق (rafiq): Companion or fellow traveler.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is it permissible to perform tayammum without searching for water, according to this passage?
A) When one is in a city with public water
B) When one has no strong assumption that water is nearby
C) When one is very tired
D) When one has a companion with water

Key Takeaway
Search for water is obligatory only when you have a strong assumption it is nearby; otherwise, it is not required. Additionally, you must ask your companion for water before performing tayammum, but if refused, tayammum becomes valid.

Seeking Water Before Tayammum: Conditioned by Strong Presumption
Ruling with proofs on seeking water before tayammum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on seeking water before tayammum and apply the condition of ghalabat al-zann to determine when tayammum is valid or invalid.

Core Idea
Seeking water before tayammum is not always required; it becomes wajib only when one has a strong presumption that water is nearby.

The Hanafi school balances practicality and legal obligation in matters of purification. This passage from al-Quduri addresses a key question: when must a person actively look for water before turning to tayammum? The answer, which depends on the strength of one's expectation, is supported by multiple proofs from the Sunnah and the practice of the Companions. Understanding this ruling is essential for correctly applying tayammum in travel and other situations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon (seeking water before tayammum) and its legal classification (wajib or not wajib) under different conditions.
The act is 'seeking water' (talab al-ma). Its hukm changes based on ghalabat al-zann.
2
Locate the condition that triggers the obligation
Identify the key condition: strong presumption (ghalabat al-zann) that water is nearby. If absent, no obligation; if present, seeking becomes wajib and tayammum without it is batil.
Ghalabat al-zann means more than 50% certainty based on visible signs or experience.
3
Examine the proofs (adillah) cited
The text provides four evidences: action of Ibn Umar, hadith of entering Madinah, statement of Alqamah, and hadith of Aishah. For each, extract how it supports the conditional obligation.
Focus on the legal implication (wajh al-dalalah) of each evidence.
4
Apply the ruling to a companion scenario
Consider the case where a companion has water: the ruling requires requesting it before tayammum. If refused, tayammum is valid.
This is a specific application of the general principle.
5
Recognize the ikhtilaf and its practical effect
Note that other schools may require seeking water unconditionally. The Hanafi position is mufta bihi and conditioned on strong presumption.
The thamarah al-khilaf: in the absence of strong presumption, Hanafis permit tayammum without seeking; others may invalidate it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ التَّيَمُّمِ وَلَيْسَ عَلَى الْمُتَيَمِّمِ إِذَا لَمْ يَغْلِبْ عَلَى ظَنِهِ أَنَّ بِقُرْبِهِ مَاءً أَنْ يَطْلُبَ الْمَاءَ فَإِنْ غَلَبَ عَلَى ظَنِهِ أَنَّ بِقُرْبِهِ مَاءً لَمْ يَجُزْ تَيَمُّمُهُ حَتَّى يَطْلُبَهُ وَإِنْ كَانَ مَعَ رَفِيقِهِ مَاءً طَلَبَهُ مِنْهُ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَتَيَمَّمَ فَإِنْ مَنَعَهُ مِنْهُ تَيَمَّمَ
وجه (١) عمل الصحابي لثبوت: عَنْ نَافِعٍ، أَنَّهُ أَقْبَلَ هُوَ وَعَبْدُ اللهِ بْنُ عُمَرَ، حَتَّى إِذَا كَانَ بِالْمَرْبَدِ، نَزَلَ عَبْدُ اللهِ، فَتَيَمَّمَ صَعِيداً طَيِّباً، فَمَسَحَ بِوَجْهِهِ وَيَدَيْهِ إِلَى الْمِرْفَقَيْنِ، ثُمَّ صَلَّى (موطأ مالك، العمل في التيمم، رقم 176)
وجه (٢) الحديث لثبوت: ثُمَّ دَخَلَ المَدِينَةَ وَالشَّمْسُ مُرْتَفِعَةٌ فَلَمْ يُعِدْ (بخاري باب التيمم في الحضر، إذا لم يجد الماء، وخاف فوت الصلاة، رقم 337)
وجه (٣) قول الصحابي لثبوت: عَنْ عَلِقٍ قَالَ: إِذَا أَجْنَبَ الرَّجُلُ فِي السَّفَرِ تَلَوَّمَ مَا بَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَ آخِرِ الْوَقْتِ فَإِنْ لَمْ يَجِدِ الْمَاءَ تَيَمَّمَ وَصَلَّى (سنن الدارقطني، باب في بيان الموضع الذي يجوز التيمم فيه، رقم 720؛ مصنف ابن أبي شيبة، من قال لا يتيمم ما رجا أن يقدر على الماء، رقم 1701)
وجه (٤) الحديث لثبوت: عَنْ عَائِشَةَ، ... ثُمَّ إِنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ اسْتَيْقَظَ وَحَضَرَتِ الصَّلَاةُ فَالْتَمَسَ النَّاسُ الْمَاءَ فَلَمْ يَجِدُوا (السنن الكبرى للبيهقي، باب إعواز الماء بعد طلبه، رقم 1062)
أصول: پانی تلاش کرنا واجب نہیں، بشر طیکہ غالب گمان یا علامت ظاہرہ موجود ہو۔
Chapter of Tayammum: It is not required for the one performing tayammum, if he does not have a strong presumption that water is near him, to seek water. If he has a strong presumption that water is near him, his tayammum is not permissible until he seeks it. And if there is water with his companion, he requests it from him before performing tayammum; if he prevents him from it, he performs tayammum.
Evidence (1) from the action of a Companion: From Nafi', that he and 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar came until when they were at al-Marbad, 'Abdullah descended, performed tayammum with pure earth, wiped his face and hands up to the elbows, then prayed. (Muwatta Malik, The Act of Tayammum, no. 176)
Evidence (2) from hadith: Then he entered Madinah while the sun was high and did not repeat (the prayer). (Bukhari, Chapter of Tayammum in Residence, When One Does Not Find Water and Fears Missing the Prayer, no. 337)
Evidence (3) from the statement of a Companion: From 'Alqamah who said: When a man becomes junub on a journey, he waits between himself and the end of the time; if he does not find water, he performs tayammum and prays. (Sunan al-Daraqutni, Chapter on the Place Where Tayammum is Permitted, no. 720; Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, Whoever Says One Should Not Perform Tayammum as Long as He Hopes to Find Water, no. 1701)
Evidence (4) from hadith: From 'Aishah, ... Then the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) woke up and the prayer was due; the people looked for water but did not find it. (Sunan al-Kubra al-Bayhaqi, Chapter on Lack of Water After Seeking, no. 1062)
Principle: Seeking water is not obligatory, unless there is a strong presumption or a visible sign.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage contains the ruling on seeking water before tayammum, followed by its proofs. The matn states: If a person does not have a strong presumption (ghalabat al-zann) that water is nearby, he is not obligated to search for it. However, if he does have such a presumption, then his tayammum is invalid until he actually searches. Additionally, if a traveling companion has water, he must request it; if refused, he may then perform tayammum. The text then provides four evidences: (1) the action of 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar who performed tayammum and did not repeat his prayer after reaching water, (2) the hadith that he entered Madinah and did not repeat, (3) the statement of 'Alqamah advising to wait until the end of the time in hope of finding water, (4) the hadith of 'Aishah about the Prophet's companions seeking water and not finding it. The usul principle (in Urdu) summarizes: seeking water is not wajib (obligatory) unless there is a strong presumption or visible sign. The Hanafi school holds that the obligation to seek water is conditioned upon a reasonable expectation; otherwise, tayammum is valid without seeking.

Key Terms
تيمم (tayammum): Dry ablution with clean earth as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or harmful.
غالب ظن (ghalabat al-zann): Strong presumption (more than 50% certainty) based on signs or experience, not mere doubt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is a person required to seek water before performing tayammum?
A) Always, regardless of circumstances
B) Only if water is visible nearby
C) When he has a strong presumption that water is near
D) Only if a companion has water

Key Takeaway
The obligation to seek water before tayammum is conditional upon a strong presumption (ghalabat al-zann) that water is nearby; without it, tayammum is valid immediately.

Wiping over Khuffs: Ruling, Duration, and Conditions
Ruling on wiping over khuffs with conditions and proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wiping over khuffs, identify its conditions, and apply the correct duration for residents and travelers.

Core Idea
Wiping over khuffs is a valid rukhsah for washing feet in wudu, with conditions and time limits confirmed by Sunnah.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on wiping over khuffs (leather socks) during wudu. The matn of al-Quduri establishes the permissibility of this dispensation and details the key conditions and the duration of validity for residents and travelers. We will work through the proofs from the Sunnah and understand the practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled? Wiping over khuffs (al-mash 'ala al-khuffayn). What is the hukm? Ja'iz (permissible) by Sunnah, not obligatory, but a valid substitute for washing feet.
The matn says 'ja'iz', but the specific hukm level is mubah.
2
Extract the conditions for validity
List the conditions from the passage: (1) wearing khuffs after complete wudu (tahara), (2) khuffs must cover the feet up to ankles, (3) the hadath must be minor (not janabah), (4) khuffs can be leather or thick material that can be walked in.
3
Note the duration for resident vs traveler
Resident: one day and one night (24 hours). Traveler: three days and three nights (72 hours). The duration begins from the first hadath after wearing the khuffs.
The starting point is 'aqib al-hadath' – immediately after the first minor hadath.
4
Analyse the proofs from the Sunnah
The passage cites five hadith evidences: (1) the Prophet's own practice, (2) the wudu verse (used as background), (3) the command to keep khuffs on for three days except janabah, (4) the incident of al-Mughira, (5) the hadith of 'Ali specifying durations.
Each hadith reinforces the permissibility and the time limits.
5
Understand the scope: minor hadath only
Wiping over khuffs is valid only for minor hadath (e.g., urine, stool, wind, sleep). Major hadath (janabah) requires removal of khuffs and full ghusl.
The hadith of Safwan explicitly states 'except from janabah'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ الْمَسْحِ عَلَى الْخُفَّيْنِ الْمَسْحُ عَلَى الْخَفَّيْنِ جَائِزَ بِالسُّنَّةِ مِنْ كُلِّ حَدَثٍ مُوجِبِ لِلْوُضُوءِ إِذَا لَبِسَ الْخَفَّيْنِ عَلَى طَهَارَةِ ثُمَّ أَحْدَثَ فَإِنْ كَانَ مُقِيمًا مَسَحَ يَوْمًا وَلَيْلَةً، وَإِنْ كَانَ مُسَافِرًا مَسَحَ ثَلَاثَةَ أَيَّامٍ وَلَيَالِيَهَا ابْتِدَاؤُهَا عَقِيبَ الْحَدَثِ
وجه (١) الحديث لثبوت: عَنْ سَعِيدِ بْنِ أَبِي وَقَّاصٍ، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ أَنَّهُ مَسَحَ عَلَى الْخَفَّيْنِ (صحيح بخاري باب: المسح على الخفين، الرقم 199)
وجه (٢) الآية لثبوت: {وَامْسَحُوا بِرُهُوسِكُمْ وَأَرْجُلَكُمْ إِلَى الْكَعْبَيْنِ} (سورة المائدة 5 آية 6)
وجه (٣) الحديث لثبوت: عَنْ صَفْوَانَ بْنِ عَمَّالٍ، قَالَ: كَانَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ يَأْمُرُنَا إِذَا كُنَّا سَفَرًا أَنْ لَا نَنْزِعَ خِفَافَنَا ثَلَاثَةَ أَيَّامٍ وَلَيَالِيهِنَّ، إِلَّا مِنْ جَنَابَةٍ، وَلَكِنْ مِنْ غَائِطِ وَبَوْلِ وَنَوْمٍ (سنن الترمذي باب: المسح على الخفين للمسافر والمقيم، الرقم 96)
وجه (٤) الحديث لثبوت: عَنْ عُرْوَةَ بْنِ الْمُغِيرَةِ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ قَالَ: كُنْتُ مَعَ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فِي سَفَرٍ، فَأَهْوَيْتُ لِأَنْزِعَ خُفَّيْهِ فَقَالَ: دَعْهُمَا فَإِنِّي أَدْخَلْتُهُمَا طَاهِرَتَيْنِ. فَمَسَحَ عَلَيْهِمَا (صحيح بخاري باب: إذا أدخل رجليه وهما طاهرتان، الرقم 206)
وجه (٥) الحديث لثبوت: أَتَيْتُ عَائِشَةَ أَسْأَلُهَا عَنِ الْمَسْحِ عَلَى الْخُفَّيْنِ: فَقَالَتْ: عَلَيْكَ بِابْنِ أَبِي طَالِبٍ فَسَلْهُ. فَإِنَّهُ كَانَ يُسَافِرُ مَعَ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَسَأَلْنَاهُ فَقَالَ: جَعَلَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم ثَلَاثَةَ أَيَّامٍ وَلَيَالِيَهُنَّ لِلْمُسَافِرِ. وَيَوْمًا وَلَيْلَةَ لِلْمُقِيمِ (صحيح مسلم باب المسح على الخفين، الرقم 273)
أصول: چمڑے کے موزے پر مسح جائز ہے۔
أصول: مقیم کے لئے ایک دن ورات اور مسافر تین دن ورات تک مسح کی گنجائش ہے۔
Chapter of Wiping over Khuffs: Wiping over khuffs is permissible by the Sunnah for every event that necessitates wudu, when he wore the khuffs in a state of purity, then he performed an event (caused hadath). Then if he is a resident, he wipes for a day and a night; and if he is a traveler, he wipes for three days and their nights; their beginning is after the hadath.
Evidence (1) from hadith: From Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas, that the Prophet (peace be upon him) wiped over khuffs. (Sahih Bukhari, Chapter of Wiping over Khuffs, no. 199)
Evidence (2) from the verse: {And wipe your heads and your feet to the ankles.} (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:6)
Evidence (3) from hadith: From Safwan ibn 'Ammar, he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) used to command us, when we were traveling, not to remove our khuffs for three days and their nights, except from janabah, but from excrement, urine, and sleep. (Sunan al-Tirmidhi, Chapter of Wiping over Khuffs for the Traveler and Resident, no. 96)
Evidence (4) from hadith: From 'Urwa ibn al-Mughira, from his father who said: I was with the Prophet (peace be upon him) on a journey, and I bent down to remove his khuffs, but he said: 'Leave them, for I put them on in a state of purity.' And he wiped over them. (Sahih Bukhari, Chapter: When He Enters His Feet While They are Pure, no. 206)
Evidence (5) from hadith: I came to 'Aishah asking her about wiping over khuffs. She said: 'Go to Ibn Abi Talib and ask him, for he used to travel with the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him).' So we asked him, and he said: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) set three days and their nights for the traveler, and a day and a night for the resident.' (Sahih Muslim, Chapter of Wiping over Khuffs, no. 273)
Principles: Wiping over leather khuffs is permissible. For a resident, wiping for a day and a night is allowed; for a traveler, three days and nights.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on wiping over khuffs (leather socks) during wudu, supported by multiple evidences. The matn states that wiping over khuffs is permissible (ja'iz) by the Sunnah for any minor hadath (event that breaks wudu), provided the khuffs were put on after complete wudu. The duration differs: one day and night for a resident, three days and nights for a traveler, starting from the first hadath after wearing. The proofs include: (1) the Prophet's own practice, (2) the verse of wudu (which Hanafis interpret as allowing wiping over khuffs by the Sunnah, not just the verse alone), (3) the command to keep khuffs on for three days except for janabah, (4) the incident of al-Mughira where the Prophet refused to remove his khuffs and wiped them, (5) the hadith of 'Ali specifying the durations. The Urdu usul notes affirm the permissibility and the time limits. Note that this ruling applies only to minor hadath; major hadath (janabah) requires removal. The khuffs must be leather or thick material that can be walked in, and worn in a state of purity.

Key Terms
خف (khuff): Leather socks or boots that cover the feet up to and including the ankles, worn for walking.
مسح (mash): Wiping the hand lightly over the khuffs, replacing the washing of feet in wudu.
حادث (hadath): An event that breaks wudu (minor hadath such as urination, defecation, sleep, etc.).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how long may a resident wipe over his khuffs from the moment of his first hadath?
A) Three days and nights
B) One day and one night
C) Until he removes them
D) Only for one prayer time

Key Takeaway
Wiping over khuffs is a valid rukhsah for minor hadath with conditions; residents wipe for one day/night, travelers for three, starting from the first hadath.

Wiping Over Khuffs: Method and Required Amount
Ruling with proof on wiping method and fard

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi method of wiping over khuffs, identify the obligatory amount, and cite the proofs from the sunnah and the companion's statement.

Core Idea
Wiping over khuffs is on the top only, in lines with three fingers from toes to shin.

Wiping over khuffs is a concession in wudu. However, its precise method and minimum amount are often misunderstood. This passage from al-Quduri lays down the rule: the wiping is on the top surface, performed in lines with the fingers, and the obligatory part is the width of three fingers. The text also provides two key proofs to anchor this ruling in the sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage is about wiping (mash) over the khuff during wudu. The ruling is that wiping is on the upper part (zahir), not the bottom or sides.
This is a concession replacing the washing of the feet under conditions.
2
Specify the method
Wiping is done in lines (khututan) with the fingers, beginning from the toes and ending at the shin. The movement is linear, not circular.
The Arabic 'khuṭūṭan bi-al-aṣābiʿ' indicates linear strokes.
3
Determine the fard amount
The obligatory (fard) part is the width of three fingers of the hand. This is the minimum coverage for the wiping to be valid.
Less than three fingers does not fulfill the obligation; the wiping would be invalid.
4
Examine the proofs
Two proofs are cited: (1) The statement of Ali that if religion were by opinion, one would wipe the bottom, but the sunnah dictates the top. (2) The hadith of Jabir where the Prophet demonstrated wiping from the tips of the fingers to the base of the shin.
The hadith is from Sunan Ibn Majah (no. 551).
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that wiping any part of the khuff suffices, while the Hanafi school requires the top and a minimum amount. The practical consequence is different rulings on validity.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ الْمَسْحِ عَلَى الْخُفَّيْنِ وَالْمَسْحُ عَلَى ظَاهِرِهِمَا خُطُوطًا بِالْأَصَابِعِ يَبْتَدِئُ مِنْ رُءُوسِ الْأَصَابِعِ إِلَى السَّاقِ وَفَرْضُ ذَلِكَ مِقْدَارُ ثَلَاثِ أَصَابِعَ مِنْ أَصَابِعِ الْيَدِ
وجه : (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَالْمَسْحُ عَلَى ظَاهِرِهِمَا خُطُوطًا بِالْأَصَابِعِ \ عَنْ عَلِيِّ، قَالَ: لَوْ كَانَ الدِّينُ بِالرَّأْيِ لَكَانَ أَسْفَلُ الْخَفِّ أَوْلَى بِالْمَسْحِ مِنْ أَعْلَاهُ (سنن ابوداود بَابُ كَيْفَ الْمَسْحُ الرقم (162)
وجه: (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَالْمَسْحُ عَلَى ظَاهِرِهِمَا خُطُوطًا بِالْأَصَابِعِ عَنْ جَابِرٍ، قَالَ: مَرَّ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ، بِرَجُلٍ يَتَوَضَّأُ، وَيَغْسِلُ خُفَّيْهِ، فَقَالَ بِيَدِهِ، كَأَنَّهُ دَفَعَهُ «إِنَّمَا أُمِرْتَ بِالْمَسْحِ» وَقَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «بِيَدِهِ هَكَذَا مِنْ أَطْرَافِ الْأَصَابِعِ إِلَى أَصْلِ السَّاقِ، وَخَطَّطَ بِالْأَصَابِعِ»(سنن ابن ماجه بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي مَسْحِ أَعْلَى الْخُفِّ وَأَسْفَلِهِ، الرقم 551)
اصول : پاوں کے مسح میں پیر کے اوپری حصہ پر ہاتھ کی تین انگلیاں پیر انگلیوں سے پنڈلی تک کھینچے۔
Chapter of wiping over the two khuffs. Wiping is on their upper part, in lines with the fingers, beginning from the tips of the toes to the shin. The fard of that is the amount of three fingers of the hand. Proof (1): Statement of a Companion to establish wiping on the upper part of them in lines with the fingers: From Ali, he said: If religion were by opinion, the bottom of the khuff would be more deserving of wiping than its top. Proof (2): Hadith to establish wiping on the upper part of them in lines with the fingers: From Jabir, he said: The Messenger of Allah passed by a man performing wudu and washing his khuffs, so he said with his hand as if pushing him: 'You have only been commanded to wipe.' And the Messenger of Allah said with his hand like this: from the tips of the fingers to the base of the shin, and he drew lines with his fingers. Principle: In wiping the feet, the upper part of the foot is drawn with three fingers of the hand from the toes to the shin.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It opens the chapter on wiping over khuffs. The matn states that wiping is performed on the upper surface of the khuff, not the bottom, in linear strokes with the fingers, starting from the toes and ending at the shin. The obligatory (fard) amount is the width of three fingers of the hand. The margin provides two proofs: first, the statement of Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) that if religion were based on personal opinion, one would wipe the bottom, but the sunnah directs otherwise. Second, the hadith of Jabir where the Prophet explicitly instructed a man to wipe, not wash, and demonstrated the method from the tips of the fingers to the base of the shin with lines. The Urdu note summarizes the method: the upper part is wiped with three fingers from toes to shin.

Key Terms
خُفّ (khuff): A leather sock worn on the foot, covering the ankles, used for warmth and protection.
مَسْح (mash): Wiping with a wet hand over a part of the body or khuff as a substitute for washing.
فَرْض (fard): Obligatory; the minimum required portion of the wiping act. Here, three fingers' width.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum obligatory (fard) amount of wiping over a khuff in the Hanafi school?
A) The entire top of the khuff
B) The width of three fingers of the hand
C) The width of three fingers of the foot
D) Any amount that wets the khuff

Key Takeaway
Wiping over khuffs must be on the top surface, in linear strokes, covering at least three fingers' width from toes to shin.

Invalidating Conditions for Wiping over Khuffs
Specifies conditions regarding holes in khuffs and janabah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions that invalidate wiping over khuffs and identify the proof for each.

Core Idea
Wiping over khuffs is invalid if the khuff has a hole exposing three toes or if the person is in janabah.

The concession of wiping over khuffs is subject to specific conditions. This lesson clarifies two key invalidators: a large hole in the khuff and the state of major impurity (janabah). The ruling is rooted in the practice of the Companions and their successors, providing a practical threshold for validity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is wiping over khuffs during wudu. The passage states when it is not permissible (la yajuz). Note the two distinct prohibitions.
The ruling is batil (invalid) if conditions are violated.
2
Locate the first condition: hole size
A 'large hole' is defined as one that exposes an area equivalent to three toes. If smaller, wiping is allowed. This is a fixed measure in the Hanafi school.
The threshold is three toes, not any hole.
3
Locate the second condition: janabah
A person in a state of janabah (requiring ghusl) cannot wipe over khuffs at all. They must perform ghusl and then wash their feet.
This applies even if the khuffs are intact.
4
Examine the proofs
The passage cites two statements from the Tabi'un as evidence. The first implies that removing khuffs after wiping requires washing the feet, indicating the earlier wiping was invalid due to a defect. The second explicitly forbids wiping if any part of the wudu area is exposed.
These are zanni proofs but sufficient for the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يَجُوزُ الْمَسْحُ عَلَى خُفٍّ فِيهِ خَرْقٌ كَبِيرٌ يُبَيِّنُ مِنْهُ مِقْدَارَ ثَلَاثِ أَصَابِعَ مِنْ أَصَابِعِ الرِّجْلِ وَإِنْ كَانَ أَقَلَّ مِنْ ذَلِكَ جَازَ وَلَا يَجُوزُ الْمَسْحُ لِمَنْ وَجَبَ عَلَيْهِ الْغُسْلُ
وجه : (۱) قول التابعي لثبوت وَلَا يَجُوزُ الْمَسْحُ عَلَى خُفٍّ فِيهِ خَرْقٌ كَبِيرٌ \ عَنْ سَعِيدِ بْنِ أَبِي مَرْيَمَ، عَنْ رَجُلٍ مِنْ أَصْحَابِ النَّبِيِّ فِي الرَّجُلِ يَمْسَحُ عَلَى خُفَّيْهِ ثُمَّ يَبْدُو لَهُ فَيَنْزِعُهُمَا قَالَ: يَغْسِلُ قَدَّمَيْهِ "السنن الكبري للبيهقي، بَابُ مَنْ خَلَعَ خُفَّيْهِ بَعْدَمَا مَسَحَ عَلَيْهِمَا، نمبر 1370)
وجه: (۲)قول التابعي لثبوت وَلَا يَجُوزُ الْمَسْحُ عَلَى خُفٍّ فِيهِ خَرْقٌ كَبِيرٌ \ سَأَلْتُ مَعْمَرًا عَنِ الْخَرْقِ يَكُونُ فِي الْخَفِّ فَقَالَ: " إِذَا خَرَجَ مِنْ مَوَاضِع الْوُضُوءِ شَيْءٌ فَلَا تَمْسَحْ عَلَيْهِ وَاخْلَعْ " (السنن الكبري للبيهقي ، بَابُ الْخُفِّ الَّذِي مَسَحَ عَلَيْهِ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم ، نمبر 1347)
It is not permissible to wipe over a khuff that has a large hole from which appears the amount of three fingers of the foot. If it is less than that, it is permissible. It is not permissible to wipe for one upon whom ghusl is obligatory. Proof (1): Statement of a Tabi'i to establish that it is not permissible to wipe over a khuff with a large hole: From Sa'id ibn Abi Maryam, from a man among the companions of the Prophet concerning a man who wipes over his two khuffs then decides to remove them, he said: He washes his feet. Proof (2): Statement of a Tabi'i to establish that it is not permissible to wipe over a khuff with a large hole: I asked Ma'mar about the hole that is in a khuff, so he said: When something (of the foot) appears from the places of wudu, then do not wipe over it, and remove it.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage lists two conditions that invalidate wiping over khuffs. First, the khuff must not have a large hole. A large hole is defined as one through which a part of the foot equivalent to three toes is visible. If the hole is smaller than this, wiping is still valid. Second, a person in a state of major impurity (junub) cannot benefit from the concession of wiping; he must perform ghusl and then wash his feet. The margin provides two statements from the Tabi'un (Successors) as proof for the hole ruling: Sa'id ibn Abi Maryam relates that if a man removes his khuffs after wiping, he must wash his feet, implying the wiping was invalid if the khuff was defective. Ma'mar explicitly states that if any part of the wudu area is exposed through a hole, wiping is not permissible.

Key Terms
خَرْق (kharq): A hole or tear in the khuff that exposes the foot.
غُسْل (ghusl): Ritual bath required after major impurity (janabah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum size of a hole in a khuff that prevents valid wiping according to this passage?
A) Any hole larger than a fingertip
B) A hole that exposes three toes
C) A hole that exposes the entire foot
D) A hole that allows water to enter

Key Takeaway
Wiping over khuffs is invalid if the khuff has a hole exposing three toes or if the person is in a state of janabah.

Nullifiers of Wiping over Khuffs
Lists what nullifies the wiping status over khuffs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two categories of nullifiers of wiping over khuffs and identify which actions fall under each.

Core Idea
Wiping over khuffs is nullified by any wudu-breaker or by removing the khuffs.

We have learned that a person in a state of wudu may wipe over khuffs for a limited duration. But what ends this concession? The classical Hanafi text lists two distinct categories of nullifiers. Understanding these ensures one knows when the concession ceases and normal foot washing resumes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of nullifiers
Read the passage and note that it mentions two distinct things: (1) everything that nullifies wudu, and (2) removal (naz') of the khuff.
2
Examine the textual proof for the removal nullifier
The author cites a hadith from al-Mughira ibn Shu'ba where the Prophet (peace be upon him) permitted wiping 'as long as he does not remove them.' This proviso directly links the continuance of the concession to the khuffs remaining on the feet.
The hadith is from Sunan al-Kubra lil-Bayhaqi, no. 1376.
3
Understand the scope of 'removal'
In the Hanafi school, removing even one khuff nullifies the wiping on both feet, as the khuffs are considered a pair for the concession.
Some other schools may hold differently.
4
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Consider: a traveler wipes over khuffs, then passes wind (a wudu-breaker). What happens? The wiping is nullified, so for the next wudu, he must wash his feet. Similarly, if he removes a khuff, the wiping is nullified.
After nullification, the concession is gone for that wudu; the duration (1 day/3 days) is for consecutive wipes, not for recovering from nullification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَنْقُضُ الْمَسْحَ كُلُّ شَيْءٍ يَنْقُضُ الْوُضُوءَ وَيَنْقُضُهُ أَيْضًا نَزْعُ الْخُفِّ
وجه: (ا) الحديث لثبوت وَيَنْقُضُ الْمَسْحَ كُلُّ شَيْءٍ يَنْقُضُ الْوُضُوءَ \ عَنِ الْمُغِيرَةَ بْنِ شُعْبَةَ، قَالَ : " غَزَوْنَا مَعَ رَسُولِ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَأَمَرَنَا بِالْمَسْحُ عَلَى الْخُفَّيْنِ ثَلَاثَةَ أَيَّامٍ وَلَيَالِيَهَا لِلْمُسَافِرٍ وَيَوْمًا وَلَيْلَةً لِلْمُقِيمِ مَا لَمْ يَخْلَعْ " (السنن الكبري للبيهقي، بَابُ مَنْ خَلَعَ خُفَّيْهِ بَعْدَمَا مَسَحَ عَلَيْهِمَا، نمبر1376 /مصنف ابن شيبه ، فِي الرَّجُلِ يَمْسَحُ عَلَى خُفَّيْهِ ثُمَّ يَخْلَعُهَا برقم 1960)
And everything that nullifies wudu nullifies the wiping, and its removal (taking off the khuff) also nullifies it. Proof: Hadith to establish that everything that nullifies wudu nullifies the wiping: From al-Mughira bin Shu'ba, he said: We went on a campaign with the Messenger of Allah, and he ordered us to wipe over the khuffs for three days and nights for the traveler and one day and night for the resident, as long as he does not remove them.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage specifies the nullifiers (nawaqid) of the wiping concession. There are two types: first, anything that breaks wudu (e.g., passing wind, urination, sleep) also breaks the state of wiping. Second, physically removing the khuffs (even without a nullifier) nullifies the wiping because the khuffs are no longer present to wipe over. The hadith of al-Mughira supports the second point: the Prophet permitted wiping for a specified period 'as long as he does not remove them,' indicating that removal ends the concession. Once the khuff is removed, one must wash the feet for the next wudu.

Key Terms
نَزْع (naz'): Removal of the khuff from the foot.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following nullifies the wiping over khuffs?
A) Only passing wind
B) Only removing the khuffs
C) Both any wudu-nullifier and removal of the khuffs
D) None of the above

Key Takeaway
Wiping over khuffs is nullified by any act that breaks wudu or by physically removing the khuffs.

Expiration of the Wiping Period
Ruling on expiration of wiping period for khuffs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when the wiping period expires and distinguish between what must be repeated and what remains valid.

Core Idea
When the wiping period expires, only the feet need washing; the rest of wudu remains valid.

In previous lessons, we learned the rules of wiping over khuffs, including the allowed duration. Now we address what happens when that time ends. This passage clarifies that the concession ends, but the wudu is not entirely broken—only the feet require rewashing.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the expiration of the wiping period. The ruling is that the person must remove the khuffs and wash the feet. This is wajib.
The rest of the wudu remains valid; no need to repeat washing face, arms, or wiping head.
2
Locate the dalil
The dalil is a statement from a Tabi'i (a successor of the Companions) recorded by al-Bayhaqi.
The hadith is a qawl sahabi (or tabi'i) and is zanni al-thubut.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Tabi'i instructs to wash the feet only after removing the khuffs. This implies that the rest of the wudu is still valid and does not need to be repeated.
If the entire wudu were invalid, he would have commanded a full wudu, not just washing the feet.
4
Note the cross-madhhab consideration
Some schools hold that the entire wudu becomes invalid when the period expires, requiring a fresh wudu. The Hanafi school relies on this Tabi'i proof to limit the requirement to washing the feet only.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; both positions are based on different proofs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمُضِيُّ الْمُدَّةِ فَإِذَا تَمَّتْ الْمُدَّةُ نَزَعَ خُفَّيْهِ وَغَسَلَ رِجْلَيْهِ وَصَلَّى وَلَيْسَ عَلَيْهِ إِعَادَةُ بَقِيَّةِ الْوُضُوءِ
وجه : (۱) قول التابعي لثبوت وَمُضِيُّ الْمُدَّةِ فَإِذَا تَمَّتْ الْمُدَّةُ نَزَعَ خُفَّيْهِ \ فَيَنْزِعُهُمَا قَالَ: يَغْسِلُ قَدَّمَيْهِ "السنن الكبري للبيهقي، بَابُ مَنْ خَلَعَ خُفَّيْهِ بَعْدَمَا مَسَحَ عَلَيْهِمَا، نمبر 1370)
And the passing of the period. So when the period has ended, he removes his two khuffs and washes his two feet and prays, and he is not required to repeat the rest of the wudu. Proof (1): Statement of a Tabi'i to establish the passing of the period: So he removes them, he said: He washes his feet.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage deals with what happens when the permitted wiping period (one day and night for a resident, three days and nights for a traveler) expires. Once the time is up, the concession ends. The person must remove the khuffs and wash his feet like normal. However, the rest of the wudu (face, arms, head) remains valid; he does not need to repeat it. The proof is a statement from a Tabi'i narrating that if the period ends, one should wash the feet.

Key Terms
مُدَّة (mudda): The prescribed time limit for wiping over khuffs: one day and night for a resident, three days and nights for a traveler.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When the wiping period for a resident ends, what must he do?
A) Remove the khuffs and perform a complete new wudu
B) Remove the khuffs and wash only the feet
C) Keep the khuffs on and repeat the wiping
D) Remove the khuffs and wash the entire body

Key Takeaway
Upon expiry of the wiping period, only the feet require washing; the rest of the wudu remains valid.

Change of Status during Wiping Period
Ruling on change of wiping period due to status change

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two adjustments to the wiping period when a resident becomes a traveler or vice versa, and apply the principle of period change.

Core Idea
Wiping period adjusts to the new status before the initial period expires.

When wiping over khuffs, the maximum period depends on whether you are a resident or a traveler. But what happens if your status changes mid-period? The Hanafi school provides a clear rule: the period can stretch or shrink accordingly. In this lesson, you will learn the two specific scenarios and the underlying principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify initial status and period
Determine whether the person begins wiping as a muqim (1 day) or musafir (3 days).
2
Apply change rule
If status changes before the original period ends, the total permissible period becomes that of the new status (with a minimum for traveler-to-resident). Change must occur before the hadath permeates.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ ابْتَدَأَ الْمَسْحَ وَهُوَ مُقِيمٌ فَسَافَرَ قَبْلَ تَمَامِ يَوْمٍ وَلَيْلَةٍ مَسَحَ تَمَامَ ثَلَاثَةِ أَيَّامٍ وَلَيَالِيهَا وَمَنْ ابْتَدَأَ الْمَسْحَ وَهُوَ مُسَافِرٌ ثُمَّ أَقَامَ وَإِنْ كَانَ مَسَحَ أَقَلَّ مِنْ يَوْمٍ وَلَيْلَةٍ أَتَمَّ مَسْحَ يَوْمٍ وَلَيْلَةٍ
اصول : حدث قدم پر سرایت کرنے سے پہلے مدت کا حکم بدل سکتا ہے، سرایت کے بعد نہیں بدلے گا۔
And whoever begins wiping while he is a resident and then travels before completing one day and one night, he wipes for the full three days and their nights. And whoever begins wiping while a traveler and then becomes a resident, even if he has wiped less than one day and night, he completes the wiping of one day and night. Principle: The ruling of the period can change before the hadath permeates (i.e., before the period is fully utilized), after permeation it does not change.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage addresses a change in status during the wiping period. Two scenarios: 1) A resident starts wiping (with a 24-hour limit) and then travels before that first day-night completes. Since his status changes, he may now benefit from the traveler's three-day concession. He completes the remainder of the three-day period. 2) A traveler starts wiping (with a 3-day limit) and then settles down (becomes resident) before completing at least one day-night. Since he is now a resident, his wiping period is capped at one day-night. He completes that period. The Urdu principle explains that the ruling can be altered before the initial period has fully run its course; after it has run, no change.

Key Terms
مُقِيم (muqim): A person who is residing in one place, not traveling. The wiping period for him is one day and night.
مُسَافِر (musafir): A traveler who is permitted to shorten prayers. His wiping period is three days and nights.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a resident begins wiping and travels after only 6 hours, what is his total permissible wiping period?
A) He continues the original 24-hour period
B) He now has three days total from the start
C) He must remove the khuffs immediately
D) He has three days from the time of travel

Key Takeaway
Wiping period adjusts to match the new residence status if the change occurs before the original period expires.
