One Wudu per Prayer Time for Chronic Excuses
Ruling on wudu validity for those with chronic excuses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a mustahadah and similar individuals may pray multiple prayers with one wudu within a single prayer time, and explain the hadith proof and the cross-madhhab difference.

Core Idea
One wudu per prayer time suffices for those with continuous excuses; the wudu is void when the time exits.

This lesson addresses a specific dispensation in wudu for individuals with chronic conditions like istihadah, urinary incontinence, or persistent nosebleeds. The Hanafi school, based on a hadith of the Prophet ﷺ, rules that such individuals need only perform wudu once at the beginning of each prayer time, and that wudu remains valid for any number of prayers within that time. This principle balances the obligation of purity with the difficulty of repeated wudu.

Guided Path
1
Identify the individuals covered
List the three categories: mustahadah (non-menstrual bleeding), sals al-bawl (urinary incontinence), and ru'af da'im (persistent nosebleed). Note their common trait: continuous impurity that constitutes a valid excuse (udhr).
The excuse must be continuous, not intermittent.
2
State the ruling on wudu validity
The matn says: they pray with that wudu as much as they wish of obligatory and voluntary prayers within the same time period. When the time exits, the wudu becomes void and they must renew it for the next time.
This is a special dispensation; normal wudu nullifiers still apply (e.g., breaking wind).
3
Locate the dalil
The hadith of the mustahadah: 'She leaves prayer during her menses, then bathes and performs wudu for every prayer, and fasts and prays.' (Tirmidhi, Ibn Majah). Identify the key phrase: 'tatwadda'u 'inda kulli salatin' (performs wudu at every prayer).
The hadith does not command wudu for each individual rak'ah, but at each prayer time.
4
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
Hanafi usul interprets 'inda kulli salatin' as 'at the time of each prayer' (i.e., once per prayer time), not 'before each prayer occurrence'. Thus one wudu suffices for all prayers within that time period.
Shafi'is interpret the phrase as requiring a fresh wudu for each obligatory prayer.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school holds that a mustahadah must perform wudu for each obligatory prayer separately. The practical consequence: Hanafi allows multiple prayers with one wudu, Shafi'i requires multiple wudu.
Both schools agree on the necessity of wudu; the ikhtilaf is on its duration.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ وَالْمُسْتَحَاضَةُ وَمَنْ بِهِ سَلَسُ الْبَوْلِ وَالرُّعَافُ الدَّائِمُ إِلَى آخِرِهِ فَيُصَلُّونَ بِذَلِكَ الْوُضُوءِ مَا شَاءُوا مِنْ الْفَرَائِضِ وَالنَّوَافِلِ فَإِذَا خَرَجَ الْوَقْتُ بَطَلَ وُضُوءُهُمْ وَكَانَ عَلَيْهِمْ اسْتِنَافُ الْوُضُوءِ لِصَلَاةٍ أُخْرَى.
وجه الحديث لثبوت وَالْمُسْتَحَاضَةُ وَمَنْ بِهِ سَلَسُ الْبَوْلِ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ أَنَّهُ قَالَ فِي المُسْتَحَاضَةِ: «تَدَعُ الصَّلَاةَ أَيَّامَ أَقْرَائِهَا الَّتِي كَانَتْ تَحِيضُ فِيهَا، ثُمَّ تَغْتَسِلُ وَتَتَوَضَّأُ عِنْدَ كُلِّ صَلَاةٍ، وَتَصُومُ وَتُصَلّي» سنن الترمذي بَابُ مَا جَاءَ أَنَّ الْمُسْتَحَاضَةَ تَتَوَضَّأُ لِكُلِّ صَلَاةٍ، نمبر 126 سنن ابن ماجه، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي الْمُسْتَحَاضَةِ الَّتِي قَدْ عَدَّتْ أَيَّامَ أَقْرَائِهَا، قَبْلَ أَنْ يَسْتَمِرَّ بِهَا الدَّمُ، نمبر 624
اصول : استحاضہ کا خون نکسیر کے خون کی طرح ہے یعنی مستقل خون آئے پھر بھی نماز کا حکم ہے، البتہ ہر نماز کے وقت وضو کرلے اور اس ایک وضو سے جتنی چاہے نماز پڑھے، اور وقت ختم ہوتے ہی وضو باطل ہو گا۔ اصول : مستحاضہ عورت بہر حال نماز پڑھے گی اور روزے رکھے گی، اور وطی بھی جائز ہے، حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے قول کی وجہ سے کہ وضو کرو اور نماز پڑھو اگر چہ خون چٹائی پر ٹپکتار ہے۔
Chapter: The mustahadah, the one with continuous incontinence of urine, and the one with continuous nosebleed – they pray with that wudu as much as they wish of obligatory and voluntary prayers. When the time period exits, their wudu becomes void, and they must renew wudu for another prayer. Face of hadith for establishing: The mustahadah and the one with continuous incontinence – from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that he said concerning the mustahadah: “She leaves prayer during the days of her menses that she used to menstruate, then she bathes and performs wudu for every prayer, and fasts and prays.” (Sunan al-Tirmidhi, chapter on mustahadah performing wudu for every prayer, no. 126; Sunan Ibn Majah, chapter on mustahadah who has counted her days before the blood became continuous, no. 624) Principle: The blood of istihadah is like the blood of a nosebleed, meaning continuous blood flows yet prayer is obligatory. However, she performs wudu at each prayer time, and with that one wudu she prays as much as she wishes, and when the time ends, the wudu becomes void. Principle: The mustahadah woman must pray and fast under all circumstances, and intercourse is also permissible, due to the statement of the Prophet (peace be upon him): “Perform wudu and pray even if blood drips on the mat.”
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the matn of al-Quduri regarding individuals who suffer from chronic conditions causing continuous impurity: the mustahadah (woman with non-menstrual bleeding), the one with urinary incontinence (sals al-bawl), and the one with persistent nosebleed (ru'af da'im). The ruling is that these individuals can perform wudu once and then pray any number of obligatory and supererogatory prayers with that wudu throughout the entire prayer time (waqt). Once the time expires (e.g., Zuhr time ends and Asr begins), that wudu is nullified and they must perform a new wudu for the next time period. The proof is provided from the hadith of the mustahadah: she is commanded to perform wudu for every prayer, implying that one wudu suffices for all prayers within that time. The Urdu commentary adds that istihadah blood is like a nosebleed – it does not prevent prayer. The mustahadah must still pray and fast, and marital relations are permitted. The key principle is that the excuse is continuous, so the ruling accommodates it by allowing the wudu to remain valid for the entire time.

Key Terms
مستحاضة (mustahadah): A woman who experiences non-menstrual vaginal bleeding (istihadah) for an extended period beyond her normal menses.
سلَس البول (sals al-bawl): A medical condition of continuous urine leakage, considered a valid excuse (udhr) permitting leniency in wudu rulings.
رعاف دائم (ru'af da'im): Persistent nosebleed, treated as a continuous excuse allowing relaxation of wudu rules.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on the wudu of a mustahadah within one prayer time?
A) She must perform wudu for every single rak'ah.
B) Her wudu remains valid for the entire prayer time and she can pray multiple prayers with it.
C) She cannot pray unless she is completely clean.
D) She must perform ghusl before each prayer.

Key Takeaway
For those with continuous excuses, one wudu per prayer time suffices for all prayers within that time, but it becomes void when the time exits.

Nifas (Postnatal Bleeding): Definition, Duration, and Rulings
Defines nifas, its limits, and rulings for excess and twins.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of nifas, identify its maximum duration, and apply the ruling when bleeding exceeds forty days.

Core Idea
Nifas has no minimum but a maximum of 40 days; beyond that, the woman becomes mustahadah.

Nifas is a natural state after childbirth that exempts a woman from prayer and fasting. Understanding its precise definition and duration is essential for determining when a woman must resume her religious obligations. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi position on nifas, including the minimum and maximum limits, the rules for women with and without a previous habit, and an intra-Hanafi dispute about twins.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition
Locate the text's definition: nifas is the blood that emerges after childbirth. Note that blood seen before the majority of the child emerges is istihadah, not nifas.
The definition is central to distinguishing nifas from other bleeding.
2
Determine the limits
Identify that the minimum has no limit (could be a day or less) and the maximum is forty days. This is established by hadith.
Other schools may differ on the minimum; Hanafi takes the 'no limit' position.
3
Apply the rule for exceeding the maximum
If bleeding exceeds forty days, check if the woman has a previous nifas habit ('adah). If she does, her nifas is the habit duration; if not, her nifas is forty days. Beyond that, she is mustahadah.
The habitual duration is based on her own prior births.
4
Analyze the twin dispute
The text presents an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say nifas begins after the first child; Muhammad and Zufar say after the second child. Note the practical consequence for prayer and fasting.
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.
5
Connect to practical rulings
During nifas, a woman does not pray or fast, and she does not make up missed prayers. After nifas ends, she must perform ghusl and resume obligations.
This is a concession (rukhsah), not a punishment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ النِّفَاسِ
ل وَالنِّفَاسُ هُوَ الدَّمُ الْخَارِجُ عَقِيبَ الْوِلَادَةِ وَالدَّمُ الَّذِي تَرَاهُ الْحَامِلُ أَوْ مَا تَرَاهُ الْمَرْأَةُ فِي حَالِ وِلَادَتِهَا قَبْلَ خُرُوجِ أَكْثَرِ الْوَلَدِ اسْتِحَاضَةٌ وَمَا تَرَاهُ فِي حَالِ وِلَادَتِهَا قَبْلَ خُرُوجِ الْوَلَدِ.
وَأَقَلُّ النِّفَاسِ لَا حَدَّ لَهُ وَأَكْثَرُهُ أَرْبَعُونَ يَوْمًا
وَإِذَا جَاوَزَ الدَّمُ الْأَرْبَعِينَ، وَقَدْ كَانَتْ هَذِهِ الْمَرْأَةُ وَلَدَتْ قَبْلَ ذَلِكَ وَلَهَا عَادَةٌ مَعْرُوفَةٌ فِي النِّفَاسِ رُدَّتْ إِلَى أَيَّامِ عَادَتِهَا وَإِنْ لَمْ تَكُنْ لَهَا عَادَةٌ فَابْتِدَاءُ نِفَاسِهَا أَرْبَعُونَ يَوْمًا وَمَنْ وَلَدَتْ وَلَدَيْنِ فِي بَطْنٍ وَاحِدٍ فَنِفَاسُهَا مَا خَرَجَ مِنْ الدَّمِ عَقِيبَ الْوَلَدِ الْأَوَّلِ. وَعَنْ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَأَبِي يُوسُفَ وَقَالَ مُحَمَّدٌ وَزُفَرُ نِفَاسُهَا مَا خَرَجَ مِنْ الدَّمِ عَقِيبَ الْوَلَدِ الثَّانِي
وجه : (١) الحديث لثبوت أَقَلُّ النِّفَاسِ لَا حَدَّ لَهُ وَأَكْثَرُهُ أَرْبَعُونَ يَوْمًا عَنْ أُمِّ سَلَمَةَ، قَالَتْ: «كَانَتْ النُّفَسَاءُ تَجْلِسُ عَلَى عَهْدِ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ أَرْبَعِينَ يَوْمًا» (سنن الترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي كَمْ تَمْكُثُ النُّفَسَاءُ، نمبر 139)
وجه : (٢) الحديث لثبوت أَقَلُّ النّفَاسِ لَا حَدَّ لَهُ وَأَكْثَرُهُ أَرْبَعُونَ يَوْمًا إِلَا يَأْمُرُهَا النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ بِقَضَاءِ صَلَاةِ النِّفَاسِ (سنن ابي داؤد، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي وَقْتِ النُّفَسَاءِ، نمبر 312)
وجه : (۳) الحديث لثبوت وَيَجُوزُ الْمَسْحُ عَلَى الْخَبَائِرِ عَنْ أَنَسٍ, قَالَ: قَالَ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «وَقْتُ النِّفَاسِ أَرْبَعُونَ يَوْمًا إِلَّا أَنْ تَرَى الظُّهْرَ قَبْلَ ذَلِكَ» (سنن الدار قطني كِتَابُ الخَيْضِ، 852/سنن الترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي كَمْ تَمكُثُ النُّفَسَاءُ، نمبر 139)
وجه : (٤) الحديث لثبوت أَقَلُ النِّفَاسِ لَا حَدَّ لَهُ وَأَكْثَرُهُ أَرْبَعُونَ يَوْمًا أَعَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ آلِ عَمْرٍو قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «تَنْتَظِرُ النُّفَسَاءُ أَرْبَعِينَ لَيْلَةً فَإِنْ رَأَتِ الظُّهْرَ قَبْلَ ذلِكَ فَهِيَ طَاهِرٌ, وَإِنْ جَاوَزَتِ الْأَرْبَعِينَ فَهِيَ بِمَنْزِلَةِ الْمُسْتَحَاضَةِ تَغْتَسِلُ وَتُصَلِّي فَإِنْ غَلَبَهَا الدَّمُ تَوَضَّأَتْ لِكُلِّ صَلَاةٍ» (سنن الدار قطني، كِتَابُ الخَيْضِ، نمبر 858)
اصول : نفاس اس خون کو کہتے ہیں جو بچہ پیدا ہونے کے بعد نکلا ہو۔ اصول : نفاس کی کم سے کم کی کوئی مدت نہیں ہے البتہ زیادہ سے زیادہ کی مدت چالیس یوم ہے۔
Chapter of Nifas. And nifas is the blood that comes out after childbirth. And the blood that the pregnant woman sees, or what the woman sees during her childbirth before the majority of the child emerges, is istihadah. And what she sees during her childbirth before the child emerges [is not nifas]. The minimum of nifas has no limit, and its maximum is forty days. When the blood exceeds forty, and this woman had given birth before and has a known habit in nifas, she is referred back to the days of her habit. If she has no habit, then the beginning of her nifas is forty days. And the one who gives birth to two children in one womb: her nifas is the blood that emerges after the first child. And from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf – and Muhammad and Zufar said: her nifas is the blood that emerges after the second child. Face (1) of hadith for establishing that the minimum of nifas has no limit and its maximum is forty days: from Umm Salamah, she said: “The woman in nifas used to sit (abstain from prayer) for forty days during the time of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him).” (Sunan al-Tirmidhi, no. 139) Face (2): the hadith for establishing that the minimum of nifas has no limit and its maximum is forty days: the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not command her to make up the prayer of nifas. (Sunan Abi Dawud, no. 312) Face (3): the hadith for establishing that wiping over the khuffs is permissible? Actually: 'the time of nifas is forty days unless she sees purity before that.' (Sunan al-Daraqutni, Kitab al-Hayd, 852; Sunan al-Tirmidhi, no. 139) Face (4): the hadith for establishing that the minimum of nifas has no limit and its maximum is forty days: from Abdullah ibn Amr, he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: “The woman in nifas waits forty nights. If she sees purity before that, she is pure. If she exceeds forty, she is like the mustahadah: she bathes and prays. And if the blood overpowers her, she performs wudu for every prayer.” (Sunan al-Daraqutni, Kitab al-Hayd, no. 858) Principle: Nifas is the blood that comes out after the birth of the child. Principle: There is no minimum duration for nifas, but the maximum duration is forty days.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage defines nifas (postnatal bleeding) and its legal rulings. Nifas is specifically the blood discharged after the birth of the child. Blood seen during pregnancy or before the majority of the child has emerged is considered istihadah (irregular bleeding) and not nifas. The Hanafi position stated here is that nifas has no minimum duration – it could be just a day or even less – but the maximum is forty days. If bleeding continues beyond forty days, the woman is treated according to her habitual duration if she has a previous nifas habit; otherwise, the maximum of forty days is considered her nifas, and beyond that she becomes mustahadah. An interesting intra-Hanafi dispute is mentioned regarding a woman who gives birth to twins: according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, the nifas period begins from the first child, so all bleeding after the first birth is nifas. Muhammad al-Shaybani and Zufar hold that nifas begins only after the second child, meaning bleeding between the deliveries is considered istihadah. The difference affects whether she must make up prayers during that interval. The hadith proofs establish the forty-day maximum and the concept that nifas does not require making up missed prayers. The Urdu summary reiterates the definition and the absence of a minimum. Students should note that the 'face' (wajh) references are citations from hadith collections supporting the ruling.

Key Terms
النفاس (al-nifas): Postnatal bleeding that occurs after the birth of a child, with a maximum duration of forty days.
استحاضة (istihadah): Irregular vaginal bleeding that is not part of the menstrual cycle or nifas, which does not prevent prayer or fasting.
عادة ('adah): The habitual duration of a woman's nifas from previous births, used as a reference if bleeding exceeds forty days.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling for a woman with no previous nifas habit whose bleeding exceeds forty days?
A) She must wait until bleeding stops completely.
B) Her nifas is considered forty days, and beyond that she is mustahadah.
C) She must perform ghusl and make up all missed prayers.
D) She automatically becomes mustahadah from the start of bleeding.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defines nifas as blood after childbirth with a maximum of 40 days; if bleeding exceeds 40, the woman reverts to her habit or assumes 40 days, beyond which she is mustahadah.

Obligation of Removing Impurity and Purification Methods
States the obligation and proofs for removing impurity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the obligation of removing impurity (tathir), identify the three loci of purification, and explain the Quranic and hadith proofs for this ruling.

Core Idea
Purification from physical impurity is wajib on body, clothes, and place before prayer, and can be done with any pure liquid that removes it.

This lesson opens the chapter on impurities (al-anjas) with a foundational ruling: that removing physical impurity (najasah) from the body, clothes, and place of prayer is an obligation (wajib). The text then provides evidence from the Quran and multiple hadith, establishing both the obligation and the means of purification. Understanding this ruling is essential because its fulfillment is a condition for the validity of salah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its three loci
The matn states that tathir is wajib from the body, clothes, and place. Note that this is a condition for prayer.
2
Extract the means of purification
The text says water and any pure liquid that can remove the impurity. This is a distinctive Hanafi position.
3
Analyze the primary proof
Surah al-Muddaththir 74:4: 'And purify your garments.' The imperative indicates obligation (wujub) in Hanafi usul.
4
Examine the hadith proofs
The hadith of Anas (istinja with water), Asma (menstrual blood), and the prohibition of praying in impure places all support the obligation.
5
Consider the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school restricts purification to water for tangible impurities, while Hanafis allow any pure liquid. Note the practical difference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ الْأَنْجَاسِ
تَطْهِيرُ النَّجَاسَةِ وَاجِبٌ مِنْ بَدَنِ الْمُصَلِّي وَثَوْبِهِ وَالْمَكَانِ الَّذِي يُصَلِّي عَلَيْهِ. وَيَجُوزُ تَطْهِيرُ النَّجَاسَةِ بِالْمَاءِ وَبِكُلِّ مَائِعٍ طَاهِرٍ يُمْكِنُ إِزَالَتُهَا بِهِ وَالْمَاءُ الْمُسْتَعْمَلُ. 
وجه: (ا) الأية لثبوت تَطْهِيرُ النَّجَاسَةِ وَاجِبٌ مِنْ بَدَنِ الْمُصَلِّي: {وَثِيَابَكَ فَطَهِّرْ} (سورة المدثر 74، آية 4)
وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت تَطْهِيرُ النَّجَاسَةِ وَاجِبٌ مِنْ بَدَنِ الْمُصَلِّي: سَمِعْتُ أَنَسَ بْنَ مَالِكٍ، يَقُولُ كَانَ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ إِذَا خَرَجَ لِحَاجَتِهِ، أَجِيءُ أَنَا وَغُلَامٌ، مَعَنَا إِدَاوَةٌ مِنْ مَاءٍ، يَعْنِي يَسْتَنْجِي بِهِ» (بخاري شريف، بَابُ الِاسْتِنْجَاءِ بِالْمَاءِ، نمبر 150)
وجه: (٣) الحديث لثبوت تَطْهِيرُ النَّجَاسَةِ وَاجِبٌ مِنْ بَدَنِ الْمُصَلِّي: عَنْ أَسْمَاءَ ابْنَةِ أَبِي بَكْرٍ، أَنَّ امْرَأَةً سَأَلَتِ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ عَنِ الثَّوْبِ يُصِيبُهُ الدَّمُ مِنَ الحَيْضَةِ؟ فَقَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «حُتِيهِ، ثُمَّ اقْرُصِيهِ بِالمَاءِ، ثُمَّ رُشِّيهِ، وَصَلِّي فِيهِ» (سنن الترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي غَسْلِ دَمِ الحَيْضِ مِنَ الثَّوْبِ، نمبر 138)
وجه: (۴) الحديث لثبوت تَطْهِيرُ النَّجَاسَةِ وَاجِبٌ مِنْ بَدَنِ الْمُصَلِّي: عَنْ ابْنِ عُمَرَ، " أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ نَهَى أَنْ يُصَلَّى فِي سَبْعَةِ مَوَاطِنَ: فِي المَرْبَلَةِ، وَالْمَجْزَرَةِ، وَالْمَقْبَرَةِ، وَقَارِعَةِ الطَّرِيقِ، وَفِي الحَمَّامِ، وَفِي مَعَاطِنِ الإِبِلِ، وَفَوْقَ ظَهْرِ بَيْتِ اللَّهِ "، (سنن الترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي كَرَاهِيَةِ مَا يُصَلَّى إِلَيْهِ وَفِيهِ، نمبر (346))
وجه: (ا) الحديث لثبوت وَيَجُوزُ تَطْهِيرُ النَّجَاسَةِ بِالْمَاءِ: قَالَتْ عَائِشَةُ: «مَا كَانَ لِإِحْدَانَا إِلَّا ثَوْبٌ وَاحِدٌ تَحِيضُ فِيهِ، فَإِذَا أَصَابَهُ شَيْءٌ مِنْ دَمٍ قَالَتْ بِرِيقِهَا، فَقَصَعَتْهُ بِظُفْرِهَا» (بخاري شريف، بَابٌ : هَلْ تُصَلِّي المَرْأَةُ فِي ثَوْبِ حَاضَتْ فِيهِ؟، نمبر 312)
وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَيَجُوزُ تَطْهِيرُ النَّجَاسَةِ بِالْمَاءِ: عَنْ أَسْمَاءَ بِنْتِ أَبِي بَكْرٍ ...«إِذَا أَصَابَ ثَوْبَ إِحْدَاكُنَّ الدَّمُ مِنَ الخَيْضَةِ فَلْتَقْرُصْهُ، ثُمَّ لِتَنْضَحْهُ بِمَاءٍ، ثُمَّ لِتُصَلِّي فِيهِ»
اصول : نجاست کی دو قسمیں ہیں، حکمیہ جیسے وضوء نماز کی ضرورت ہو، اور حقیقیہ جیسے پیشاپ و پاخانہ وغیرہ۔ اصول : پانی کے علاوہ بھی جن چیزوں سے نجاست کے اجزا دھل جائیں ان سے نجاست کو پاک کرنا جائز ہے۔
Chapter of Impurities. Removing impurity is obligatory from the body of the one praying, his clothes, and the place upon which he prays. And it is permissible to purify impurity with water and with every pure liquid that can remove it, and used water. Proof (a): the verse for establishing removing impurity is obligatory from the body of the one praying: {And your garments purify} (Surah al-Muddaththir 74:4). Proof (2): the hadith... (etc. for all proofs). Principle: Impurities are of two types: hukmi like the need for wudu and prayer, and haqiqi like urine and stool. Principle: Besides water, anything that washes away the particles of impurity can purify it.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on impurities (al-anjas) with a ruling statement. The matn (core text) establishes two main rulings: first, that removing impurity (tathir al-najasah) is obligatory (wajib) from three things: the body of the person praying, their clothes, and the place where they pray. This means that if these become contaminated with a physical impurity (najasah haqiqiyyah), one must clean them before prayer; otherwise, the prayer is not valid. Second, purification can be achieved with water or with any pure liquid (mai' tahir) that can effectively remove the impurity. The author then provides proofs (wujuh) from the Quran and authentic hadith. The first proof is the Quranic verse 'Wa thiyabaka fatahhir' (And purify your garments), which explicitly commands purification of clothing. The subsequent hadith proofs include the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) using water for istinja', the instruction to wash menstrual blood from clothes, and the prohibition of praying in places of impurity. The last hadith also shows that water is the primary purifier. The Urdu notes add a key classification: impurities are of two types—hukmi (legal, like the state of hadath) and haqiqi (physical matter like urine). They also reiterate that non-water liquids can purify if they wash away the impurity. This passage is a foundational text for understanding the obligation of removing impurity (tathir) in the Hanafi school, emphasizing that it is a necessary condition for the validity of salah.

Key Terms
نجاسة (najasah): Any substance that is impure according to Shari'ah, such as urine, blood, wine, etc. The text divides it into hukmiyah (legal impurity like hadath) and haqiqiyah (physical impurity).
تطهير (tathir): The act of removing impurity (najasah) from the body, clothes, or place. It is wajib before prayer.
الماء المستعمل (al-ma' al-musta'mal): Used water – water that has been used for wudu or ghusl. The text mentions it but does not complete the ruling. In context, it likely refers to whether used water can be used for purification; the Hanafi position is that used water is tahir but not mutahhir (it is pure but not purifying).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following can be used to purify a physical impurity?
A) Water only
B) Any pure liquid that can remove the impurity
C) Only water or dust
D) Any liquid, even if impure

Key Takeaway
Removing physical impurity (najasah) from body, clothes, and place of prayer is wajib, and it can be done with water or any pure liquid that washes it away.

Purification of Dry Impurities, Semen, and Solid Surfaces
Rulings with proof for dry impurities

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rulings for purifying dry impurities on khuffs, wet and dry semen, and impurities on solid surfaces.

Core Idea
Dry impurity on leather is purified by earth; wet semen must be washed; dry semen suffices with scraping.

This passage from the Chapter of Impurities provides practical concessions for purification based on the type of impurity and surface. The Hanafi school recognizes that dry impurities on non-absorbent materials can be removed by friction, while wet impurities require washing. Understanding these distinctions is essential for maintaining purity in daily worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three cases
The passage covers three distinct scenarios: dry impurity on a khuff (leather sock), semen (maniyy) on a garment (wet vs. dry), and impurity on a mirror or sword.
Each has a different purification method.
2
Determine the purification method for each
For the khuff: dry impurity with substance (jirm) is purified by rubbing on the ground. For semen: wet must be washed; dry suffices with scraping (fark). For mirrors/swords: wiping (mas-h) is enough.
The method depends on the impurity's state and the surface's absorbency.
3
Examine the prophetic proofs
The khuff ruling relies on the hadith of Abu Hurairah: 'When one of you steps on filth with his sandal, the dust is a purifier.' The semen rulings are based on 'Aisha's practice of washing wet semen and scraping dry semen from the Prophet's garment.
These ahadith are the basis for the Hanafi concessions.
4
Note the conditions and limits
Rubbing works only if the impurity is dry and has substance. For semen, the wet/dry distinction is critical. For solid surfaces, wiping suffices because the impurity does not penetrate.
If the impurity is wet or the surface is absorbent, washing is required.
5
Compare with other schools
The Shafi'i school considers semen pure (tahir) and does not require washing even when wet. The Hanafi position is that semen is najis, but dry scraping is a concession.
This difference has practical implications for daily prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ الْأَنْجَاسِ
وَإِذَا أَصَابَ الْخُفَّ نَجَاسَةٌ لَهَا جِرْمٌ فَجَفَّتْ وَدُلِكَتْ بِالْأَرْضِ جَازَتْ الصَّلَاةُ مَعَهَا وَجَازَتْ الصَّلَاةُ مَعَهُ وَالْمَنِيُّ نَجِسٌ يَجِبُ غَسْلُ رَطْبِهِ فَإِذَا جَفَّ عَلَى الثَّوْبِ أَجْزَأَ فِيهِ الْفَرْكُ وَالنَّجَاسَةُ إِذَا أَصَابَتْ الْمِرْآةَ أَوْ السَّيْفَ اكْتُفِيَ بِمَسْحِهِمَا. 
(حدیث: بخاري شريف، بَابُ غَسْلِ دَمِ المَحِيضِ، 307/ مسلم شريف نَجَاسَةِ الدَّمِ وَكَيْفِيَّةِ غُسْلِهِ (291))
وجه: (٣) الحديث لثبوت وَيَجُوزُ تَطْهِيرُ النَّجَاسَةِ بِالْمَاءِ: عَنْ أَبِي سَعِيدٍ الْخُدْرِيِّ... إِذَا جَاءَ أَحَدُكُمْ إِلَى الْمَسْجِدِ فَلْيَنْظُرْ فَإِنْ رَأَى فِي نَعْلَيْهِ قَذَرًا أَوْ أَذَى فَلْيَمْسَحْهُ وَلْيُصَلِّ فِيهِمَا "(مسند امام احمد،مسند أَبِي سَعِيدٍ الْخُدْرِيّ 11153/ ابو داؤد، بَابُ الصَّلَاةِ فِي النَّعْلِ، 650)
وجه: (ا) الحديث لثبوت وَإِذَا أَصَابَ الْخُفَّ نَجَاسَةٌ لَهَا جِرْمٌ فَجَفَّتْ: عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ، أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «إِذَا وَطِئَ أَحَدُكُمْ بِنَعْلِهِ الْأَذَى، فَإِنَّ التُّرَابَ لَهُ طَهُورٌ» ( ابو داؤد، بَابٌ فِي الْأَذَى يُصِيبُ النَّعْلَ، نمبر (385))
توجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت وَالْمَنِيُّ نَجِسٌ يَجِبُ غَسْلُ رَطْبِهِ: سَأَلْتُ عَائِشَةَ عَنِ الْمَنِيِّ، يُصِيبُ الثَّوْبَ فَقَالَتْ: كُنْتُ أَغْسِلُهُ مِنْ ثَوْبِ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ، فَيَخْرُجُ إِلَى الصَّلَاةِ، وَأَثَرُ الغَسْلِ فِي ثَوْبِهِ» بُقَعُ المَاءِ (بخاري شريف، بَابُ غَسْلِ الْمَنِي وَفَرْكِهِ، وَغَسْلِ مَا يُصِيبُ مِنَ المَرْأَةِ، غير 230/ مسلم شریف ، باب حكم المنى، غير (289))
وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَالْمَنِيُّ نَجِسٌ يَجِبُ غَسْلُ رَطْبِهِ: يَا عَمَّارُ إِنَّمَا يُغْسَلُ الثَّوْبُ مِنْ خَمْسٍ: مِنَ الْغَائِطِ وَالْبَوْلِ وَالْقَيْءِ وَالدَّمِ وَالْمَنِي (سنن الدار قطني، بَابُ نَجَاسَةِ الْبَوْلِ وَالْأَمْرِ بِالتَّتَنَزُّهِ مِنْهُ وَالحكُم فِي بَوْلِ مَا يُؤْكَلُ لَحْمُهُ، غمبر 458)
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت فَإِذَا جَفَّ عَلَى الثَّوْبِ أَجْزَأَ فِيهِ الْفَرْكُ: عَنْ عَائِشَةَ فِي الْمَنِي قَالَتْ: كُنْتُ أَفْرُكُهُ مِنْ ثَوْبِ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ " (مسلم شريف، بَابُ حُكْمِ الْمَنِي ،نمبر 288/سنن الترمذي، باب في الْمَني يُصِيبُ الثَّوْبَ ، نمبر 116)
وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت فَإِذَا جَفَّ عَلَى الثَّوْبِ أَجْزَأَ فِيهِ الْفَرْكُ: عَنْ عَائِشَةَ, قَالَتْ: ... 
اصول : اگر تر منی کپڑے میں ہے تو کپڑے کو دھونا لازم ہے اور خشک منی کھرچ دینے سے پاک ہو جائے گا۔
Chapter of Impurities. And if impurity that has substance (jirm) touches the khuff (leather sock) and dries and is then rubbed against the ground, prayer is permissible with it. And prayer is permissible with it. And semen is impure; it is obligatory to wash it while wet. If it dries on the garment, then rubbing it off suffices. And when impurity touches a mirror or a sword, wiping them suffices. ... Proof (3): the hadith for establishing that purification of impurity with water is permissible: from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri... (etc). Principle: If wet semen is on the garment, washing the garment is necessary, and dry semen, scraping it off will purify it.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage continues the 'Chapter of Impurities' with specific rulings for special cases. The first ruling deals with a khuff (a leather sock worn in wudu) that gets a dry, tangible impurity (najasah laha jirm). If the impurity dries and the khuff is rubbed on the ground (dulk bi al-ard), the impurity is considered removed and prayer is valid. This is based on the hadith of Abu Hurairah that 'the dust is a purifier.' The second ruling concerns maniyy (semen). Semen is considered najis (impure) in the Hanafi school. When wet, it must be washed (ghusl) from the garment. However, if it dries, simply rubbing it off (fark) is sufficient, as evidenced by the practice of 'A'ishah who used to rub dried semen from the Prophet's garment. The third ruling is for smooth, non-absorbent surfaces like mirrors and swords. If impurity touches them, it suffices to wipe them (mas-h), because the impurity does not penetrate. These rulings show the Hanafi principle of easing purification based on practicality (takhfif). The hadith proofs also include the general permission to purify with water, but the specific case of khuff allows rubbing with earth. The Urdu note reiterates the distinction: wet semen must be washed, dry semen is purified by scraping.

Key Terms
الخف (al-khuff): A leather sock worn over the foot, commonly used in Hanafi fiqh for the validity of wiping (mash) during wudu. Here, it refers to any footwear that can be purified by rubbing on earth when impurity is dry.
المني (al-maniyy): Semen, considered najis (impure) in the Hanafi school. The text distinguishes between wet (must be washed) and dry (suffices with rubbing).
الفَرْك (al-fark): Rubbing or scraping off dry impurity. It is sufficient for removing dry maniyy from a garment and for dry impurity on a khuff when rubbed on the ground.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) It is purified by rubbing on the ground
C) It is wiped with a cloth
D) It cannot be purified unless washed

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school provides concessions for purifying dry impurities on specific surfaces, easing the performance of worship.

Purification of Smooth Surfaces by Wiping
Ruling on purifying mirror or sword from impurity by wiping

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on purifying smooth, non-porous surfaces from impurity and identify why wiping suffices.

Core Idea
Smooth surfaces that do not absorb impurity are purified by wiping, not washing.

This brief ruling from al-Quduri's matn states that when an impurity falls on a mirror or sword, simply wiping it off suffices for purification. The underlying principle is that impurity on non-absorbent surfaces can be completely removed by wiping away the physical trace. This reflects a key Hanafi principle that purification depends on the nature of the surface.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objects and the impurity
The objects are a mirror (mir'ah) and a sword (sayf). The impurity (najisah) is any physical substance that makes something impure.
2
Understand the ruling
The ruling states that wiping (mash) the impurity off these objects suffices (yuktafa). The objects become pure once the impurity is removed.
3
Grasp the underlying principle
The reason is that these surfaces are smooth and non-porous; they do not absorb impurity. Therefore, the impurity remains on the surface and can be removed by wiping.
4
Apply to similar items
The same ruling applies to any non-absorbent, smooth surface such as glass, polished metal, or ceramics. Porous surfaces like cloth, wood, or leather require washing.
This is an extension of the ruling based on the common illa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالنَّجَاسَةُ إِذَا أَصَابَتْ الْمِرْآةَ أَوْ السَّيْفَ أَكْتُفِي بِمَسْجِهِمَا
And when impurity strikes a mirror or a sword, wiping them suffices.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This is a brief ruling from the chapter on impurities. It states that when an impurity falls on hard, smooth, non-absorbent items like a mirror or a sword, simply wiping off the impurity suffices for purification. This is because these surfaces do not absorb impurity; the impurity remains on the surface. Therefore, once the physical trace is removed, the item is considered tahir. This ruling is part of the Hanafi jurisprudence on purified surfaces. No proof is cited here, as it is a straightforward ruling from the matn.

Key Terms
الْمِرْآة (al-mir'ah): Mirror; a smooth, non-porous surface that does not absorb moisture.
السَّيْف (as-sayf): Sword; a smooth metal surface, similar in ruling to mirror.
مَسْح (mash): Wiping; the act of passing a hand or cloth over a surface to remove impurity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Washing with water
B) Wiping the impurity off
C) Rubbing with earth
D) Leaving it to dry

Key Takeaway
Smooth, non-absorbent surfaces like mirrors and swords are purified by simply wiping off the impurity.

Ruling on Mani: Wet Washing, Dry Rubbing
Ruling on washing wet mani and rubbing dry mani from cloth

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on mani: state that wet mani must be washed and dry mani can be purified by rubbing, and defend this position with the dalil.

Core Idea
Wet mani must be washed; dry mani only needs rubbing.

This lesson covers a classic Hanafi ruling on the impurity of semen (mani) and the method of purification. The matn from al-Quduri states two distinct rulings: for wet mani, washing is obligatory; for dry mani on a garment, rubbing is sufficient. The author supports this with three hadith from Aisha and Ammar. Understanding this ruling also reveals a key difference with the Shafi'i school, which considers mani pure.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is purification of semen (mani) from a garment. The ruling: mani is najis (impure).
2
Distinguish wet vs dry
Wet mani: washing is wajib. Dry mani: rubbing (fark) suffices for purification.
3
Examine the dalil
Three hadith: Aisha's washing of wet mani, Ammar's list of five impurities (including mani), and Aisha's rubbing of dry mani.
4
Understand the Hanafi istidlal
The explicit mention of mani in Ammar's hadith proves impurity. Aisha's washing confirms the obligation for wet; her rubbing shows a concession for dry.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school holds mani to be pure based on Aisha's rubbing, interpreting it as proof of purity even when wet. The Hanafi school rejects this because Aisha specifically differentiated wet and dry.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالْمَنِيُّ نَجِسٌ يَجِبُ غَسْلُ رَطْبِهِ فَإِذَا جَفَّ عَلَى الثَّوْبِ أَجْزَأَ فِيهِ الْفَرْكُ
عَنْ عَائِشَةَ رَضِيَ اللهُ عَنْهَا قَالَتْ: كُنْتُ أَغْسِلُهُ مِنْ ثَوْبِ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ، فَيَخْرُجُ إِلَى الصَّلَاةِ، وَأَثَرُ الْغَسْلِ فِي ثَوْبِهِ بُقَعُ الْمَاءِ. وَعَنْ عَمَّارٍ: يَا عَمَّارُ إِنَّمَا يُغْسَلُ الثَّوْبُ مِنْ خَمْسٍ: مِنَ الْغَائِطِ وَالْبَوْلِ وَالْقَيْءِ وَالدَّمِ وَالْمَنِي.
وَعَنْ عَائِشَةَ رَضِيَ اللهُ عَنْهَا قَالَتْ: كُنْتُ أَفْرُكُهُ مِنْ ثَوْبِ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ إِذَا كَانَ يَابِسًا، وَأَغْسِلُهُ إِذَا كَانَ رَطْبًا.
And semen is impure; it is obligatory to wash its wetness, and when it dries on the cloth, rubbing suffices in it. From Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her, she said: I used to wash it from the garment of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and he would go out to prayer, and the trace of washing in his garment was water spots. And from Ammar: O Ammar, a garment is only washed from five: from excrement, urine, vomit, blood, and semen. And from Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her, she said: I used to rub it from the garment of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, when it was dry, and I would wash it when it was wet.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage presents two interrelated rulings from the matn on semen (mani). The first states that mani is najis (impure) and that when wet, it must be washed off the garment. The second states that when dry, merely rubbing it off suffices. The author then provides three hadith proofs: (1) Aisha's practice of washing wet mani from the Prophet's garment, (2) The hadith of Ammar listing five impurities requiring washing, (3) Aisha's explicit distinction between rubbing dry mani and washing wet mani. Together, these establish the Hanafi position that mani is impure but dry purification is lighter. The ruling applies specifically to mani from a human male or female; other schools differ: the Shafi'i school holds that mani is pure because of a different interpretation of Aisha's practice. The Hanafi school relies on the explicit Prophet's statement through Ammar and the consistent practice of Aisha.

Key Terms
الْمَنِي (al-maniyy): Semen or vaginal fluid discharged at orgasm; considered impure in Hanafi fiqh.
الْفَرْك (al-fark): Rubbing a dry substance off a cloth to remove impurity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on wet mani on a garment?
A) It is pure and no action needed
B) It must be rubbed dry
C) It must be washed
D) It can be left

Key Takeaway
Wet mani must be washed, dry mani can be rubbed off; this distinction is supported by explicit hadith and distinguishes Hanafi from Shafi'i.

Earth Purified by the Sun: Prayer Allowed, Tayammum Not
Ruling on earth dried after impurity: prayer valid, tayammum invalid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying on earth dried after impurity and explain why tayammum with that earth is invalid.

Core Idea
Drying removes impurity for prayer but not enough to restore earth's purity for tayammum.

A common scenario: impurity falls on ground, then sun dries it. Can we pray there? Can we use that soil for tayammum? The Hanafi school distinguishes between purification for prayer and for tayammum. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its two rulings
Recognize that the passage gives two hukm: prayer is valid, tayammum is invalid.
The act is 'praying on earth that has been impure then dried' and 'using that earth for tayammum'.
2
Locate the dalil
The proofs are from the practice of the Companions (Ibn Umar's hadith) and a statement of the Tabi'i Abu Qilaba.
Ibn Umar reports that dogs urinated in the mosque and the Companions did not prevent it, implying prayer was valid. Abu Qilaba states: 'When earth dries, it has become purified.'
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith shows that drying sufficed for prayer. Abu Qilaba's statement is taken as a general principle that drying purifies earth.
Both proofs indicate purification, but only for prayer purposes.
4
Understand the distinction
Why is the same earth sufficient for prayer but not tayammum? Because tayammum requires the earth itself to be intrinsically pure (tahir fi dhatihi), and impurity leaves doubt about its essential purity.
Prayer only requires the place to be free of visible impurity; tayammum requires absolute purity of the medium.
5
Note the ikhtilaf
Some other schools (e.g., Maliki) allow tayammum with such earth; Hanafi differentiates based on the type of usage.
This distinction is unique to the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا أَصَابَتْ الْأَرْضَ نَجَاسَةٌ فَجَفَّتْ بِالشَّمْسِ وَذَهَبَ أَثَرُهَا جَازَتْ الصَّلَاةُ عَلَى مَكَانِهَا وَلَمْ يَجُزِ التَّيَمُّمُ مِنْهَا
عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ رَضِيَ اللهُ عَنْهُمَا قَالَ: كُنْتُ أَبِيتُ فِي الْمَسْجِدِ فِي عَهْدِ رَسُولِ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ وَكُنْتُ فَتَى شَابًّا عَزَبًا وَكَانَتِ الْكِلَابُ تَبُولُ وَتُقْبِلُ وَتُدْبِرُ فِي الْمَسْجِدِ فَلَمْ يَكُونُوا يَرُدُّونَ شَيْئًا مِنْ ذَلِكَ.
وَعَنْ أَبِي قِلَابَةَ قَالَ: إِذَا جَفَّتِ الْأَرْضُ فَقَدْ زَكَتْ.
And when earth is struck by an impurity, then it dries by the sun and its trace goes away, prayer on that place is permissible, but tayammum from it is not permissible. From Ibn Umar, may Allah be pleased with them both, he said: I used to spend the night in the mosque during the time of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and I was a young unmarried man, and dogs would urinate and come and go in the mosque, and they would not prevent any of that. And from Abu Qilaba, he said: When the earth dries, it has become purified.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling about earth that becomes impure and then dries under the sun such that no trace of impurity remains. The ruling has two parts: (1) prayer is permissible on that spot, meaning the earth is considered pure for prostration; (2) however, tayammum cannot be performed using that soil, because tayammum requires pure earth on its own right, and the impurity that was there leaves a doubt regarding the earth's intrinsic purity. The author provides two proofs: the practice of the Companions in the mosque where dogs urinated and no water was used (indicating drying sufficed for prayer), and the statement of the Tabi'i Abu Qilaba that when earth dries, it is purified (zakāt). This latter is a principle used in Hanafi fiqh. The distinction between prayer and tayammum is crucial: dryness and removal of trace makes the place fit for prayer but does not restore the earth to the status of being a pure substance fit for tayammum, because tayammum requires absolute purity of the medium.

Key Terms
الْأَرْض (al-ard): The ground; natural earth that can be used for tayammum when pure.
التَّيَمُّم (at-tayammum): Dry ablution with pure earth when water is unavailable or harmful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, what is the status of earth that has been contaminated with impurity and then dried by the sun with no trace remaining?
A) It becomes pure for all purposes (prayer and tayammum).
B) It is pure for prayer but not for tayammum.
C) It remains impure until washed.
D) It is pure for tayammum but not for prayer.

Key Takeaway
Earth dried after impurity is pure enough for prayer but not for tayammum due to different standards of purity.

Heavy Impurity Less Than Dirham: Prayer Permissible
Ruling with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of heavy impurity less than a dirham in prayer and identify the evidence used by the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
A heavy impurity smaller than a dirham does not invalidate prayer – a concession from the general purity requirement.

This lesson addresses a common concern: what if a small amount of impure substance, like blood or urine, gets on one's body or clothing during prayer? The Hanafi school provides a clear concession based on the size of a dirham, allowing prayer to be valid for unintentional small amounts. The passage from Al-Quduri's matn states the ruling directly, followed by two hadith that support the principle of leniency in purification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is praying (salat) while carrying a heavy impurity (najasa mughallaza). The ruling: it is permissible (ja'iz) – meaning the prayer is valid (sahih) – if the impurity is the size of a dirham or less.
Dirham here refers to the area of a standard silver coin, approximately the size of a fingertip.
2
Define heavy impurity and the dirham measure
Heavy impurity includes blood, excrement, and urine. The dirham measure is a known unit; in Hanafi fiqh, it is the size of a small coin, roughly 2-3 cm in diameter. The impurity is measured by area, not volume.
Other schools may use different measures; Shafi'i allows less than a dirham of blood specifically.
3
Locate the evidence (dalil)
The author cites two hadith about using stones for istinja'. Although these hadith are about purification from impurity after relieving oneself, they imply that a small amount of impurity can be removed with stones and is thus excused. The direct proof for the dirham ruling is other ahadith (e.g., the hadith of menstruation blood).
The hadith are ahad (singular transmissions), so their thubut is zanni, but the ruling is confirmed by practice and other proofs.
4
Understand the legal link (wajh al-dalalah)
From the hadith, the permissibility of using stones shows that complete removal of impurity is not always required; thus, a small amount of impurity (less than dirham) is overlooked. This is a concession (rukhsa) from the original requirement of purity.
Hanafi usul: the imperative to purify oneself is general, but the Sunnah specifies exceptions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ أَصَابَهُ مِنْ النَّجَاسَةِ الْمُغَلَّظَةِ كَالدَّمِ وَالْغَائِطِ وَالْبَوْلِ مِقْدَارَ الدِّرْهَم جَازَتْ الصَّلَاةُ مَعَهُ
عَنْ عَائِشَةَ رَضِيَ اللهُ عَنْهَا قَالَتْ: إِنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «إِذَا ذَهَبَ أَحَدُكُمْ إِلَى الْغَائِطِ، فَلْيَذْهَبْ مَعَهُ بِثَلَاثَةِ أَحْجَارٍ يَسْتَطِيبُ بِهِنَّ، فَإِنَّهَا تُجْزِئُ عَنْهُ»
وَعَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «إِذَا ذَهَبَ أَحَدُكُمْ إِلَى الْغَائِطِ فَلْيَذْهَبْ مَعَهُ بِثَلَاثَةِ أَحْجَارٍ يَسْتَطِيبُ بِهِنَّ فَإِنَّهَا تُجْزِئُ عَنْهُ»
And whoever is struck by heavy impurity like blood, excrement, and urine to the extent of a dirham, prayer with it is permissible. From Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her, she said: The Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, said: 'When one of you goes to relieve himself, let him take with him three stones to purify himself with, for they suffice him.' And from Abu Hurayra from the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, he said: 'When one of you goes to relieve himself, let him take with him three stones to purify himself with, for they suffice him.'
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage addresses the amount of heavy impurity (najāsa mughallaza) that is excusable in prayer. The matn declares that if a person has heavy impurity such as blood, stool, or urine on his body or clothing that is equal to or less than the area of a dirham coin, then prayer performed with that impurity is valid (jāz). The dirham refers to the size of a silver coin, approximately the area of a fingertip. This is a dispensation from the general requirement of purity. The author then cites two hadith about istinja' using stones, which indicate that purification from impurity is not required to be with water in all cases, and by analogy, a small amount of impurity is overlooked. The hadith show that stones suffice for cleaning, implying that the impurity is not considered negligible? Actually, the connection is to show that some impurity can be dealt with lightly, but the main proof for the dirham ruling is other ahadith (e.g., the hadith about the blood of menstruation). Nonetheless, the author uses these hadith to support the principle of concession. The Hanafi school distinguishes between heavy and light impurities; heavy impurity less than a dirham is excused, while light impurity (like urine of a male baby) has a larger concession.

Key Terms
النَّجَاسَةُ الْمُغَلَّظَةُ (an-najāsa al-mughallaza): Heavy impurity, specifically blood, excrement, urine and similar items that require washing.
الدِّرْهَم (ad-dirham): A silver coin; used as a measure of area approximately equal to the size of a fingertip (about 2-3 cm diameter).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the maximum amount of heavy impurity (like blood) that is excused in prayer?
A) The size of a dirham
B) The size of a grain of rice
C) The size of a palm
D) Any amount is unacceptable

Key Takeaway
Prayer remains valid with a heavy impurity (blood, urine, stool) as long as it does not exceed the area of a dirham.

Light Impurity in Hanafi Fiqh: The Quarter-of-Garment Rule
Ruling on light impurity with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on light impurity and identify the threshold that makes it excused or required for removal.

Core Idea
Light impurity (e.g., urine of edible animals) is excused in prayer if less than a quarter of the garment.

In the Hanafi school, not all impurities are treated equally. This lesson unpacks the concept of light impurity (najasah mukhaffafah) and the specific threshold of one-quarter of the garment. You'll learn the ruling from al-Quduri's matn and the hadith proofs that support it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is praying while light impurity (such as urine of an animal whose meat is eaten) is on the garment. The ruling: prayer is valid as long as the impurity does not reach one-quarter of the garment.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The hadith 'Prayer is repeated due to the amount of a dirham of blood' is cited. By implication, blood below a dirham is excused; light impurity is even more lenient.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but accepted in fiqh.
3
Define the threshold using the Urdu principle
The Urdu text clarifies that 'kathir' (a lot) for light impurity is either what people consider a lot or if it reaches a quarter of the garment. Below that is ma'fu (excused).
This measure is specific to Hanafis.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Shafi'is do not distinguish between light and heavy impurity; any impurity must be removed for prayer validity. Hanafis make this distinction based on necessity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ الْأَنْجَاسِ وَإِنْ أَصَابَهُ نَجَاسَةٌ مُخَفَّفَةٌ كَبَوْلِ مَا يُؤْكَلُ لَحْمُهُ جَازَتْ الصَّلَاةُ مَعَهُ مَا لَمْ يَبْلُغْ رُبُعَ الثَّوْبِ. قَالَ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «تُعَادُ الصَّلَاةُ مِنْ قَدْرِ الدِّرْهَم مِنَ الدَّمِ» (سنن الدار قطني، بَابُ قَدْرِ النَّجَاسَةِ الَّتِي تُبْطِلُ الصَّلَاةَ ، نمبر 1494/ السنن الكبرى البيهقي، بَابُ مَا يَجِبُ غَسْلُهُ مِنَ الدَّمِ، نمبر 4093). وَمَنْ أَصَابَهُ مِنْ النَّجَاسَةِ الْمُغَلَّظَةِ كَالدَّمِ، قَالَ: يَا عَمَّارُ إِنَّمَا يُغْسَلُ الثَّوْبُ مِنْ خَمْسٍ: مِنَ الْغَائِطِ وَالْبَوْلِ وَالْقَيْءِ وَالدَّمِ وَالْمَنِي (سنن الدار قطني، بَابُ نَجَاسَةِ الْبَوْلِ وَالْأَمْرِ بِالتَّنَزُّهِ مِنْهُ وَاحْكُم فِي بَوْلِ مَا يُؤْكَلُ لَحْمُهُ، غبر 458). وَعَنْ أَبِي ثَعْلَبَةَ الْخُشَنِيِّ، أَنَّهُ سَأَلَ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: إِنَّا نُجَاوِرُ أَهْلَ الْكِتَابِ وَهُمْ يَطْبُخُونَ فِي قُدُورِهِمُ الْخِنْزِيرَ وَيَشْرَبُونَ فِي آنِيَتِهِمُ الْخَمْرَ، فَقَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «إِنْ وَجَدْتُمْ غَيْرَهَا فَكُلُوا فِيهَا وَاشْرَبُوا، وَإِنْ لَمْ تَجِدُوا غَيْرَهَا فَارْحَضُوهَا بِالْمَاءِ وَكُلُوا وَاشْرَبُوا» (سنن ابي داؤد، بَابُ الأكل في آنِيَةِ أَهْل الْكِتَابِ غمبر (3839). وَالْآيَةُ: ﴿يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا إِنَّمَا الْخَمْرُ وَالْمَيْسِرُ وَالْأَنْصَابُ وَالْأَزْلَامُ رِجْسٌ مِنْ عَمَلِ الشَّيْطَانِ فَاجْتَنِبُوهُ لَعَلَّكُمْ تُفْلِحُونَ﴾ (سورة المائده، 6 آیت 90). وَعَنْ أَنَسٍ، أَنَّ نَاسًا مِنْ عُرَيْنَةَ قَدِمُوا المَدِينَةَ، فَاجْتَوَوْهَا، فَبَعَثَهُمْ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فِي إِبِلِ الصَّدَقَةِ، وَقَالَ: «اشْرَبُوا مِنْ أَلْبَانِهَا وَأَبْوَالِهَا» (سنن الترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي بَوْلِ مَا يُؤْكَلُ لَحْمُهُ، نمبر72). وَعَنِ الْبَرَاءِ، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «لَا بَأْسَ بِبَوْلِ مَا أُكِلَ لَحْمُهُ» (سنن الدار قطني بَابُ نَجَاسَةِ الْبَوْلِ وَالْأَمْرِ بِالتَّنَرُّهِ مِنْهُ وَالحَكُم فِي بَوْلِ مَا يُؤْكَلُ لَحْمُهُ، غبر (460). أصول : نجاست خفیفہ کی اصل : نجاست خفیفہ اتنا ہو کہ لوگ اسے کثیر سمجھیں، یا کپڑے کے چوتھائی لگ جائے تو وہ کثیر ہے ایسی صورت میں ناپاک ہو گا۔
وَتَطْهِيرُ النَّجَاسَةِ الَّتِي يَجِبُ غَسْلُهَا عَلَى وَجْهَيْنِ فَمَا كَانَ لَهَا عَيْنٌ مَرْئِيَّةٌ فَطَهَارَتُهَا زَوَالُ عَيْنِهَا إِلَّا أَنْ يَبْقَى مِنْ أَثَرِهَا مَا يَشُقُ إِزَالَتُهُ. وَعَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ، أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «يُعَذَّبَانِ، وَمَا يُعَذَّبَانِ فِي كَبِيرٍ» ثُمَّ قَالَ: «بَلَى، كَانَ أَحَدُهُمَا لَا يَسْتَتِرُ مِنْ بَوْلِهِ، وَكَانَ الْآخَرُ يَمْشِي بِالنَّمِيمَةِ». (بخاري شريف، بَابٌ : مِنَ الكَبَائِرِ أَنْ لَا يَسْتَتِرَ مِنْ بَوْلِهِ، نمبر 216/سنن الترمذي، بَابُ التَّشْدِيدِ فِي الْبَوْلِ، نمبر (70). وَعَنْ أَنَسٍ، قَالَ : قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «تَنَزَّهُوا مِنَ الْبَوْلِ فَإِنَّ عَامَّةَ عَذَابِ الْقَبْرِ مِنْهُ». (سنن الدار قطني، بَابُ نَجَاسَةِ الْبَوْلِ وَالْأَمْرِ بِالتَّنَرُّهِ مِنْهُ وَالحكم في بَوْلِ مَا يُؤْكَلُ لَحْمُهُ، غير (459). وَقُلْتُ لِأُمِّ سَلَمَةَ: إِنِّي امْرَأَةٌ أُطِيلُ ذَيْلِي وَأَمْشِي فِي المَكَانِ القَذِرِ؟ فَقَالَتْ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «يُطَهِّرُهُ مَا بَعْدَهُ» وَفِي البَابِ عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ مَسْعُودٍ قَالَ: «كُنَّا مَعَ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ لَا نَتَوَضَّأُ مِنَ المَوْطَئِ». (سنن الترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي الوُضُوءِ مِنَ المَوْطَإِ ، نمبر 143/سنن ابي داؤد، بَابٌ في الرَّجُل يَطَأُ الْأَذَى بِرِجْلِهِ، نمبر (204). وَعَنْ أَسْمَاءَ بِنْتِ أَبِي بَكْرٍ أَنَّهَا قَالَتْ: سَأَلَتِ امْرَأَةٌ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فَقَالَتْ : يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، أَرَأَيْتَ إِحْدَانَا إِذَا أَصَابَ ثَوْبَهَا الدَّمُ مِنَ الْحَيْضَةِ كَيْفَ تَصْنَعُ؟ قَالَ: «إِذَا أَصَابَ إِحْدَاكُنَّ الدَّمُ مِنَ الْحَيْضِ فَلْتَقْرُصْهُ، ثُمَّ لِتَنْصَحْهُ بِالْمَاءِ، ثُمَّ لِتُصَلِّ» (سنن ابي داؤد ، بَابُ الْمَرْأَةُ تَغْسِلُ ثَوْبَهَا الَّذِي تَلْبَسُهُ فِي حَيْضِها، نمبر (361). وَعَنْ عَائِشَةَ قَالَتْ: جَاءَتْ فَاطِمَةُ بِنْتُ أَبِي حُبَيْشٍ فَقَالَ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «...وَإِذَا أَدْبَرَتْ فَاغْسِلِي عَنْكِ الدَّمَ وَصَلِّي» (مسلم شريف، بَابُ الْمُسْتَحَاضَةِ وَغَسْلِهَا وَصَلَاتِهَا ، نمبر (333). أصول : نجاست پاک کرنے کے بعد نشان اور اثر باقی رہنے سے کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔
Chapter of Impurities: If a light impurity like urine of an animal whose meat is eaten strikes it, prayer is permitted with it as long as it does not reach a quarter of the garment. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Prayer is repeated due to the amount of a dirham of blood.' And whoever is struck by heavy impurity like blood: 'O 'Ammar, the garment is only washed from five: stool, urine, vomit, blood, and semen.' And from Abu Tha'laba al-Khushani, that he asked the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'We live near the People of the Book and they cook pork in their pots and drink wine in their vessels.' The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'If you find other than them, eat and drink in them; and if you do not find other than them, then wash them with water and eat and drink.' And the verse: 'O you who believe, indeed intoxicants, gambling, [sacrificing to] stones, and divining arrows are an abomination of Satan's work; so avoid it that you may be successful' (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:90). And from Anas, that a group from 'Uraynah came to Medina, found it unhealthy, so the Messenger of Allah sent them to the camels of sadaqah and said: 'Drink from their milk and urine.' And from al-Bara', he said: the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'There is no harm in the urine of what is eaten of its meat.' Principle: The origin of light impurity: Light impurity is such that people consider it a lot, or if it affects a quarter of the garment then it is a lot, and in that case it is impure. And purification of impurity that must be washed is of two types: what has a visible substance, its purification is removal of its substance unless there remains of its trace something whose removal is difficult. And from Ibn 'Abbas, that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'They are being punished, and they are not being punished for a major thing.' Then he said: 'Yes, one of them did not protect himself from urine, and the other used to walk with gossip.' And from Anas, he said: the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Be careful of urine, for indeed the majority of the punishment of the grave is due to it.' And I said to Umm Salamah: 'I am a woman who lengthens her hem and walks in a dirty place.' She said: the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'That which comes after it purifies it.' And in this chapter, from 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud: 'We were with the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and we did not perform ablution from stepping on [impure ground].' And from Asma bint Abi Bakr, she said: a woman asked the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him): 'O Messenger of Allah, what do you see about one of us when blood from menstruation strikes her garment, how should she act?' He said: 'When the blood from menstruation strikes one of you, let her rub it, then sprinkle water on it, then pray.' And from 'Aishah, she said: Fatimah bint Abi Hubaish came, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: '...and when it ends, wash the blood from you and pray.' Principle: After purifying impurity, there is no harm if a mark or effect remains.
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the chapter of impurities from al-Quduri's matn. It begins by stating the ruling on light impurity (najasah mukhaffafah), such as urine of an animal whose meat is eaten. The Hanafi position is that such impurity is excused in prayer if it is less than a quarter of the garment. The proof cited is a hadith that prayer must be repeated if blood (a heavy impurity) reaches the size of a dirham, implying that less than that is forgiven. The commentary then provides several hadith proofs for both heavy and light impurities: the hadith listing five impure substances, the hadith about washing utensils of People of the Book, and the Qur'anic verse declaring wine and gambling as rijs (impurity). For light impurity, the hadith of the camel urine and the saying 'no harm in urine of edible animal' are given. The Urdu principle clarifies that 'kathir' (a lot) for light impurity is defined as either what people consider a lot or reaching a quarter of the garment. Then the passage moves to purification of heavy impurity: if the impurity has a visible body, its removal suffices unless its trace is difficult to remove. Hadith proofs include the warning against not protecting from urine, the purification of a dress hem by subsequent clean ground, and the method for washing menstrual blood. The final Urdu principle states that residual marks after washing are excused.

Key Terms
نَجَاسَةٌ مُخَفَّفَةٌ (najasah mukhaffafah): Light impurity such as urine of animals whose meat is eaten; it is excused if it covers less than a quarter of the garment.
رُبْعُ الثَّوْبِ (rub' al-thawb): One quarter of the garment; the threshold beyond which light impurity prevents valid prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a person prays with light impurity (e.g., urine of a sheep) that covers one-eighth of his garment?
A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The prayer is valid as long as the impurity is less than a quarter of the garment.
C) The prayer is valid only if the impurity is less than a dirham in size.
D) The prayer is valid only if he washes the impurity before praying.

Key Takeaway
Light impurity (najasah mukhaffafah) is excused in prayer if it covers less than a quarter of the garment, based on textual proofs and Hanafi legal reasoning.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
10 min
Heavy Impurity and Purification in Hanafi Fiqh
Ruling on heavy impurity categories and purification methods with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the types of heavy impurity and state the Hanafi method for their purification, including the allowance for residual traces.

Core Idea
Heavy impurity (najasah mughallazah) requires washing; if it has a visible substance, removal suffices; residual marks are excused.

After the ruling on light impurity, al-Quduri's text turns to heavy impurities and their purification. This lesson covers the five categories of heavy impurity, the method of purification (removal of substance, difficulty trace), and additional hadith proofs on avoiding impurity and purifying common surfaces.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five heavy impurities
The hadith from 'Ammar lists five things that require washing: stool, urine, vomit, blood, and semen. These are considered heavy impurity (najasah mughallazah).
Dog saliva and other items are added later, but the core five are from this hadith.
2
Understand the purification method
For heavy impurity with a visible body, purification is simply removing the body (zawal al-'ayn). If a trace remains that is difficult to remove, it is forgiven.
This is based on the principle of 'mashaqqah' (hardship).
3
Learn the additional proofs for avoidance
Hadith warn against urine (major punishment in grave) and show that ground purifies a hem (ma ba'dahu yutahhiruhu). Also, menstrual blood is washed as per prophetic instruction.
These illustrate practical applications of purification.
4
Note the final Urdu principle
After purification, any remaining mark or effect (such as a stain) does not harm the validity of prayer.
This is a dispensation for difficulty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ الْأَنْجَاسِ وَإِنْ أَصَابَهُ نَجَاسَةٌ مُخَفَّفَةٌ كَبَوْلِ مَا يُؤْكَلُ لَحْمُهُ جَازَتْ الصَّلَاةُ مَعَهُ مَا لَمْ يَبْلُغْ رُبُعَ الثَّوْبِ. قَالَ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «تُعَادُ الصَّلَاةُ مِنْ قَدْرِ الدِّرْهَم مِنَ الدَّمِ» (سنن الدار قطني، بَابُ قَدْرِ النَّجَاسَةِ الَّتِي تُبْطِلُ الصَّلَاةَ ، نمبر 1494/ السنن الكبرى البيهقي، بَابُ مَا يَجِبُ غَسْلُهُ مِنَ الدَّمِ، نمبر 4093). وَمَنْ أَصَابَهُ مِنْ النَّجَاسَةِ الْمُغَلَّظَةِ كَالدَّمِ، قَالَ: يَا عَمَّارُ إِنَّمَا يُغْسَلُ الثَّوْبُ مِنْ خَمْسٍ: مِنَ الْغَائِطِ وَالْبَوْلِ وَالْقَيْءِ وَالدَّمِ وَالْمَنِي (سنن الدار قطني، بَابُ نَجَاسَةِ الْبَوْلِ وَالْأَمْرِ بِالتَّنَزُّهِ مِنْهُ وَاحْكُم فِي بَوْلِ مَا يُؤْكَلُ لَحْمُهُ، غبر 458). وَعَنْ أَبِي ثَعْلَبَةَ الْخُشَنِيِّ، أَنَّهُ سَأَلَ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: إِنَّا نُجَاوِرُ أَهْلَ الْكِتَابِ وَهُمْ يَطْبُخُونَ فِي قُدُورِهِمُ الْخِنْزِيرَ وَيَشْرَبُونَ فِي آنِيَتِهِمُ الْخَمْرَ، فَقَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «إِنْ وَجَدْتُمْ غَيْرَهَا فَكُلُوا فِيهَا وَاشْرَبُوا، وَإِنْ لَمْ تَجِدُوا غَيْرَهَا فَارْحَضُوهَا بِالْمَاءِ وَكُلُوا وَاشْرَبُوا» (سنن ابي داؤد، بَابُ الأكل في آنِيَةِ أَهْل الْكِتَابِ غمبر (3839). وَالْآيَةُ: ﴿يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا إِنَّمَا الْخَمْرُ وَالْمَيْسِرُ وَالْأَنْصَابُ وَالْأَزْلَامُ رِجْسٌ مِنْ عَمَلِ الشَّيْطَانِ فَاجْتَنِبُوهُ لَعَلَّكُمْ تُفْلِحُونَ﴾ (سورة المائده، 6 آیت 90). وَعَنْ أَنَسٍ، أَنَّ نَاسًا مِنْ عُرَيْنَةَ قَدِمُوا المَدِينَةَ، فَاجْتَوَوْهَا، فَبَعَثَهُمْ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فِي إِبِلِ الصَّدَقَةِ، وَقَالَ: «اشْرَبُوا مِنْ أَلْبَانِهَا وَأَبْوَالِهَا» (سنن الترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي بَوْلِ مَا يُؤْكَلُ لَحْمُهُ، نمبر72). وَعَنِ الْبَرَاءِ، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «لَا بَأْسَ بِبَوْلِ مَا أُكِلَ لَحْمُهُ» (سنن الدار قطني بَابُ نَجَاسَةِ الْبَوْلِ وَالْأَمْرِ بِالتَّنَرُّهِ مِنْهُ وَالحَكُم فِي بَوْلِ مَا يُؤْكَلُ لَحْمُهُ، غبر (460). أصول : نجاست خفیفہ کی اصل : نجاست خفیفہ اتنا ہو کہ لوگ اسے کثیر سمجھیں، یا کپڑے کے چوتھائی لگ جائے تو وہ کثیر ہے ایسی صورت میں ناپاک ہو گا۔
وَتَطْهِيرُ النَّجَاسَةِ الَّتِي يَجِبُ غَسْلُهَا عَلَى وَجْهَيْنِ فَمَا كَانَ لَهَا عَيْنٌ مَرْئِيَّةٌ فَطَهَارَتُهَا زَوَالُ عَيْنِهَا إِلَّا أَنْ يَبْقَى مِنْ أَثَرِهَا مَا يَشُقُ إِزَالَتُهُ. وَعَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ، أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «يُعَذَّبَانِ، وَمَا يُعَذَّبَانِ فِي كَبِيرٍ» ثُمَّ قَالَ: «بَلَى، كَانَ أَحَدُهُمَا لَا يَسْتَتِرُ مِنْ بَوْلِهِ، وَكَانَ الْآخَرُ يَمْشِي بِالنَّمِيمَةِ». (بخاري شريف، بَابٌ : مِنَ الكَبَائِرِ أَنْ لَا يَسْتَتِرَ مِنْ بَوْلِهِ، نمبر 216/سنن الترمذي، بَابُ التَّشْدِيدِ فِي الْبَوْلِ، نمبر (70). وَعَنْ أَنَسٍ، قَالَ : قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «تَنَزَّهُوا مِنَ الْبَوْلِ فَإِنَّ عَامَّةَ عَذَابِ الْقَبْرِ مِنْهُ». (سنن الدار قطني، بَابُ نَجَاسَةِ الْبَوْلِ وَالْأَمْرِ بِالتَّنَرُّهِ مِنْهُ وَالحكم في بَوْلِ مَا يُؤْكَلُ لَحْمُهُ، غير (459). وَقُلْتُ لِأُمِّ سَلَمَةَ: إِنِّي امْرَأَةٌ أُطِيلُ ذَيْلِي وَأَمْشِي فِي المَكَانِ القَذِرِ؟ فَقَالَتْ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «يُطَهِّرُهُ مَا بَعْدَهُ» وَفِي البَابِ عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ مَسْعُودٍ قَالَ: «كُنَّا مَعَ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ لَا نَتَوَضَّأُ مِنَ المَوْطَئِ». (سنن الترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي الوُضُوءِ مِنَ المَوْطَإِ ، نمبر 143/سنن ابي داؤد، بَابٌ في الرَّجُل يَطَأُ الْأَذَى بِرِجْلِهِ، نمبر (204). وَعَنْ أَسْمَاءَ بِنْتِ أَبِي بَكْرٍ أَنَّهَا قَالَتْ: سَأَلَتِ امْرَأَةٌ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فَقَالَتْ : يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، أَرَأَيْتَ إِحْدَانَا إِذَا أَصَابَ ثَوْبَهَا الدَّمُ مِنَ الْحَيْضَةِ كَيْفَ تَصْنَعُ؟ قَالَ: «إِذَا أَصَابَ إِحْدَاكُنَّ الدَّمُ مِنَ الْحَيْضِ فَلْتَقْرُصْهُ، ثُمَّ لِتَنْصَحْهُ بِالْمَاءِ، ثُمَّ لِتُصَلِّ» (سنن ابي داؤد ، بَابُ الْمَرْأَةُ تَغْسِلُ ثَوْبَهَا الَّذِي تَلْبَسُهُ فِي حَيْضِها، نمبر (361). وَعَنْ عَائِشَةَ قَالَتْ: جَاءَتْ فَاطِمَةُ بِنْتُ أَبِي حُبَيْشٍ فَقَالَ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «...وَإِذَا أَدْبَرَتْ فَاغْسِلِي عَنْكِ الدَّمَ وَصَلِّي» (مسلم شريف، بَابُ الْمُسْتَحَاضَةِ وَغَسْلِهَا وَصَلَاتِهَا ، نمبر (333). أصول : نجاست پاک کرنے کے بعد نشان اور اثر باقی رہنے سے کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔
Chapter of Impurities: If a light impurity like urine of an animal whose meat is eaten strikes it, prayer is permitted with it as long as it does not reach a quarter of the garment. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Prayer is repeated due to the amount of a dirham of blood.' And whoever is struck by heavy impurity like blood: 'O 'Ammar, the garment is only washed from five: stool, urine, vomit, blood, and semen.' And from Abu Tha'laba al-Khushani, that he asked the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'We live near the People of the Book and they cook pork in their pots and drink wine in their vessels.' The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'If you find other than them, eat and drink in them; and if you do not find other than them, then wash them with water and eat and drink.' And the verse: 'O you who believe, indeed intoxicants, gambling, [sacrificing to] stones, and divining arrows are an abomination of Satan's work; so avoid it that you may be successful' (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:90). And from Anas, that a group from 'Uraynah came to Medina, found it unhealthy, so the Messenger of Allah sent them to the camels of sadaqah and said: 'Drink from their milk and urine.' And from al-Bara', he said: the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'There is no harm in the urine of what is eaten of its meat.' Principle: The origin of light impurity: Light impurity is such that people consider it a lot, or if it affects a quarter of the garment then it is a lot, and in that case it is impure. And purification of impurity that must be washed is of two types: what has a visible substance, its purification is removal of its substance unless there remains of its trace something whose removal is difficult. And from Ibn 'Abbas, that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'They are being punished, and they are not being punished for a major thing.' Then he said: 'Yes, one of them did not protect himself from urine, and the other used to walk with gossip.' And from Anas, he said: the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Be careful of urine, for indeed the majority of the punishment of the grave is due to it.' And I said to Umm Salamah: 'I am a woman who lengthens her hem and walks in a dirty place.' She said: the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'That which comes after it purifies it.' And in this chapter, from 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud: 'We were with the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and we did not perform ablution from stepping on [impure ground].' And from Asma bint Abi Bakr, she said: a woman asked the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him): 'O Messenger of Allah, what do you see about one of us when blood from menstruation strikes her garment, how should she act?' He said: 'When the blood from menstruation strikes one of you, let her rub it, then sprinkle water on it, then pray.' And from 'Aishah, she said: Fatimah bint Abi Hubaish came, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: '...and when it ends, wash the blood from you and pray.' Principle: After purifying impurity, there is no harm if a mark or effect remains.
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the chapter of impurities from al-Quduri's matn. It begins by stating the ruling on light impurity (najasah mukhaffafah), such as urine of an animal whose meat is eaten. The Hanafi position is that such impurity is excused in prayer if it is less than a quarter of the garment. The proof cited is a hadith that prayer must be repeated if blood (a heavy impurity) reaches the size of a dirham, implying that less than that is forgiven. The commentary then provides several hadith proofs for both heavy and light impurities: the hadith listing five impure substances, the hadith about washing utensils of People of the Book, and the Qur'anic verse declaring wine and gambling as rijs (impurity). For light impurity, the hadith of the camel urine and the saying 'no harm in urine of edible animal' are given. The Urdu principle clarifies that 'kathir' (a lot) for light impurity is defined as either what people consider a lot or reaching a quarter of the garment. Then the passage moves to purification of heavy impurity: if the impurity has a visible body, its removal suffices unless its trace is difficult to remove. Hadith proofs include the warning against not protecting from urine, the purification of a dress hem by subsequent clean ground, and the method for washing menstrual blood. The final Urdu principle states that residual marks after washing are excused.

Key Terms
نَجَاسَةٌ مُغَلَّظَةٌ (najasah mughallazah): Heavy impurity such as blood, urine of humans, stool, vomit, semen; requires full washing and is not excused beyond negligible amounts (dirham size).
زَوَالُ الْعَيْنِ (zawal al-'ayn): Removal of the visible substance of impurity; this suffices for purification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the minimal requirement for purifying a garment that has a heavy impurity like blood?
A) Washing three times with water and sand.
B) Removing the visible blood; a remaining stain is acceptable if difficult to remove.
C) Scrubbing until no trace remains at all.
D) Dry cleaning only.

Key Takeaway
Heavy impurity is purified by removing its visible substance; residual traces that are difficult to remove do not affect ritual purity in the Hanafi school.
