Taharah — Purification
beginner
6 min
Purification of Visible Impurities (Najasah 'Ayniyyah)
Ruling on purifying najasah with a visible substance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for purifying a visible impurity (najasah 'ayniyyah) and apply the hadith proofs to determine when a residual stain is excused.

Core Idea
Removal of the substance itself purifies the garment; a difficult-to-remove stain is excused.

In this lesson, we examine a key ruling from al-Quduri on how to purify garments when a visible impurity, such as menstrual blood or urine, is present. The Hanafi school emphasizes the removal of the substance itself, but allows for residual traces that cannot be practically eliminated. We will also study the hadith proofs that support this principle, including the famous hadith about the woman with menstrual blood and the command to rub and rinse.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage begins with 'وَتَطْهِيرُ النَّجَاسَةِ الَّتِي يَجِبُ غَسْلُهَا' — the purification of an impurity that must be washed. Identify the ruling (wajib) and the act (removing visible substance).
The word 'يجب' indicates obligation (wujub).
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites hadith proofs for both light impurities (urine) and heavy impurities (menstrual blood). Identify the key proof: the hadith of Asma bint Abi Bakr for menstrual blood.
Other hadiths on urine emphasize severity but follow the same principle.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
In the hadith of Asma, the Prophet instructs: 'فلتقرصه، ثم لتنضحه بالماء' — rub, then rinse. This shows that removal of the substance is the method; a residual stain is tolerated.
The rubbing removes the visible substance; rinsing cleanses the area.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school requires complete disappearance of color, smell, and taste. The Hanafi school allows moderate residue if removal is difficult, as stated in the matn: 'إلا أن يبقى من أثرها ما يشق إزالته'.
This ikhtilaf is based on differing interpretations of the same hadith.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi due to the principle of ease (yusr) and the explicit wording of the matn. The residual stain is excused if its removal causes hardship.
The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ الْأَنْجَاسِ
وَتَطْهِيرُ النَّجَاسَةِ الَّتِي يَجِبُ غَسْلُهَا عَلَى وَجْهَيْنِ فَمَا كَانَ لَهَا عَيْنٌ مَرْئِيَّةٌ فَطَهَارَتُهَا زَوَالُ عَيْنِهَا إِلَّا أَنْ يَبْقَى مِنْ أَثَرِهَا مَا يَشُقُ إِزَالَتُهُ.
وَجْهٌ (٣) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَإِنْ أَصَابَهُ نَجَاسَةٌ مُخَفَّفَةٌ: عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ... فَقَالَ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «يُعَذَّبَانِ، وَمَا يُعَذِّبَانِ فِي كَبِيرٍ» ثُمَّ قَالَ: «بَلَى، كَانَ أَحَدُهُمَا لَا يَسْتَتِرُ مِنْ بَوْلِهِ، وَكَانَ الْآخَرُ يَمْشِي بِالنَّمِيمَةِ».
وَجْهٌ (٤) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَإِنْ أَصَابَهُ نَجَاسَةٌ مُخَفَّفَةٌ: عَنْ أَنَسٍ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «تَنَزَّهُوا مِنَ الْبَوْلِ فَإِنَّ عَامَّةَ عَذَابِ الْقَبْرِ مِنْهُ».
وَجْهٌ (٥) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَإِنْ أَصَابَهُ نَجَاسَةٌ مُخَفَّفَةٌ: قُلْتُ لِأُمِّ سَلَمَةَ إِنِّي امْرَأَةٌ أُطِيلُ ذَيْلِي وَأَمْشِي فِي الْمَكَانِ الْقَذِرِ؟ فَقَالَتْ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «يُطَهِّرُهُ مَا بَعْدَهُ». وَفِي الْبَابِ عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ مَسْعُودٍ قَالَ: كُنَّا مَعَ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ لَا نَتَوَضَّأُ مِنَ الْمَوْطَإِ.
وَجْهٌ (١) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَتَطْهِيرُ النَّجَاسَةِ الَّتِي يَجِبُ غَسْلُهَا: عَنْ أَسْمَاءَ بِنْتِ أَبِي بَكْرٍ أَنَّهَا قَالَتْ: سَأَلَتِ امْرَأَةٌ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فَقَالَتْ: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، أَرَأَيْتَ إِحْدَانَا إِذَا أَصَابَ ثَوْبَهَا الدَّمُ مِنَ الْخَيْضَةِ كَيْفَ تَصْنَعُ؟ قَالَ: «إِذَا أَصَابَ إِحْدَاكُنَّ الدَّمُ مِنَ الْخَيْضِ فَلْتَقْرُصْهُ، ثُمَّ لِتَنْصَحْهُ بِالْمَاءِ، ثُمَّ لِتُصَلِّ».
وَجْهٌ (٢) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَتَطْهِيرُ النَّجَاسَةِ الَّتِي يَجِبُ غَسْلُهَا: عَنْ عَائِشَةَ قَالَتْ: جَاءَتْ فَاطِمَةُ بِنْتُ أَبِي حُبَيْشٍ... وَإِذَا أَدْبَرَتْ فَاغْسِلِي عَنْكِ الدَّمَ وَصَلِّي.
Chapter of impurities. And purification of the impurity which must be washed is of two types: that which has a visible substance, its purification is the removal of its substance unless there remains from its trace something whose removal is difficult. Proof (3) for establishing that if a light impurity afflicts him: from Ibn Abbas... the Prophet said, 'They are being punished, and they are not being punished for something great.' Then he said, 'Indeed, one of them did not protect himself from urine, and the other went about with tale-bearing.' Proof (4) for establishing that if a light impurity afflicts him: from Anas, he said: the Messenger of Allah said, 'Protect yourselves from urine, for indeed most of the punishment of the grave is from it.' Proof (5) for establishing that if a light impurity afflicts him: I said to Umm Salamah, 'I am a woman who lengthens my dress and walks in a dirty place?' She said: the Messenger of Allah said, 'What comes after it purifies it.' And in this chapter from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud who said, 'We were with the Messenger of Allah and did not perform wudu from stepping on impurity.' Proof (1) for establishing the purification of the impurity which must be washed: from Asma bint Abi Bakr, she said: a woman asked the Messenger of Allah, 'O Messenger of Allah, what do you think if one of us gets blood from menstruation on her garment, what should she do?' He said, 'If one of you gets blood from menstruation, let her rub it, then rinse it with water, then pray.' Proof (2) for establishing the purification of the impurity which must be washed: from Aisha, she said: Fatimah bint Abi Hubaysh came... 'And when it recedes, wash the blood from yourself and pray.'
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from al-Quduri's matn on the purification of impurities. The core ruling is that if an impurity has a visible substance (like blood or urine), it must be washed until the substance is completely removed. However, if a stain remains that is extremely difficult to remove, it is excused, and the garment is considered pure. The hadith proofs emphasize the severity of not cleaning urine and provide practical guidance for menstrual blood. The hadith of the woman with the long dress shows that if one walks on a dirty surface, subsequent clean ground purifies the footsteps, which is a specific application of the principle of removal of the substance. The overall lesson is that the method of purification depends on the nature of the impurity.

Key Terms
نَجَاسَة (najasah): An impurity that requires washing to purify
عَيْنٌ مَرْئِيَّة ('ayn mar'iyyah): A visible substance of the impurity that can be seen
مُخَفَّفَة (mukhaffafah): Light impurity, such as small amounts of urine

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a visible impurity like menstrual blood gets on a garment, what is the method of purification?
A) Wipe the garment three times
B) Rub the spot, then rinse with water
C) Wash the entire garment three times
D) Sprinkle water over the stain

Key Takeaway
Removal of the visible substance is obligatory; any residual trace that is extremely difficult to remove is excused, based on the hadith of Asma and the principle of ease.

Taharah — Purification
beginner

Purification of Non-Visible Impurities (Najasah Ghayr Mar'iyyah)
Ruling on purifying najasah without visible substance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for purifying non-visible impurities and apply the criterion of ghalabat al-zann (dominant opinion) to determine when purification is achieved.

Core Idea
Non-visible impurities are purified by washing until one is dominantly sure it is clean – ghalabat al-zann suffices, not absolute certainty.

This passage completes the chapter on impurities by addressing what to do when the impurity has no visible substance. Unlike heavy impurities that require a specific number of washes, here the standard is the washer's dominant opinion (ghalabat al-zann) that the impurity is gone. The text provides three hadith proofs to illustrate this principle, including the famous hand-washing after sleep and dog lapping. Understanding this ruling prevents excessive or insufficient washing in daily life.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being purified? A garment or vessel contaminated with a non-visible impurity. The ruling is that it must be washed until the washer is dominantly sure (ghalabat al-zann) it is clean.
Non-visible means no color, taste, or smell can be perceived.
2
Locate the dalil
Three hadith are cited: 1) The hand after sleep hadith, 2) The dog lapping hadith, 3) The menstruation blood hadith. Each demonstrates washing based on probability of impurity.
The proofs are ahad (single-narrator) hadith, which are zanni in thubut.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hand hadith shows that because one does not know where the hand spent the night, it is treated as possibly impure, and washing three times is recommended to achieve dominant opinion of cleanliness. Similarly for dog lapping.
The proof does not mandate three washes for all cases; it illustrates the principle of overcoming doubt.
4
Understand the criterion: ghalabat al-zann
Ghalabat al-zann means the stronger probability, not certainty. As long as the person is fairly sure the impurity is gone, no further washing is required. Traces or marks that remain after thorough washing are excused.
This criterion is unique to the Hanafi school in many rulings, based on ease.
5
Apply the consequence
If after washing the area appears clean according to dominant opinion, the item is pure. If a trace remains (e.g., a stain that cannot be removed), it does not harm purity.
This applies to both light and heavy impurities when they are non-visible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَا لَيْسَ لَهَا عَيْنٌ مَرْئِيَّةٌ فَطَهَارَتُهَا أَنْ تُغْسَلَ حَتَّى يَغْلِبَ عَلَى ظَنِّ الْغَاسِلِ أَنَّهَا قَدْ طَهُرَتْ.
وَجْهٌ (٣) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَتَطْهِيرُ النَّجَاسَةِ الَّتِي يَجِبُ غَسْلُهَا: سَأَلْتُ عَائِشَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهَا عَنِ الْخَائِضِ يُصِيبُ ثَوْبَهَا الدَّمُ قَالَتْ: «تَغْسِلُهُ فَإِنْ لَمْ يَذْهَبْ أَثَرُهُ فَلْتُغَيَّرَهُ بِشَيْءٍ مِنْ صُفْرَةِ».
وَجْهٌ (١) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَمَا لَيْسَ لَهَا عَيْنٌ مَرْئِيَّةٌ فَطَهَارَتُهَا أَنْ تُغْسَلَ: عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «إِذَا اسْتَيْقَظَ أَحَدُكُمْ مِنْ نَوْمِهِ، فَلَا يَغْمِسْ يَدَهُ فِي الْإِنَاءِ حَتَّى يَغْسِلَهَا ثَلَاثًا، فَإِنَّهُ لَا يَدْرِي أَيْنَ بَاتَتْ يَدُهُ».
وَجْهٌ (٢) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَمَا لَيْسَ لَهَا عَيْنٌ مَرْئِيَّةٌ فَطَهَارَتُهَا أَنْ تُغْسَلَ: عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ قَالَ: «إِذَا وَلَغَ الْكَلْبُ فِي الْإِنَاءِ فَاهْرِقْهُ ثُمَّ اغْسِلْهُ ثَلَاثَ مَرَّاتٍ»
أُصُولٌ: نَجَاسَتْ پاک کرنے کے بعد نشان اور اثر باقی رہنے سے کوئی حرج نہیں ہے.
And that which does not have a visible substance, its purification is that it be washed until it is dominant in the opinion of the washer that it has become pure. Proof (3) for establishing the purification of the impurity which must be washed: I asked Aisha about a menstruating woman whose garment gets blood on it; she said: 'Wash it, and if its trace does not go, then change it with something of yellowness.' Proof (1) for establishing that what has no visible substance, its purification is that it be washed: from Abu Hurayrah that the Prophet said: 'If one of you wakes from sleep, do not dip his hand into the vessel until he washes it three times, for he does not know where his hand spent the night.' Proof (2) for establishing that what has no visible substance, its purification is that it be washed: from Abu Hurayrah who said: 'If a dog laps from a vessel, then pour it out and wash it three times.' Principles: After purifying impurity, there is no harm if a mark or trace remains.
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage completes the chapter on impurities by addressing non-visible impurities. The ruling is that if the impurity has no visible substance (e.g., residual traces of alcohol or diluted urine), one must wash the area until it is the dominant opinion (ghalib al-zann) that it is clean. This is based on the principle that complete certainty is not required; a strong likelihood suffices. The hadith proofs include instructions for washing hands after sleep due to possibility of impurity, and for cleansing a vessel from a dog's lapping. These emphasize thorough washing based on probability. The Urdu note at the end reiterates that if a trace or mark remains after washing, it is not harmful, as long as the impurity is gone. This is consistent with the first ruling's exception for difficult-to-remove stains.

Key Terms
غَلَبَة الظَّن (ghalabat al-zann): Dominant opinion or reasonable certainty, not absolute certainty
الْأَنْجَاس (al-anjas): Plural of najas, substances considered impure
أَصَابَهُ نَجَاسَةٌ مُخَفَّفَة (asabahu najasah mukhaffafah): A light impurity, such as urine of animals whose meat is eaten

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
For a non-visible impurity (like residual alcohol on a cloth), how many times should one wash according to the Hanafi school?
A) Exactly three times
B) Until no trace remains
C) Until one is dominantly sure it is clean
D) It must be purified by the sun

Key Takeaway
Non-visible impurities require washing until ghalabat al-zann of cleanliness; complete removal of trace is not required.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
10 min
Purifying Non-Visible Impurities: The Criterion of Dominant Assumption
Ruling with three hadith proofs for cleaning non-visible impurities

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for purifying non-visible impurities (najasat ghayr mar'iyya) and explain how the three cited hadith support the criterion of ghalabat al-zann.

Core Idea
Non-visible impurities are purified by washing until the washer is reasonably certain—no fixed number.

This passage from al-Quduri presents a foundational ruling in Hanafi taharah: how to purify an impurity that leaves no visible trace. Unlike visible impurities where removal of trace is the standard, for non-visible impurities the criterion is the washer's dominant assumption (ghalabat al-zann) that the impurity is gone. The author then adduces three hadiths that reinforce this principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the opening sentence: 'وَمَا لَيْسَ لَهَا عَيْنٌ مَرْتَيَّةٌ فَطَهَارَتُهَا أَنْ تُغْسَلَ حَتَّى يَغْلِبَ عَلَى ظَنِّ الْغَاسِلِ أَنَّهَا قَدْ طَهُرَتْ'. State the ruling in your own words: what is the purification method and what is the criterion?
Note the term 'غَلَبَة الظَّنّ' (dominant assumption).
2
Locate the evidence
The passage cites three hadiths. List them: (1) Hadith of Aisha on menstrual blood, (2) Hadith of not dipping hand after sleep, (3) Hadith of dog licking a vessel. Identify the source and key phrase of each.
The numbers (١, ٢, ٣) correspond to the order in the text.
3
Analyze the Aisha hadith
Focus on 'تَغْسِلُهُ فَإِنْ لَمْ يَذْهَبْ أَثَرُهُ فَلْتُغَيَّرَهُ بِشَيْءٍ مِنْ صُفْرَةِ'. How does this prove that the standard is removal of trace, not a fixed number? What does the mention of yellow clay indicate?
The hadith implies that even if a trace remains, it can be treated with a colorant; the goal is to make it imperceptible, not to achieve a precise number of washes.
4
Consider the other hadiths
The hand-washing hadith mentions three washes; the dog hadith also says three times. Do these contradict the principle of ghalabat al-zann? Explain how the Hanafi school reconciles them (e.g., they refer to cases where the impurity is visible or potentially visible, or they are interpreted as recommended numbers, not absolute requirements).
The Urdu summary clarifies the two categories: visible impurity (najasat mar'iyya) requires washing until visible trace is gone; non-visible impurity relies on assumption. The hadiths with specified numbers may fall under visible or specific cases.
5
Understand the cross-madhhab difference
Contrast the Hanafi approach with the Shafi'i school, which often requires a fixed number of washes for certain impurities (e.g., three for dog saliva). How does the Hanafi principle of ghalabat al-zann lead to a different ruling?
The disagreement is rooted in how each school interprets the hadiths: Shafi'is take the number as part of the ruling, Hanafis see it as incidental.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ الْأَنْجَاسِ ١٠ وَمَا لَيْسَ لَهَا عَيْنٌ مَرْتَيَّةٌ فَطَهَارَتُهَا أَنْ تُغْسَلَ حَتَّى يَغْلِبَ عَلَى ظَنِّ الْغَاسِلِ أَنَّهَا قَدْ طَهُرَتْ. وجه : (۳) الحديث لثبوت وَتَطْهِيرُ النَّجَاسَةِ الَّتِي يَجِبُ غَسْلُهَا سَأَلْتُ عَائِشَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهَا عَنِ الخائض يُصِيبُ ثَوْبَهَا الدَّمُ قَالَتْ: «تَغْسِلُهُ فَإِنْ لَمْ يَذْهَبْ أَثَرُهُ فَلْتُغَيَّرَهُ بِشَيْءٍ مِنْ صُفْرَةِ» (سنن ابي داؤد ، بَابُ الْمَرْأَةُ تَغْسِلُ ثَوْبَهَا الَّذِي تَلْبَسُهُ فِي حَيْضِهَا، نمبر 357) 10 وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَمَا لَيْسَ لَهَا عَيْنٌ مَرْتِيَّةٌ فَطَهَارَتُهَا أَنْ تُغْسَلَ \ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ، أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «إِذَا اسْتَيْقَظَ أَحَدُكُمْ مِنْ نَوْمِهِ، فَلَا يَغْمِسْ يَدَهُ فِي الْإِنَاءِ حَتَّى يَغْسِلَهَا ثَلَاثًا، فَإِنَّهُ لَا يَدْرِي أَيْنَ بَاتَتْ يَدُهُ» مسلم شریف ، بَابُ كَرَاهَةِ غَمْسِ الْمُتَوَضِئ وَغَيْرِهِ يَدَهُ الْمَشْكُوكَ في تَجَاسَتِها في الإناءِ قَبْلَ غَسْلِهَا ثَلَاثًا ، غبر (278)
وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَمَا لَيْسَ لَهَا عَيْنٌ مَرْيَيَّةٌ فَطَهَارَتُهَا أَنْ تُغْسَلَ \ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ, قَالَ: «إِذَا وَلَغَ الْكَلْبُ فِي الْإِنَاءِ فَاهْرِقْهُ ثُمَّ اغْسِلْهُ ثَلَاثَ مَرَّاتٍ (سنن الدار قطني ، بَابُ وُلُوعَ الْكَلْبِ في الإناء،نمبر 196/مصنف عبد الرزاق، بَابُ الْكَلْبِ يَلَعُ فِي الْإِنَاءِ، نمبر 336) اصول : : نجاست کی دو قسمیں ہیں انجاست مرئیہ اور نجاست غیر مرئیہ ، غیر مرئیہ کو اتنا دھوئے کہ غالب گمان ہو جائے کہ پاک ہو گیا، اور مرئیہ جب تک نجاست نظر آرہی ہے تو اس کو دھوئیں۔
Chapter of Impurities. And that which has no visible substance, its purification is to wash it until the washer's dominant assumption overcomes that it has become pure. Proof (3): The hadith for proof of 'and purifying the impurity which must be washed': I asked Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) about a menstruating woman whose garment is stained with blood. She said: 'Wash it, and if its trace does not go, then change it with something of yellowness.' (Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter of the woman washing her garment which she wears during her menses, no. 357) 10 Proof (1): The hadith for proof of 'and that which has no visible substance, its purification is to wash it': From Abu Hurairah that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'When one of you wakes from sleep, he should not dip his hand into the vessel until he washes it three times, for he does not know where his hand spent the night.' (Muslim, chapter of dislike of the person performing wudu or others dipping his hand whose impurity is doubtful into the vessel before washing it three times, no. 278) Proof (2): The hadith for proof of 'and that which has no visible substance, its purification is to wash it': From Abu Hurairah, he said: 'When a dog drinks from a vessel, pour it out and then wash it three times.' (Sunan al-Daraqutni, chapter of a dog drinking from a vessel, no. 196; Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, chapter of the dog drinking from the vessel, no. 336) Principles: There are two types of impurity: visible impurity and non-visible impurity. For non-visible, wash until dominant assumption overcomes that it has become pure. For visible, as long as the impurity is visible, wash it.
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage from al-Quduri states the ruling for impurities that have no visible substance (e.g., invisible traces of urine or blood). The ruling is that such impurities are purified by washing until the washer is reasonably certain (ghalabat al-zann) that the impurity has been removed. The author then cites three hadiths as evidence. The first is the hadith of Aisha regarding menstrual blood, where she instructs to wash until the trace is gone, and if not, to use yellow clay. This indicates that the criterion is the disappearance of the impurity, not a specific number of washes. The second hadith is about washing hands after sleep, which implies that unseen impurity is removed by washing sufficiently. The third is the hadith about a dog licking a vessel, which requires washing three times. The Urdu summary clarifies the two categories: visible impurity (najasat mar'iyya) and non-visible impurity (najasat ghayr mar'iyya). For non-visible, one washes until dominant assumption of cleanliness; for visible, one washes until the impurity is no longer visible. This is a foundational ruling in Hanafi fiqh regarding najasat hukmiyya (legal impurity) versus 'ayniyya (physical impurity).

Key Terms
لَيْسَ لَهَا عَيْنٌ مَرْتَيَّةٌ (laysa laha 'aynun martiyya): Impurity that has no visible substance (color, smell, taste).
يَغْلِبَ عَلَى ظَنِّ الْغَاسِلِ (yaghliba 'ala zann al-ghasil): The washer's dominant assumption (that the impurity is removed).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how should a non-visible impurity (najasat ghayr mar'iyya) be purified?
A) By washing exactly three times.
B) By washing until the impurity is no longer visible.
C) By washing until the washer is confident that it has become pure.
D) By sprinkling water on it.

Key Takeaway
Purification of non-visible impurities is achieved by washing until the washer's dominant assumption (ghalabat al-zann) of cleanliness, without a fixed number of washes.

The Four Rulings of Istinja in Hanafi Fiqh
Rulings on istinja with supporting evidences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four Hanafi rulings on istinja and identify the hadith proofs for each.

Core Idea
Istinja is sunnah, stones suffice, no fixed number, water is better—if impurity spreads, water is necessary.

This section from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar outlines the foundational Hanafi rulings on cleansing after relieving oneself. The text presents these rulings concisely, followed by several prophetic hadith and a companion statement that serve as evidence. Understanding these rulings is essential for daily practice and for recognizing the Hanafi approach to taharah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rulings
List the four distinct rulings stated in the matn: 1) Istinja is sunnah, 2) Stones or their substitutes suffice, 3) There is no fixed prescribed number of stones, 4) Washing with water is better, but if the impurity spreads beyond the exit, nothing except water suffices.
These are all explicitly stated in the first few lines.
2
Locate the proofs
For each ruling, find the corresponding hadith or saying cited in the text: ruling 1 & 2 from hadith of Aisha; ruling 3 from hadith of Salman; ruling 4 from hadith of Anas and saying of Ali.
The text labels proofs as وجه (1), وجه (2), etc.
3
Analyse the dalala
Explain how each proof supports the ruling. For example, the command in the hadith of Aisha (فَلْيَذْهَبْ) indicates recommendation (sunnah) in Hanafi usul. The phrase تُجْزِئُ عَنْهُ shows stones suffice. The prohibition of less than three stones implies minimum, not a fixed number.
The Hanafi principle: amr for acts of worship indicates sunnah unless evidence of obligation.
4
Note the exception
Identify the condition that changes the ruling: if impurity exceeds the exit (e.g., reaches thighs), water becomes necessary (wajib/necessary).
The text says فَإِنْ تَجَاوَزَتْ النَّجَاسَةُ مَخْرَجَهَا لَمْ يَجْزْ فِيهِ إِلَّا الْمَاءُ.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الِاسْتِنْجَاءِ
وَالِاسْتِنْجَاءُ سُنَّةٌ يُجْزِئُ فِيهِ الْحَجَرُ وَمَا قَامَ مَقَامَهُ يَمْسَحُهُ حَتَّى يُنْقِيَهُ لَ وَلَيْسَ فِيهِ عَدَدٌ مَسْئُونٌ ٣ وَغَسْلُهُ بِالْمَاءِ أَفْضَلُ : فَإِنْ تَجَاوَزَتْ النَّجَاسَةُ مَخْرَجَهَا لَمْ يَجْزْ فِيهِ إِلَّا الْمَاءُ. وجه (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَالِاسْتِنْجَاءُ سُنَّةٌ يُجْزِئُ فِيهِ الْحَجَرُ \ عَنْ عَائِشَةَ، أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «إِذَا ذَهَبَ أَحَدُكُمْ إِلَى الْغَائِطِ، فَلْيَذْهَبْ مَعَهُ بِثَلَاثَةِ أَحْجَارٍ يَسْتَطِيبُ بِهِنَّ، فَإِنَّهَا تُجْزِئُ عَنْهُ» (سنن ابي داؤد ، بَابُ الِاسْتِنْجَاءِ بِالْحِجَارَةِ، نمبر (40)
وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَالِاسْتِنْجَاءُ سُنَّةٌ يُجْزِئُ فِيهِ الْحَجَرُ \ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ .... وَمَنْ اسْتَجْمَرَ فَلْيُوتِرُ ، مَنْ فَعَلَ فَقَدْ أَحْسَنَ وَمَنْ لَا فَلَا خَرَجَ (سنن ابي داؤد ، باب الاستتار في الخلاء، غمبر (35)
وجه: (ا) الحديث لثبوت وَلَيْسَ فِيهِ عَدَدٌ مَسْنُونٌ \ عَنْ سَلْمَانَ، قَالَ: قِيلَ لَهُ: قَدْ عَلَّمَكُمْ نَبِيُّكُمْ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ كُلَّ شَيْءٍ حَتَّى الْخِرَاءَةَ قَالَ: فَقَالَ: أَجَلْ «لَقَدْ نَهَانَا أَنْ نَسْتَقْبِلَ الْقِبْلَةَ لِغَائِطِ، أَوْ بَوْلٍ، أَوْ أَنْ نَسْتَنْجِيَ بِالْيَمِينِ، أَوْ أَنْ نَسْتَنجِيَ بِأَقَلَّ مِنْ ثَلَاثَةِ أَحْجَارٍ، أَوْ أَنْ نَسْتَلْجِيَ بِرَجِيعِ أَوْ بِعَظْمٍ» (مسلم شريف، بَابُ الاسْتِطَابَةِ، نمبر 262) وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَلَيْسَ فِيهِ عَدَدٌ مَسْئُونٌ \ (قَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ) : فَمَنْ تَخَلَّى أَوْ بَالَ لَمْ يُجْزِهِ إِلَّا أَنْ يَتَمَسَّحَ بِثَلَاثَةِ أَحْجَارٍ ثَلَاثَ مَرَّاتٍ الام) للشافعي، بَابٌ فِي الِاسْتِنْجَاءِ)
وجه (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَغَسْلُهُ بِالْمَاءِ أَفْضَلُ \ سَمِعْتُ أَنَسَ بْنَ مَالِكٍ، يَقُولُ كَانَ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ «إِذَا خَرَجَ لِحَاجَتِهِ، أَجِيءُ أَنَا وَغُلامٌ، مَعَنَا إدَاوَةٌ مِنْ مَاءٍ، يَعْنِي يَسْتَنْجِي بِهِ» (بخاري شريف، بَابُ الِاسْتِنْجَاءِ بِالْمَاءِ، نمبر 150/)
وجه (۱) قول الصحابى لثبوت فَإِنْ تَجَاوَزَتْ النَّجَاسَةُ فَخَرَجَهَا لَمَّ يَجُزْ فِيهِ إِلَّا الْمَاءُ \ قَالَ عَلِيٌّ بْنُ أَبِي طَالِبِ : " إِنَّهُمْ كَانُوا يَبْعَرُونَ بَعْرًا، وَأَنْتُمْ تُخْلِطُونَ ثَلْطَا، فَاتَّبِعُوا الْحِجَارَةَ الْمَاءَ "(سنن الكبري للبيهقي، بَابُ الجمع في الِاسْتِنْجَاءِ بَيْنَ الْمَسْحُ بِالأَحْجَارِ وَالْغَسْلِ بِالْمَاءِ، غير 517) اصول : استنجاء سے متعلق تین بنیادی باتیں : ۱ استنجاء سنت ہے، ۲ پتھر یا اس کے قائم مقام شی سے استنجاء ہو سکتا ہے، ۱۳ تنی دفعہ پونچھنا جس سے پاکی حاصل ہو جائے۔
Section on Istinja. Istinja is a sunnah. Stone and what stands in its place suffice for it; he wipes until it cleans him. And there is no fixed prescribed number for it. And washing with water is better. Then if the impurity exceeds its exit, nothing suffices except water. Proof (1): The hadith for proof of 'istinja is a sunnah, stone suffices': From Aisha that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'When one of you goes to defecate, let him take with him three stones to clean himself with, for they suffice for him.' (Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter of istinja with stones, no. 40) Proof (2): The hadith for proof of 'istinja is a sunnah, stone suffices': From Abu Hurairah from the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: '...And whoever uses stones (istijmar) let him use an odd number. Whoever does so has done well, and whoever does not, there is no harm.' (Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter of concealment in the toilet, no. 35) Proof (1): The hadith for proof of 'there is no fixed prescribed number': From Salman, he said: It was said to him: Your Prophet has taught you everything, even how to relieve yourself. He said: Yes. 'He forbade us from facing the qibla while defecating or urinating, or to clean ourselves with the right hand, or to clean ourselves with less than three stones, or to clean ourselves with dung or bone.' (Muslim, chapter of istitaba, no. 262) Proof (2): The hadith for proof of 'there is no fixed prescribed number': Al-Shafi'i said: 'Whoever relieves himself or urinates, it does not suffice unless he wipes with three stones three times.' (Al-Umm for al-Shafi'i, chapter on istinja) Proof (1): The hadith for proof of 'washing with water is better': I heard Anas ibn Malik say: The Prophet (peace be upon him) when he went to relieve himself, I and a boy would come with a small container of water, meaning he would clean himself with it. (Sahih al-Bukhari, chapter of istinja with water, no. 150) Proof (1): The saying of the Companion for proof of 'if the impurity exceeds its exit, nothing suffices except water': Ali ibn Abi Talib said: 'They used to pass solid droppings, but you mix soft droppings, so follow the stones with water.' (Sunan al-Kubra lil-Bayhaqi, chapter of combining in istinja between wiping with stones and washing with water, no. 517) Principles: Three basic points regarding istinja: 1. Istinja is sunnah. 2. Stone or its substitute can be used for istinja. 3. Wipe until cleanliness is achieved.
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This section from al-Quduri presents the Hanafi rulings on istinja (cleansing after using the toilet). The author states four rulings: (1) Istinja is sunnah (recommended, not obligatory). (2) Stones or any dry, absorbent material suffice. (3) There is no fixed number of stones required—one wipes until clean. (4) Washing with water is better. However, if the impurity spreads beyond the exit (e.g., onto the thighs), then water is necessary. The proofs cited include hadith from Aisha about taking three stones, from Abu Hurairah about odd numbers being recommended but not required, from Salman forbidding less than three stones (indicating minimum, but not that exactly three is compulsory), and from Anas about the Prophet using water. The author also includes a quote from Imam al-Shafi'i, who holds that one must wipe three times with three stones (each stone once). The Hanafi response is implied: the hadith of Salman only forbids less than three, not that three is mandatory three times. The Urdu summary reiterates the three basics: istinja is sunnah, stones suffice, and wiping until clean.

Key Terms
الِاسْتِنْجَاءُ (al-istinja): Cleansing the private parts after urination or defecation.
سُنَّةٌ (sunnah): Recommended, not obligatory. The text explicitly states istinja is sunnah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on istinja (cleansing after using the toilet)?
A) It is obligatory (wajib).
B) It is a sunnah (recommended).
C) It is mubah (permitted).
D) It is haram if not done.

Key Takeaway
Istinja is a recommended sunnah in Hanafi fiqh, and the goal is cleanliness, not a ritual number of wipes.

7 min
The Hanafi-Shafi'i Disagreement on the Number of Stones for Istinja
Disagreement on the method of istinja

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on the required number of stones for istinja and evaluate the Hanafi rebuttal.

Core Idea
Hanafis require only cleanliness, not a ritual three-times wiping; Shafi'is insist on three separate wipes.

The source text presents a disagreement between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the number of stones needed for istinja. While both schools agree that fewer than three stones is insufficient, they differ on whether three stones must be used three times. This lesson unpacks that dispute and the underlying evidence.

Guided Path
1
State the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i is quoted as saying: 'Whoever relieves himself or urinates, it does not suffice unless he wipes with three stones three times.' This means wiping three separate times, each time with a stone.
The text labels this as Proof (2) for 'no fixed number', but it is actually the opponent's view.
2
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that there is no fixed prescribed number; one wipes until clean. The minimum is three wipes if using stones, but not three separate stones each used three times.
The matn says: 'وَلَيْسَ فِيهِ عَدَدٌ مَسْنُونٌ' (there is no fixed prescribed number).
3
Identify the proofs
Shafi'i may rely on the outward command of the hadith of Aisha (take three stones). Hanafi relies on the hadith of Salman, which only forbids using less than three stones, not three times.
The Hanafi proof is the hadith of Salman (Muslim). The Shafi'i proof is not explicitly cited in this text but is referenced by his statement.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that the prohibition (نهى) of less than three indicates a minimum, not a mandate for three separate wipes. The command is understood as a recommendation.
The Hanafi principle: نهى for something indicates prohibition of that specific thing; it does not create a positive obligation to do the opposite in a specific manner.
5
Determine the thamarah
The practical difference: A Hanafi may achieve cleanliness with one wipe using multiple stones (or one stone wiped multiple times in one stroke), while a Shafi'i requires three distinct wiping actions.
This affects daily practice, especially when using toilet paper.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الِاسْتِنْجَاءِ
وَالِاسْتِنْجَاءُ سُنَّةٌ يُجْزِئُ فِيهِ الْحَجَرُ وَمَا قَامَ مَقَامَهُ يَمْسَحُهُ حَتَّى يُنْقِيَهُ لَ وَلَيْسَ فِيهِ عَدَدٌ مَسْئُونٌ ٣ وَغَسْلُهُ بِالْمَاءِ أَفْضَلُ : فَإِنْ تَجَاوَزَتْ النَّجَاسَةُ مَخْرَجَهَا لَمْ يَجْزْ فِيهِ إِلَّا الْمَاءُ. وجه (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَالِاسْتِنْجَاءُ سُنَّةٌ يُجْزِئُ فِيهِ الْحَجَرُ \ عَنْ عَائِشَةَ، أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «إِذَا ذَهَبَ أَحَدُكُمْ إِلَى الْغَائِطِ، فَلْيَذْهَبْ مَعَهُ بِثَلَاثَةِ أَحْجَارٍ يَسْتَطِيبُ بِهِنَّ، فَإِنَّهَا تُجْزِئُ عَنْهُ» (سنن ابي داؤد ، بَابُ الِاسْتِنْجَاءِ بِالْحِجَارَةِ، نمبر (40)

Istinja': Sunnah, Stones, and the Shafi'i Dispute on Number
Text of Al-Quduri on istinja' with hadith proofs and a Shafi'i dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on istinja' (sunnah muakkadah), identify the evidences, and explain the dispute with the Shafi'i school regarding the number of stones.

Core Idea
Istinja' is sunnah, not wajib; cleanliness matters, not a fixed number of stones.

In this passage from Al-Quduri, we encounter the Hanafi position on istinja' (cleansing after relieving oneself). The text establishes that istinja' is sunnah muakkadah, that stones suffice, and that there is no fixed number – cleanliness is the condition. The author then cites hadith proofs and contrasts with Imam al-Shafi'i's view that three stones must be used three times. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the evidence, and the practical consequence of the khilaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its level
State the hukm of istinja' according to the Hanafi school. Note that it is sunnah muakkadah, not fard or wajib.
The primary obligation is removal of najis; istinja' is the recommended method.
2
Examine the sufficiency of stones
Understand that any dry, absorbent substance (like stones) suffices for istinja' as long as the impurity has not spread beyond the exit. If it spreads, water is required.
The text says 'stone and what stands in its place suffices'.
3
Analyze the dispute on number of stones
Compare the Hanafi position (no fixed number, cleanliness is key) with the Shafi'i position (three stones three times are obligatory). Identify the key hadith used by each side.
Abu Huraira's hadith explicitly says 'whoever does not is not sinful', supporting the Hanafi view.
4
List prohibited items for istinja'
Identify what cannot be used: bone, dung, excrement, food, and the right hand. Understand the reasoning: bones and dung are food for jinn, the right hand is for honorable acts.
These are forbidden because they are either impure, disrespectful, or ineffective.
5
Synthesize the Hanafi proof
Combine the hadith evidence to support the Hanafi position that istinja' is sunnah and that three stones are recommended but not required. Note the role of istihsan in preferring leniency.
The text uses multiple ahadith to establish the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الِاسْتِنْجَاءِ وَالِاسْتِنْجَاءُ سُنَّةٌ يُجْزِئُ فِيهِ الْحَجَرُ وَمَا قَامَ مَقَامَهُ يَمْسَحُهُ حَتَّى يُنْقِيَهُ وَلَيْسَ فِيهِ عَدَدٌ مَسْئُونٌ وَغَسْلُهُ بِالْمَاءِ أَفْضَلُ : فَإِنْ تَجَاوَزَتْ النَّجَاسَةُ مَخْرَجَهَا لَمْ يَجْزْ فِيهِ إِلَّا الْمَاءُ. وَعَنْ عَائِشَةَ أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «إِذَا ذَهَبَ أَحَدُكُمْ إِلَى الْغَائِطِ فَلْيَذْهَبْ مَعَهُ بِثَلَاثَةِ أَحْجَارٍ يَسْتَطِيبُ بِهِنَّ فَإِنَّهَا تُجْزِئُ عَنْهُ» (سنن أبي داود، باب الاستنجاء بالحجارة، رقم 40) وَعَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «...وَمَنْ اسْتَجْمَرَ فَلْيُوتِرْ، مَنْ فَعَلَ فَقَدْ أَحْسَنَ وَمَنْ لَا فَلَا حَرَجَ» (سنن أبي داود، باب الاستتار في الخلاء، رقم 35) وَعَنْ سَلْمَانَ قَالَ: قِيلَ لَهُ: قَدْ عَلَّمَكُمْ نَبِيُّكُمْ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ كُلَّ شَيْءٍ حَتَّى الْخِرَاءَةَ قَالَ: فَقَالَ: أَجَلْ «لَقَدْ نَهَانَا أَنْ نَسْتَقْبِلَ الْقِبْلَةَ لِغَائِطٍ أَوْ بَوْلٍ أَوْ أَنْ نَسْتَنْجِيَ بِالْيَمِينِ أَوْ أَنْ نَسْتَنْجِيَ بِأَقَلَّ مِنْ ثَلَاثَةِ أَحْجَارٍ أَوْ أَنْ نَسْتَنْجِيَ بِرَجِيعٍ أَوْ بِعَظْمٍ» (مسلم، باب الاستطابة، رقم 262) قَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ: فَمَنْ تَخَلَّى أَوْ بَالَ لَمْ يُجْزِهِ إِلَّا أَنْ يَتَمَسَّحَ بِثَلَاثَةِ أَحْجَارٍ ثَلَاثَ مَرَّاتٍ (الأم للشافعي، باب في الاستنجاء) وَسَمِعْتُ أَنَسَ بْنَ مَالِكٍ يَقُولُ: كَانَ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ «إِذَا خَرَجَ لِحَاجَتِهِ أَجِيءُ أَنَا وَغُلَامٌ مَعَنَا إِدَاوَةٌ مِنْ مَاءٍ يَعْنِي يَسْتَنْجِي بِهِ» (البخاري، باب الاستنجاء بالماء، رقم 150) وَقَالَ عَلِيُّ بْنُ أَبِي طَالِبٍ: «إِنَّهُمْ كَانُوا يَبْعَرُونَ بَعْرًا وَأَنْتُمْ تُخْلِطُونَ ثَلْطًا فَاتَّبِعُوا الْحِجَارَةَ الْمَاءَ» (السنن الكبرى للبيهقي، باب الجمع في الاستنجاء بين المسح بالأحجار والغسل بالماء، رقم 517) وَلَا يَسْتَنْجِي بِعَظْمٍ وَلَا بِرَوْثٍ وَلَا بِرَجِيعٍ وَلَا بِطَعَامٍ وَلَا بِيَمِينِهِ. وَعَنْ سَلْمَانَ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ نَهَى أَنْ نَسْتَنْجِيَ بِالْيَمِينِ أَوْ بِرَجِيعٍ أَوْ بِعَظْمٍ (مسلم، رقم 262) وَعَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ مَسْعُودٍ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «لَا تَسْتَنْجُوا بِالرَّوْثِ وَلَا بِالْعِظَامِ فَإِنَّهُ زَادُ إِخْوَانِكُمْ مِنَ الْجِنِّ» (الترمذي، باب كراهية ما يستنجى به، رقم 18) وَعَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ قَالَ: اتَّبَعْتُ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فَقَالَ: «ابْغِنِي أَحْجَارًا وَلَا تَأْتِنِي بِعَظْمٍ وَلَا رَوْثٍ» (البخاري، باب الاستنجاء بالحجارة، رقم 155) وَعَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ قَالَ: أَتَى النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ الْغَائِطَ فَأَمَرَنِي أَنْ آتِيَهُ بِثَلَاثَةِ أَحْجَارٍ فَوَجَدْتُ حَجَرَيْنِ وَالْتَمَسْتُ الثَّالِثَ فَلَمْ أَجِدْهُ فَأَخَذْتُ رَوْثَةً فَأَتَيْتُهُ بِهَا فَأَخَذَ الْحَجَرَيْنِ وَأَلْقَى الرَّوْثَةَ وَقَالَ: «هَذَا رِكْسٌ» (البخاري، باب لا يستنجى بروث، رقم 156)
Chapter on Istinja'. Istinja' is sunnah. Stone and what stands in its place suffices in it. He wipes it until he cleans it. There is no prescribed number in it. Washing it with water is better. If the impurity exceeds its exit, nothing suffices in it except water. From Aisha that the Messenger of Allah said: 'When one of you goes to relieve himself, let him take with him three stones and cleanse himself with them, for indeed they suffice him.' From Abu Huraira from the Prophet: 'Whoever uses stones for istijmar let him make it odd; whoever does so has done well and whoever does not is not sinful.' From Salman: 'He forbade us from facing the qibla for stool or urine, from wiping with the right hand, from wiping with less than three stones, and from wiping with dung or bone.' Al-Shafi'i said: 'Whoever relieves himself or urinates, nothing suffices him except to wipe with three stones three times.' I heard Anas bin Malik say: 'The Prophet when he went to relieve himself, I and a young boy would come with a small water vessel, meaning he would wash with it.' Ali bin Abi Talib said: 'They used to defecate dry stool while you produce soft stool, so follow the stones with water.' And he should not wipe with bone, nor with dung, nor with excrement, nor with food, nor with his right hand. From Salman from the Prophet forbidding wiping with the right hand or with dung or bone. From Abdullah bin Mas'ud: 'Do not wipe with dung or bones for indeed it is the provision of your brothers among the jinn.' From Abu Huraira: 'Bring me stones and do not bring me bone or dung.' From Abdullah: 'The Prophet came to relieve himself and ordered me to bring him three stones; I found two stones and sought the third but did not find it, so I took a dung and brought it; he took the two stones and threw away the dung saying: This is filthy.'
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage from Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar presents the rulings of istinja' (cleansing after answering the call of nature). The author begins by stating that istinja' is a sunnah (recommended, not obligatory). He then clarifies that dry stones or any similarly dry, absorbent, non-respected substance suffice for cleansing, provided the impurity has not spread beyond the exit. The user wipes until the area is clean, and there is no fixed number of stones prescribed; rather, the goal is cleanliness. However, washing with water is superior. If the impurity exceeds the area of the exit (i.e., spreads to the surrounding skin), then only water is sufficient; stones alone will not purify. The text then provides hadith proofs: Aisha's hadith mentions three stones, but that is recommended, not obligatory, as the Salman hadith forbids using less than three, but the Abu Huraira hadith allows odd numbers with leniency. Importantly, the author quotes Imam al-Shafi'i's position that one must wipe exactly three times with three stones; the Hanafi school disagrees, holding that cleanliness is what matters, and any number achieving that suffices. This is based on the principle of istihsan. The passage then lists prohibited items for istinja': bones, dung, dried excrement (rajee'), food, and the right hand. Evidence includes the hadith that bones and dung are food for jinn, and the right hand is reserved for honorable acts. The author concludes with the principle: anything that defeats the purpose of cleansing is prohibited, and the purpose is removal of impurity.

Key Terms
اسْتِنْجَاء (istinja'): Cleansing the private parts after answering the call of nature, using water, stones, or similar substances.
سُنَّة (sunnah): Recommended act; not obligatory but rewarded, and omission without excuse is disliked.
حَجَر (hajar (pl. ahjar)): A stone used for wiping after toilet; any clean, dry, absorbent substance that removes impurity without causing harm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on using exactly three stones for istinja'?
A) Obligatory
B) Sunnah, but not required
C) Haram
D) Valid only if three stones are used

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules istinja' as sunnah muakkadah; stones suffice without a fixed number, and the Shafi'i requirement of three stones three times is not binding in the Hanafi school.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
12 min
Conditions of Prayer: Purification and Covering the Awrah
Conditions of prayer with proofs and definitions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions of prayer from this passage, identify the proofs for each, and explain the Hanafi definition of 'awrah and the dispute regarding the knee.

Core Idea
The validity of prayer depends on purification and covering the 'awrah; the man's 'awrah includes the knee.

This lesson examines the foundational conditions that must be fulfilled before prayer can begin. Using Quranic verses and authentic hadiths, the Hanafi school establishes that purification from ritual and physical impurities, and covering the 'awrah are individual obligations. We will also delve into the precise definition of 'awrah for men and free women, and address the well-known difference with the Shafi'i school regarding the inclusion of the knee.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conditions
State the two preconditions for the validity of prayer mentioned: purification (taharah) from hadath and najas, and covering the 'awrah.
These are shurut (conditions) performed before prayer, not arkan (pillars) within it.
2
Locate the proofs
Find the Quranic verses and hadiths cited: for purification, Surah al-Ma'idah 5:6 and Surah al-Muddaththir 74:4; for covering, Surah al-A'raf 7:31 and the hadith 'the prayer of a menstruating woman is not accepted except with a headcover'.
Also note the hadith listing five impurities requiring washing.
3
Understand shurut vs arkan
Read the Urdu principle: obligations before prayer are shurut (conditions), those during prayer are arkan (pillars). This distinction is crucial for fiqh analysis.
Conditions must be present before starting; pillars are integral to the act.
4
Define the 'awrah
State the Hanafi definitions: for a man, from below the navel to the knee including the knee; for a free woman, the entire body except the face and hands.
The knee is explicitly included via the hadith 'al-rukbatu min al-'awrah'.
5
Analyze the dispute over the knee
Examine al-Shafi'i's view that the navel and knee are not 'awrah. Identify the Hanafi response using the explicit hadith and the phrasing 'above the knee' to prove inclusion.
Practical consequence: praying with knees exposed invalidates the prayer in the Hanafi school but not in the Shafi'i school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ شُرُوطِ الصَّلَاةِ
yَجِبُ عَلَى الْمُصَلِّي أَنْ يُقَدِّمَ الطَّهَارَةَ مِنْ الْأَحْدَاثِ وَالْأَنْجَاسِ عَلَى مَا قَدَّمْنَاهُ. وَيَسْتُرُ عَوْرَتَهُ.

وَجْه (1) الْآيَةَ لِثُبُوتِ يَجِبُ عَلَى الْمُصَلِّي أَنْ يُقَدِّمَ الطَّهَارَةَ مِنَ الْأَحْدَاثِ: ﴿يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا إِذَا قُمْتُمْ إِلَى الصَّلَاةِ فَاغْسِلُوا وُجُوهَكُمْ وَأَيْدِيَكُمْ إِلَى الْمَرَافِقِ وَامْسَحُوا بِرُءُوسِكُمْ وَأَرْجُلَكُمْ إِلَى الْكَعْبَيْنِ﴾ (سورة المائدة، آية 6)
وَجْه (2) الْآيَةَ لِثُبُوتِ الطَّهَارَةِ مِنَ الْأَحْدَاثِ: ﴿وَإِنْ كُنْتُمْ جُنُبًا فَاطَّهَّرُوا وَإِنْ كُنْتُمْ مَرْضَى أَوْ عَلَى سَفَرٍ أَوْ جَاءَ أَحَدٌ مِنْكُمْ مِنَ الْغَائِطِ أَوْ لَامَسْتُمُ النِّسَاءَ فَلَمْ تَجِدُوا مَاءً فَتَيَمَّمُوا صَعِيدًا طَيِّبًا فَامْسَحُوا بِوُجُوهِكُمْ وَأَيْدِيكُمْ مِنْهُ﴾ (سورة المائدة، آية 6)
وَجْه (3) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ يَجِبُ عَلَى الْمُصَلِّي أَنْ يُقَدِّمَ الطَّهَارَةَ مِنَ الْأَحْدَاثِ: ﴿وَثِيَابَكَ فَطَهِّرْ﴾ (سورة المدثر، آية 4)
وَجْه (4) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ الطَّهَارَةِ مِنَ الْأَنْجَاسِ: يَا عَمَّارُ إِنَّمَا يُغْسَلُ الثَّوْبُ مِنْ خَمْسٍ: مِنَ الْغَائِطِ وَالْبَوْلِ وَالْقَيْءِ وَالدَّمِ وَالْمَنِيِّ، يَا عَمَّارُ مَا بَصَقَتُكَ وَدُمُوعُ عَيْنَيْكَ وَالْمَاءُ الَّذِي فِي رَكْوَتِكَ إِلَّا سَوَاءٌ (سُنَنُ الدَّارَقُطْنِيِّ، بَابُ تَجَاسَةِ الْبَوْلِ وَالْأَمْرِ بِالتَّنَزُّهِ مِنْهُ، رقم 458)

وَجْه (1) الْآيَةَ لِثُبُوتِ وَيَسْتُرُ عَوْرَتَهُ: ﴿يَا بَنِي آدَمَ خُذُوا زِينَتَكُمْ عِنْدَ كُلِّ مَسْجِدٍ﴾ (سورة الأعراف، آية 31)
وَجْه (2) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَيَسْتُرُ عَوْرَتَهُ: عَنْ عَائِشَةَ قَالَتْ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «لَا تُقْبَلُ صَلَاةُ الْحَائِضِ إِلَّا بِخِمَارٍ» (سُنَنُ التِّرْمِذِيِّ، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ لَا تُقْبَلُ صَلَاةُ الْحَائِضِ إِلَّا بِخِمَارٍ، رقم 377؛ سُنَنُ أَبِي دَاوُدَ، بَابُ الْمَرْأَةِ تُصَلِّي بِغَيْرِ خِمَارٍ، رقم 641)

أُصُولٌ: جَوْ فَرَائِضِ نَمَازٍ سَيْ پَہْلے اَدَا كِئے جَائیں اُسے شَرَائِطٌ اور جَو نَمَازٍ كے انْدَرْ لَازِم ہیں انْہیں اَرْكَانْ كَہْتے ہیں۔

وَالْعَوْرَةُ مِنَ الرَّجُلِ مَا تَحْتَ السُّرَّةِ إِلَى الرَّكْبَةِ وَالرَّكْبَةُ مِنَ الْعَوْرَةِ، وَبَدَنُ الْمَرْأَةِ الْحُرَّةِ كُلُّهُ عَوْرَةٌ إِلَّا وَجْهَهَا وَكَفَّيْهَا.

وَجْه (1) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَالْعَوْرَةُ مِنَ الرَّجُلِ مَا تَحْتَ السُّرَّةِ إِلَى الرَّكْبَةِ: سَمِعْتُ عَلِيًّا رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ يَقُولُ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «الرَّكْبَةُ مِنَ الْعَوْرَةِ» (سُنَنُ الدَّارَقُطْنِيِّ، بَابُ الْأَمْرِ بِتَعْلِيمِ الصَّلَوَاتِ وَالضَّرْبِ عَلَيْهَا وَحَدِّ الْعَوْرَةِ الَّتِي يَجِبُ سَتْرُهَا، رقم 889)
وَجْه (2) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ ذَلِكَ: عَنْ عَمْرِو بْنِ شُعَيْبٍ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ، عَنْ جَدِّهِ، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «مُرُوا أَوْلَادَكُمْ بِالصَّلَاةِ وَهُمْ أَبْنَاءُ سَبْعِ سِنِينَ، وَاضْرِبُوهُمْ عَلَيْهَا وَهُمْ أَبْنَاءُ عَشْرٍ، وَفَرِّقُوا بَيْنَهُمْ فِي الْمَضَاجِعِ». حَدَّثَنِي دَاوُدُ بْنُ سَوَّارٍ الْمُزَنِيُّ بِإِسْنَادِهِ وَمَعْنَاهُ وَزَادَ: «وَإِذَا زَوَّجَ أَحَدُكُمْ خَادِمَهُ عَبْدَهُ أَوْ أَجِيرَهُ فَلَا يَنْظُرْ إِلَى مَا دُونَ السُّرَّةِ وَفَوْقَ الرُّكْبَةِ» (سُنَنُ أَبِي دَاوُدَ، رقم 496)
وَجْه (1) دَلِيلُ الشَّافِعِيِّ الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ: عَنْ عَمْرِو بْنِ شُعَيْبٍ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ، عَنْ جَدِّهِ، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «فَلَا يَنْظُرُ إِلَى مَا دُونَ السُّرَّةِ وَفَوْقَ الرُّكْبَةِ، فَإِنَّ مَا تَحْتَ السُّرَّةِ إِلَى الرَّكْبَةِ مِنَ الْعَوْرَةِ» (سُنَنُ الدَّارَقُطْنِيِّ، رقم 887)
وَجْه (2) قَوْلُ التَّابِعِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ ذَلِكَ: قَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ: وَعَوْرَةُ الرَّجُلِ مَا دُونَ سُرَّتِهِ إِلَى رُكْبَتَيْهِ، لَيْسَتْ سُرَّتُهُ وَلَا رُكْبَتَاهُ مِنْ عَوْرَتِهِ (كِتَابُ الْأُمِّ، بَابُ كَيْفَ لُبْسُ الثِّيَابِ فِي الصَّلَاةِ)

وَجْه (1) الْآيَةَ لِثُبُوتِ وَبَدَنُ الْمَرْأَةِ الْحُرَّةِ كُلُّهُ عَوْرَةٌ إِلَّا وَجْهَهَا وَكَفَّيْهَا: ﴿وَلَا يُبْدِينَ زِينَتَهُنَّ إِلَّا مَا ظَهَرَ مِنْهَا﴾ (سورة النور، آية 31)
وَجْه (2) قَوْلُ الصَّحَابِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ ذَلِكَ: عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ فِي قَوْلِهِ: ﴿وَلَا يُبْدِينَ زِينَتَهُنَّ إِلَّا مَا ظَهَرَ مِنْهَا﴾ قَالَ: الْكُحْلُ وَالْخَاتَمُ (سُنَنُ الْبَيْهَقِيِّ، بَابُ عَوْرَةِ الْمَرْأَةِ الْحُرَّةِ، رقم 3216)

أُصُولٌ: نَمَازٍ كے لِئے اِتْنَا كَپْڑَا پَہَنْنَا ضَرُورِي ہے جِس سے سَتْرْ ڈھَكْ جائے۔
Chapter of the conditions of prayer. It is obligatory upon the one praying to perform purification from hadath (ritual impurities) and najas (filth) as we have presented, and to cover his/her 'awrah. Proof (1) the verse for establishing that the one praying must perform purification from hadath: [5:6]... Proof (2) the verse... Proof (3) the hadith... [74:4]... Proof (4) the hadith... [hadith about washing the garment from five things]. Proof (1) the verse for covering 'awrah: [7:31]. Proof (2) the hadith: 'The prayer of a menstruating woman is not accepted except with a headcover.' Principle: Obligations performed before prayer are called conditions, and those within prayer are called pillars. The 'awrah of a man is from below the navel to the knee, and the knee is part of the 'awrah. The entire body of a free woman is 'awrah except her face and hands. Proof (1) the hadith: 'The knee is part of the 'awrah.' Proof (2) the hadith: 'Command your children to pray at seven, beat them at ten, separate their beds... and let none look at what is below the navel and above the knee.' Proof (1) al-Shafi'i's proof: the hadith... Proof (2) saying of the follower: al-Shafi'i said: 'The 'awrah of a man is what is below his navel to his knees; his navel and knees are not part of his 'awrah.' Proof (1) the verse for the free woman's 'awrah: [24:31]. Proof (2) saying of the Companion: Ibn Abbas said about the verse: 'The kohl and the ring.' Principle: For prayer, it is necessary to wear enough clothing to cover the 'awrah.
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage is from the chapter on the conditions of prayer. It begins by stating two preconditions for the validity of salah: purification from ritual impurity (hadath) and physical impurity (najas), and covering the 'awrah. The author then provides scriptural evidence for each. For purification, he cites verses from Surah al-Ma'idah (5:6) regarding wudu and ghusl, and a hadith listing five substances that require washing. For covering the 'awrah, he cites the general command to take adornment at every mosque (7:31) and the specific hadith that a woman's prayer is not accepted without a headcover. An Urdu note explains the terminology: obligations performed before prayer are 'shurut' (conditions), while those done during prayer are 'arkan' (pillars). Next, the passage defines 'awrah: for a man, from below the navel to the knee (including the knee), and for a free woman, the entire body except the face and hands. Proofs for the man's 'awrah include the hadith 'The knee is part of the 'awrah' and another hadith about not looking below the navel and above the knee. The author also presents al-Shafi'i's view, which agrees that the 'awrah is from navel to knee but does not include the navel and knee themselves. This is a point of difference: the Hanafi school includes the knee as 'awrah, while the Shafi'i school excludes it. For the woman, the verse 'let them not reveal their adornment except what appears' is cited, and Ibn Abbas is reported to have interpreted 'what appears' as the kohl (eyes) and ring (hands), thus face and hands are excluded. An Urdu note concludes that sufficient clothing must be worn to cover the 'awrah.

Key Terms
شُرُوطُ الصَّلَاةِ (shurut al-salah): Obligations that must be fulfilled before entering the prayer, as opposed to arkan (pillars) which are performed during the prayer.
عَوْرَة ('awrah): The part of the body that must be concealed during prayer and in front of non-mahram. For a man: navel to knee including the knee; for a free woman: all except face and hands.
طَهَارَة (taharah): Purification from ritual impurity (hadath) by wudu or ghusl, and from physical impurity (najas) by washing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the 'awrah of a free woman during prayer?
A) The entire body including face and hands
B) The entire body except the face and hands
C) The entire body except the face, hands, and feet
D) Only the private parts

Key Takeaway
Purification and covering the 'awrah are mandatory conditions for valid prayer; the Hanafi school includes the knee in the man's 'awrah, a point of difference with the Shafi'i school.

8 min
Facing the Qibla and When Ijtihad is Allowed
Ruling on facing qibla with exceptions and ijtihad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on facing qibla, identify the exception for fear, and apply the rule that ijtihad suffices when qibla is unclear, with no repetition required if mistaken.

Core Idea
Facing qibla is wajib; if unclear, ijtihad suffices and prayer is valid even if wrong.

Facing the qibla is a key condition for prayer. This passage from Al-Quduri explains the obligation, the exception for fear, and the procedure when direction is unknown. It also resolves a common worry: what if I prayed in the wrong direction? The Hanafi school, citing prophetic practice, confirms the prayer is valid if ijtihad was made.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its conditions
The passage states that facing qibla is wajib (obligatory) for prayer, except when one is in a state of fear (e.g., danger from enemy or predator). Note the exception.
2
Examine the exception for fear
When fearful, one may pray in any direction they are able. This is based on the verse 'And to Allah belongs the east and the west...' (2:115).
Fear must be genuine and immediate.
3
Understand ijtihad for unclear qibla
If the qibla is unclear and no knowledgeable person is available, one must perform ijtihad (effort to determine direction) using signs such as the sun, stars, or landmarks.
Ijtihad is a duty; guesswork without effort is not sufficient.
4
Discover the consequence of error
If after completing the prayer one realizes the direction was wrong, the prayer is valid and no repetition is needed. This is based on the hadith of Jabir. If error is realized during prayer, one should turn to the correct direction and continue.
Turning during prayer is allowed and does not invalidate the prayer.
5
Recognize the proof structure
The passage cites Quran (2:144 for obligation, 2:115 for exception), hadith of Jabir (for validity after error), and incident of change of qibla (for turning during prayer). These are all dalil naqli.
The imperative 'fawalli' in 2:144 indicates obligation per Hanafi usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ شُرُوطِ الصَّلَاةِ وَيَسْتَقْبِلُ الْقِبْلَةَ إِلَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ خَائِفًا فَيُصَلِّيَ إِلَى أَي وِجْهَةٍ قَدَرَ. فَإِنْ اشْتَبَهَتْ عَلَيْهِ الْقِبْلَةُ وَلَيْسَ بِحَضْرَتِهِ مَنْ يَسْأَلُهُ عَنْهَا اجْتَهَدَ وَصَلَّى فَإِنْ عَلِمَ أَنَّهُ أَخْطَاً بَعْدَ مَا صَلَّى فَلَا إِعَادَةَ عَلَيْهِ . وَإِنْ عَلِمَ ذَلِكَ وَهُوَ فِي الصَّلَاةِ اسْتَدَارَ إِلَى الْقِبْلَةِ وَبَنَى عَلَيْهِا ۱۰ وجه : (۱) الآية لثبوت وَيَسْتَقْبِلُ الْقِبْلَةَ إِلَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ خَائِفًا \ ﴿فَوَلِ وَجْهَكَ شَطْرَ الْمَسْجِدِ الْحَرَامِ وَحَيْثُ مَا كُنتُمْ فَوَلُّوا وُجُوهَكُمْ شَطْرَهُ (سورة البقرة آيت نمبر 144) وجه: (٢) الآية لثبوت وَيَسْتَقْبِلُ الْقِبْلَةَ إِلَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ خَائِفًا \ وَلِلَّهِ الْمَشْرِقُ وَالْمَغْرِبُ فَأَيْنَمَا تُوَلُّواْ فَثَمَّ وَجْهُ الله ) ،(سورة البقرة، أيت (115) الوجه: (ا) الحديث لثبوت فَإِنْ اشْتَبَهَتْ عَلَيْهِ الْقِبْلَةُ وَلَيْسَ بِحَضْرَتِهِ \ عَنْ جَابِرٍ قَالَ: " كُنَّا مَعَ رَسُولِ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فِي مَسِيرٍ أَوْ سَرِيَّةٍ فَأَصَابَنَا غَيْمٌ فَتَحَرَّيْنَا، وَاخْتَلَفْنَا فِي الْقِبْلَةِ فَصَلَّى كُلُّ رَجُلٍ مِنَّا عَلَى حِدَةٍ، فَجَعَلَ أَحَدُنَا يَخُطُّ بَيْنَ يَدَيْهِ لِنَعْلَمَ أَمْكِنَتَنَا، فَلَمَّا أَصْبَحْنَا نَظَرْنَاهُ، فَإِذَا نَحْنُ قَدْ صَلَّيْنَا عَلَى غَيْرِ الْقِبْلَةِ " فَذَكَرْنَا ذَلِكَ لِلنَّبِيِّ ، فَقَالَ : " قَدْ أَجْزَأَتْ صَلَاتُكُمْ،(سنن بيهقي، بَابُ الاخْتِلَافِ فِي الْقِبْلَةِ عِنْدَ التَّحَرِي، نمبر 2235/سنن ترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي الرَّجُلِ يُصَلِّي لِغَيْرِ القِبْلَةِ فِي الغَيْمِ، نمبر 345) وجه : (۲) قول التابعى لثبوت فَإِنْ اشْتَبَهَتْ عَلَيْهِ الْقِبْلَةُ وَلَيْسَ بِحَضْرَتِهِ قال: ولو افتتح الصلاة على اجتهاده ثم رأى القبلة في غيره ، كتاب الام للشافعي، استبان الخطأ بعد الاجتهاد،نمبر 115 وجه: (3) الحديث لثبوت فَإِنْ اشْتَبَهَتْ عَلَيْهِ الْقِبْلَةُ وَلَيْسَ بِحَضْرَتِهِ \ عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عُمَرَ قَالَ: بَيْنَا النَّاسُ بِقُبَاءَ فِي صَلَاةِ الصُّبْحِ، إِذْ جَاءَهُمْ آتِ فَقَالَ: إِنَّ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَدْ أُنْزِلَ عَلَيْهِ اللَّيْلَةَ قُرْآنٌ، وَقَدْ أُمِرَ أَنْ يَسْتَقْبِلَ الْكَعْبَةَ، فَاسْتَقْبِلُوهَا، وَكَانَتْ وُجُوهُهُمْ إِلَى الشَّامِ، فَاسْتَدَارُوا إِلَى الْكَعْبَةِ. (بخاري بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي الْقِبْلَةِ ، نمبر 403/ مسلم شريف، بَاب تَحْوِيلِ الْقِبْلَةِ مِنَ الْقُدْسِ إلَى الْكَعْبَةِ، نمبر 526) اصول : شرائط نماز میں سے ایک شرط استقبال قبلہ ہے فول و جک شطر المسجد الحرام کی وجہ سے۔ اصول : اگر قبلہ مشتبہ ہو جائے تو تحری کر کے نماز ادا کرے، پھر اگر نماز کے بعد معلوم ہوا کہ قبلہ درست نہ تھا تب بھی نماز لوٹانے کی ضرورت نہیں۔
Chapter of Conditions of Prayer: He faces the qibla unless he is fearful, then he prays towards whatever direction he can. If the qibla is unclear to him and there is no one present to ask about it, he performs ijtihad and prays. If he knows that he was mistaken after having prayed, then no repetition is required. If he knows that while still in the prayer, he turns towards the qibla and builds upon it. [Proofs:] Face (1): The verse to establish 'He faces the qibla except if fearful'... (Surah al-Baqarah 2:144). Face (2): The verse... (Surah al-Baqarah 2:115). Face (a): The hadith to establish 'If the qibla is unclear to him and there is no one present...' from Jabir... (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Sunan al-Tirmidhi). Face (2): The saying of the Tabi'i... from al-Shafi'i's al-Umm. Face (3): The hadith from Ibn Umar... (Bukhari, Muslim). Principle: One of the conditions of prayer is facing the qibla due to the verse 'Turn your face toward al-Masjid al-Haram.' Principle: If the qibla becomes unclear, one performs tahari and prays, then if it becomes known after prayer that it was incorrect, there is no need to repeat.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Matn of al-Quduri concerning the condition of facing the qibla. The ruling states that facing the qibla is obligatory (wajib) for prayer, except when one is in a state of fear (e.g., danger from enemy or predator), in which case one may pray in any direction they are able. When the qibla is unknown and no knowledgeable person is available, one must perform ijtihad (effort to determine the direction) based on available signs (e.g., sun, stars, landmarks) and pray accordingly. If after completing the prayer one realizes the direction was wrong, the prayer is valid and no repetition is needed—this is based on the hadith of Jabir where the Companions prayed in the wrong direction due to clouds and the Prophet confirmed their prayer. If the error is realized during the prayer, one should turn to the correct direction and continue the prayer from that point, as demonstrated by the incident of the change of qibla from Jerusalem to the Kaaba, where the Companions turned in prayer. The Urdu commentary summarizes these principles, emphasizing tahari (investigation) over blind guesswork.

Key Terms
الاجتهاد (al-ijtihad): Effort to determine the qibla direction when it is unclear, using signs like sun, stars, or landmarks.
التحري (al-tahari): Investigation and estimation to find the correct qibla direction in the absence of clear evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated
B) The prayer is valid and no repetition is needed
C) The prayer is valid only if he was unable to ask anyone
D) The prayer must be repeated only if the error was discovered during the prayer

Key Takeaway
Facing qibla is wajib; if unclear, ijtihad suffices and prayer is valid even if mistaken, per Hanafi school.

Who May Lead and Follow in Congregational Prayer
Rulings on valid and invalid imam–ma'mum pairings with hadith evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on valid and invalid imam–ma'mum pairings in congregational prayer and derive the underlying conditions from the hadith proofs.

Core Idea
The imam is a guarantor; his state must match or exceed the follower's for the prayer to be valid.

In this passage, Al-Quduri lists several prohibitions and permissions regarding who can lead and who can follow in congregational prayer. Each ruling is supported by a hadith, reinforcing that the imam's role demands a certain level of purity, recitation ability, and intention. We will walk through each prohibition, examine its proof, and understand the Hanafi position that such imamates, while valid in terms of prayer validity, are sinful (makruh tahrimi).

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibitions
List the five cases where a pure person cannot follow a deficient imam: (1) pure behind one with incontinence, (2) pure women behind mustahadah, (3) reciter behind illiterate, (4) clothed behind naked, (5) one who bows/prostrates behind one who gestures. Also note two contraindicated pairings: fard behind nafl, and fard behind a different fard.
These are all considered makruh tahrimi; prayer is valid but sinful.
2
Examine the permissions
Note the three allowed pairings: a mutayammim may lead wudu performers, a person who wiped over khuffs may lead those who washed feet, and a standing person may pray behind a sitting imam. Also, a nafl performer may lead a fard performer.
These are permissible despite apparent differences in purity or posture.
3
Locate the hadith proofs
For each ruling, find the hadith cited in the passage. The 'imam is a guarantor' hadith supports the purity-based prohibitions. The hadith of Amr ibn al-As supports the mutayammim leading. The hadiths of Aisha, Ibn Abbas, and Anas support standing behind a sitting imam. The hadith of Mu'adh supports nafl behind fard, and the hadith of Jabir's father supports fard behind nafl only for the nafl performer? Actually the passage uses Mu'adh for fard behind nafl (disallowed) and the hadith of the two men for nafl behind fard (allowed).
Some hadith are cited as 'wajh' (evidence) without full text; the truncation is noted.
4
Derive the underlying conditions
From the prohibitions, infer that for valid imamah, the imam must: (1) be pure (no halat of hadath or najis), (2) be able to recite properly (not ummi), (3) be properly clothed, (4) be capable of actual movements (not just gestures), (5) have the same intention as the follower (both fard or both nafl, or imam fard with ma'mum nafl).
The Hanafi principle 'al-umamā'u dāminūn' (imams are guarantors) implies they must be on a higher or equal level.
5
Apply the rulings to a modern scenario
Consider a person with urinary incontinence who leads a healthy person in prayer. The follower's prayer is valid (sahih) but sinful (makruh tahrimi) because the imam is in a state of continuous impurity. The follower must avoid such imams when possible. Similarly, a person who only gestures due to illness cannot be followed by a healthy person who can bow and prostrate.
This highlights the tension between ritual validity and optimal practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الجَمَاعَة
وَلَا يُصَلِّي الطَّاهِرُ خَلْفَ مَنْ بِهِ سَلَسُ الْبَوْلِ وَلَا الطَّاهِرَاتُ خَلْفَ الْمُسْتَحَاضَةِ وَلَا الْقَارِئُ خَلْفَ الْأُمِّيِّ وَلَا الْمُكْتَسِي خَلْفَ الْعُرْيَانِ ١٢ وَيَجُوزُ أَنْ يَؤُمَ الْمُتَيَمِّمُ الْمُتَوَضِّئِينَ وَالْمَاسِحُ عَلَى الْخُفَّيْنِ الْعَاسِلِينَ ١٥ وَيُصَلِّي الْقَائِمُ خَلْفَ الْقَاعِدِ
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يُصَلِّي الطَّاهِرُ خَلْفَ مَنْ بِهِ سَلَسُ الْبَوْلِ 
عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «الإِمَامُ ضَامِنٌ، وَالْمُؤَذِّنُ مُؤْتَمَنٌ، اللَّهُمَّ أَرْشِدِ الْأَئِمَّةَ، وَاغْفِرْ لِلْمُؤَذِّنِينَ»
وجه (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَيَجُوزُ أَنْ يَؤُمُ الْمُتَيَمِّمُ الْمُتَوَضِّئِينَ 
عَنْ عَمْرِو بْنِ الْعَاصِ قَالَ: احْتَلَمْتُ فِي لَيْلَةٍ بَارِدَةٍ فِي غَزْوَةِ ذَاتِ السُّلَاسِلِ فَأَشْفَقْتُ إِنِ اغْتَسَلْتُ أَنْ أَهْلِكَ فَتَيَمَّمْتُ، ثُمَّ صَلَّيْتُ بِأَصْحَابِي الصُّبْحَ
وَوُجُوهٌ لِحَدِيثِ وَيُصَلِّي الْقَائِمُ خَلْفَ الْقَاعِدِ:
(۱) عَنْ عَائِشَةَ: ... فَلَمَّا رَآهُ أَبُو بَكْرٍ، ذَهَبَ لِيَتَأَخَّرَ، فَأَوْمَا إِلَيْهِ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم بِأَنْ لَا يَتَأَخَّرَ، قَالَ: أَجْلِسَانِي إِلَى جَنْبِهِ. فَأَجْلَسَاهُ إِلَى جَنْبِ أَبِي بَكْرٍ، قَالَ: فَجَعَلَ أَبُو بَكْرٍ يُصَلِّي وَهُوَ يَأْتَمُّ بِصَلَاةِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَالنَّاسُ بِصَلَاةِ أَبِي بَكْرٍ، وَالنَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَاعِدٌ
(۲) عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ: ... وَقَامَ أَبُو بَكْرٍ، وَكَانَ أَبُو بَكْرٍ يَأْتَمُ بِالنَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَالنَّاسُ يَأْتَمُّونَ بِأَبِي بَكْرٍ
(۳) عَنْ أَنَسِ بْنِ مَالِكٍ: أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم رَكِبَ فَرَسًا فَصُرِعَ عَنْهُ، فَجُحِشَ شِقُهُ الْأَيْمَنُ، فَصَلَّى صَلَاةً مِنَ الصَّلَوَاتِ وَهُوَ قَاعِدٌ، فَصَلَّيْنَا وَرَاءَهُ قُعُودًا، فَلَمَّا انْصَرَفَ قَالَ: إِنَّمَا جُعِلَ الْإِمَامُ لِيُؤْتَمَّ بِهِ؛ فَإِذَا صَلَّى قَائِمًا فَصَلُّوا قِيَامًا، فَإِذَا رَكَعَ فَارْكَعُوا، وَإِذَا رَفَعَ فَارْفَعُوا، وَإِذَا قَالَ: سَمِعَ اللهُ لِمَنْ حَمِدَهُ، فَقُولُوا: رَبَّنَا وَلَكَ الْحَمْدُ، وَإِذَا صَلَّى قَائِمًا فَصَلُّوا قِيَامًا، وَإِذَا صَلَّى جَالِسًا فَصَلُّوا جُلُوسًا أَجْمَعُونَ
وَلَا يُصَلِّي الَّذِي يَرْكَعُ وَيَسْجُدُ خَلْفَ الْمُومِي [المُؤْمِي] وَلَا يُصَلِّي الْمُفْتَرِضُ خَلْفَ الْمُتَنَقِّلِ وَلَا مَنْ يُصَلِّي فَرْضًا خَلْفَ مَنْ يُصَلِّي فَرْضًا آخَرَ وَيُصَلِّي الْمُتَنَفِّلُ خَلْفَ الْمُفْتَرِضِ
وجه: (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يُصَلِّي الْمُفْتَرِضُ خَلْفَ الْمُتَنَقِّلِ 
عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ؛ أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: إِنَّمَا الإِمَامُ لِيُؤْتَمَّ بِهِ فَلَا تَخْتَلِفُوا عَلَيْهِ
وجه: (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يُصَلِّي الْمُفْتَرِضُ خَلْفَ الْمُتَنَقِّلِ 
عَنْ جَابِرِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ، أَنَّ مُعَاذَ بْنَ جَبَلٍ كَانَ يُصَلِّي مَعَ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم الْعِشَاءَ، ثُمَّ يَأْتِي قَوْمَهُ فَيُصَلِّي بِهِمْ تِلْكَ الصَّلَاةَ
وجه : (۳) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يُصَلِّي الْمُفْتَرِضُ خَلْفَ الْمُتَنَفِّلِ 
أَنَّ مُعَاذَا كَانَ يُصَلِّي مَعَ النَّبِيِّ الْعِشَاءَ، ثُمَّ يَنْصَرِفُ إِلَى قَوْمِهِ فَيُصَلِّي بِهِمْ، هِيَ لَهُ تَطَوُّعٌ وَلَهُمْ فَرِيضَةٌ
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَيُصَلِّي الْمُتَنَفِّلُ خَلْفَ الْمُفْتَرِضِ 
عَنْ جَابِرِ بْنِ يَزِيدَ بْنِ الْأَسْوَدِ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ، أَنَّهُ صَلَّى مَعَ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَهُوَ غُلَامٌ شَابٌ، فَلَمَّا صَلَّى إِذَا رَجُلَانِ لَمْ يُصَلِّيَا فِي نَاحِيَةِ الْمَسْجِدِ، فَدَعَا بِهِمَا فَجِئَ بِهِمَا تُرْعَدُ فَرَائِصُهُمَا، فَقَالَ: مَا مَنَعَكُمَا أَنْ تُصَلِّيَا مَعَنَا؟ قَالَا: قَدْ صَلَّيْنَا فِي رِحَالِنَا، فَقَالَ: لَا تَفْعَلُوا إِذَا صَلَّى أَحَدُكُمْ فِي رَحْلِهِ ثُمَّ أَدْرَكَ الْإِمَامَ وَلَمْ يُصَلِّ، فَلْيُصَلِّ مَعَهُ فَإِنَّهَا لَهُ نَافِلَةٌ
اصول : امام ضامن ہوتا ہے لہذا امام کا اعلی درجہ کا ہونایا کم از کم مقتدی کے برابر ہو نا ضروری ہے
اصول : رکوع سجدہ والا اشارہ والے کی اور فرض والا متنفل کی اقتداء نہیں کر سکتا ہے، نیز فرض پڑھنے والا دوسری فرض پڑھنے والے کی اقتداء بھی نہ کرے۔
Chapter on Congregation. A pure person should not pray behind one with urinary incontinence, nor pure women behind a mustahadah, nor a reciter behind an illiterate, nor a clothed person behind a naked one. It is permissible for a mutayammim to lead those who have performed wudu, and one who wiped over khuffs to lead those who washed [their feet]. A standing person may pray behind a sitting one. Evidence for 'a pure person should not pray behind one with urinary incontinence': from Abu Hurayra: the Prophet said: 'The imam is a guarantor and the mu'adhdhin is trusted; O Allah, guide the imams and forgive the mu'adhdhins.' Evidence for 'it is permissible for a mutayammim to lead those with wudu': from Amr ibn al-'As: I had a wet dream on a cold night in the expedition of Dhat al-Salasil, feared death if I bathed, so I performed tayammum and led my companions in Fajr prayer. Evidence for 'a standing person may pray behind a sitting one': (1) from Aisha: ... when Abu Bakr saw him, he began to step back, but the Prophet gestured not to step back; he said: 'Seat me next to him,' so they seated him beside Abu Bakr; Abu Bakr prayed following the Prophet's prayer, and the people followed Abu Bakr, and the Prophet was sitting. (2) from Ibn Abbas: ... Abu Bakr stood, following the Prophet, and the people followed Abu Bakr. (3) from Anas: the Prophet rode a horse, fell, and the right side was scratched; he prayed a prayer sitting, and we prayed behind him sitting; after finishing he said: 'The imam is only appointed to be followed; when he prays standing, pray standing; when he bows, bow; when he raises, raise; when he says Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah, say Rabbana wa laka al-hamd; when he prays sitting, all of you pray sitting.' A person who bows and prostrates should not pray behind one who gestures, nor should one praying fard behind one praying nafl, nor one praying one fard behind one praying a different fard; but one praying nafl may pray behind one praying fard. Evidence for 'one praying fard should not pray behind one praying nafl': from Abu Hurayra: the Prophet said: 'The imam is only appointed to be followed, so do not differ from him.' Evidence: from Jabir: Mu'adh used to pray Isha with the Prophet, then go to his people and lead them in that prayer. Evidence: that Mu'adh used to pray Isha with the Prophet, then go to his people and lead them; it was supererogatory for him and obligatory for them. Evidence for 'one praying nafl may pray behind one praying fard': from Jabir's father: he prayed with the Prophet as a young man; after the prayer, two men were in the mosque who had not prayed; the Prophet called them and asked why; they said they had prayed at their camp; he said: 'Do not do that; when one of you prays at his camp then catches the imam and has not prayed, let him pray with him, for it is a nafl for him.' Principles: The imam is a guarantor, so the imam must be of a higher rank or at least equal to the follower. A person who bows and prostrates cannot follow one who gestures, nor one praying fard follow one praying nafl, nor one praying fard follow another praying a different fard.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage from al-Quduri with its hadith commentaries presents rulings on who may lead or follow in congregational prayer. It begins by stating that a person who is pure (tahir) cannot pray behind one who has urinary incontinence (salis al-bawl), because the imam's state of purity is compromised, and the follower is considered to be praying behind an impure leader. Similarly, pure women cannot pray behind a woman with chronic blood discharge (mustahada), as her state is like that of a minor impurity. A literate reciter cannot pray behind an illiterate (ummi) who may not recite properly, and a clothed person cannot pray behind a naked one, as covering is a prerequisite. However, a person who performed tayammum may lead those who performed wudu, and one who wiped over khuffs may lead those who washed their feet, because their purification is valid and the imam's state does not diminish the follower's prayer. A standing person may pray behind a sitting imam, as proven by multiple hadiths from the Prophet's illness. The passage then prohibits a person who bows and prostrates from following one who gestures due to incapacity, and prohibits one praying an obligatory prayer (fard) from following one praying a supererogatory prayer (nafl) or a different obligatory prayer, due to lack of uniformity of intention. However, one praying nafl may follow one praying fard, as shown in the hadith of Mu'adh, where his prayer was nafl for him but fard for his people. The commentary concludes with usul principles: the imam is a guarantor, so he should be equal or superior in status. These rulings ensure the validity and integrity of congregational prayer.

Key Terms
أُمِّي (ummī): An illiterate person who cannot recite Quran properly.
مُتَنَفِّل (mutanaffil): One performing a supererogatory (nafl) prayer.
سَلَسُ الْبَوْلِ (salis al-bawl): Urinary incontinence; continuous leakage of urine.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, can a person praying a fard prayer follow an imam praying a nafl prayer?
A) Yes, it is permissible and the follower's prayer is valid.
B) No, it is not permissible because intentions differ.
C) Yes, but only if the nafl prayer is a sunnah mu'akkadah.
D) No, it is invalid and both prayers become void.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits several imam–ma'mum pairings to ensure the imam’s state matches or exceeds the follower's, with proof from hadith and the principle that the imam is a guarantor.
