Taharah — Purification
intermediate
10 min
Definition of Travel and Obligation of Qasr
Defines travel distance and states the mandatory qasr for the traveler.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of travel distance, explain the proofs for it, and derive that qasr is fard not a concession.

Core Idea
Travel that changes rulings is three days by camel; qasr is fard, not optional.

This lesson introduces the key concept of shar'i travel in the Hanafi school. We explore the minimum distance that triggers travel concessions, and then examine the ruling that the traveler must shorten four-rakat prayers to two. The lesson also addresses the inter-madhhab dispute over the distance definition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi definition of shar'i travel
The text states: travel is a journey of three days or more by camel, and travel by water is not considered. This is the distance that changes legal rulings.
2
Analyse the three Hanafi proofs for the distance
Three proofs are cited: (1) Hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: a woman may not travel three days without a mahram; (2) Hadith of Aisha: the traveler wipes over khuffs for three days; (3) Practice of Ibn Umar and Ibn Abbas: they shortened in four barid (16 farsakh). These establish three days as the minimum.
The third proof is a qawl sahabi (companion's saying), considered a strong proof in Hanafi usul.
3
Compare with the Shafi'i proof
The Shafi'i school uses a hadith of Abu Hurairah setting one day and one night. The Hanafi response is that the three-day hadiths are more specific and consistent with the duration for wiping over khuffs and other rulings.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference): a person traveling two days is muqim for Hanafis but musafir for Shafi'is.
4
State the Hanafi ruling on qasr
The text declares: 'The obligation of the traveler in every four-rakat prayer is two rakats; it is not permissible to increase beyond them.' This means qasr is fard, not a concession.
Contrast with Shafi'i view: qasr is rukhsah, and itmam (completing four) is permissible.
5
Analyse the proof for qasr
The hadith of Ibn Abbas is cited: 'Allah obligated the prayer on the tongue of your Prophet: in residence, four; in travel, two; in fear, one.' The wording 'two' indicates the original obligation, so adding to it is not allowed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ صَلَاةِ الْمُسَافِرِ
السَّفَرُ الَّذِي تَتَغَيَّرُ بِهِ الْأَحْكَامُ أَنْ يَقْصِدَ الْإِنْسَانُ مَوْضِعًا بَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَ مِصْرِهِ مَسِيرَةُ ثَلَاثَةِ أَيَّامٍ فَصَاعِدًا بِسَيْرِ الْإِبِلِ وَلَا مُعْتَبَرَ فِي ذَلِكَ بِالسَّيْرِ فِي الْمَاءِ لَ وَفَرْضُ الْمُسَافِرِ عِنْدَنَا فِي كُلِّ صَلَاةٍ رُبَاعِيَّةٍ رَكْعَتَانِ لَا يَجُوزُ لَهُ الزِّيَادَةُ عَلَيْهِمَا

وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت السَّفَرُ الَّذِي تَتَغَيَّرُ بِهِ الْأَحْكَامُ ، عَنْ أَبِي سَعِيدٍ الْخُدْرِيِّ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم : « لَا يَحِلُّ لِامْرَأَةٍ تُؤْمِنُ بِاللَّهِ وَالْيَوْمِ الْآخِرِ أَنْ تُسَافِرَ سَفَرًا يَكُونُ ثَلَاثَةَ أَيَّامٍ فَصَاعِدًا إِلَّا وَمَعَهَا أَبُوهَا، أَوِ ابْنُهَا، أَوْ زَوْجُهَا، أَوْ أَخُوهَا، أَوْ ذُو مَحْرَمٍ مِنْهَا،( مسلم شریف، بَابُ سَفَرِ الْمَرْأَةِ مَعَ تَحْرَمٍ إِلَى حَجَ وَغَيْرِهِ، 1340/ بخاري شريف ، بَابٌ فِي كَمْ يَقْصُرُ الصَّلَاةَ ، 1086) وجه:(۲) الحديث لثبوت السَّفَرُ الَّذِي تَتَغَيَّرُ بِهِ الْأَحْكَامُ \ قَالَ: « أَتَيْتُ عَائِشَةَ أَسْأَلُهَا عَن الْمَسْحِ عَلَى الْخُفَّيْنِ.... فَقَالَ: جَعَلَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم ثَلَاثَةَ أَيَّامٍ وَلَيَالِيَهُنَّ لِلْمُسَافِرِ، وَيَوْمًا وَلَيْلَةً لِلْمُقِيمِ، قَالَ : وَكَانَ سُفْيَانُ إِذَا ذَكَرَ عَمْرًا أَلْفَ عَلَيْهِ ، ، ) مسلم شریف ، بَابُ التَّوْقِيتِ فِي الْمَسْحِ عَلَى الْخُفَّيْنِ،نمبر276/سنن ابوداود، بَابٌ فِي تَرْكِ الْوُضُوءِ مِمَّا مَسَّتِ النَّارُ، نمبر 187)
وجه:(۳) قول الصحابي لثبوت السَّفَرُ الَّذِي تَتَغَيَّرُ بِهِ الْأَحْكَامُ \ وَكَانَ ابْنُ عُمَرَ وَابْنُ عَبَّاسٍ يَقْصُرَانِ وَيُفْطِرَانِ فِي أَرْبَعَةِ بُرُدٍ وَهِيَ سِتَّةَ عَشَرَ فَرْسَخًا ، بخاري شريف بَابٌ فِي كَمْ يَقْصُرُ الصَّلَاةَ ،نمبر 1086) وجه (1) دليل الشافعى الحديث لثبوت السَّفَرُ الَّذِي تَتَغَيَّرُ بِهِ الْأَحْكَامُ اعَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ رضي الله عنهما قَالَ: قَالَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «لَا يَحِلُّ لِامْرَأَةٍ تُؤْمِنُ بِاللَّهِ وَالْيَوْمِ الْآخِرِ أَنْ تُسَافِرَ مَسِيرَةَ يَوْمٍ وَلَيْلَةٍ لَيْسَ مَعَهَا حُرْمَةٌ (بخاري شريف ، بَابٌ فِي كَمْ يَقْصُرُ الصَّلَاةَ ، غمبر 1088)
وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت فَرْضُ الْمُسَافِرِ عِنْدَنَا فِي كُلِ صَلَاةٍ \ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ قَالَ: « فَرَضَ اللهُ الصَّلَاةَ عَلَى لِسَانِ نَبِيِّكُمْ في الحَضَر أَرْبَعًا، وَفي السَّفَر رَكْعَتَيْنِ، وَفِي الْخَوْفِ رَكْعَةً، ) مسلم شريف ، بَابُ صَلَاةِ الْمُسَافِرِينَ وَقَصْرِهَا ، نمبر 687)
اصول : سفر شرعی کامرتکب مسافر کہلاتا ہے، مسافر سفر میں قصر یعنی چار رکعت والی نماز کو دور کعت پڑھے۔
اصول سفر شرعی کا مسافر اپنی رباعی نماز میں قصر کرے اتمام جائز نہیں ہے امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک۔
Chapter of the traveler's prayer. The travel by which the rulings change is that a person intends a place between which and his town is a distance of three days or more by camel travel, and travel by water is not considered in that. And the obligation of the traveler with us in every four-rakat prayer is two rakat; it is not permissible for him to increase beyond them. Proof (1): Hadith to establish the travel by which rulings change: from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri that the Prophet said: 'It is not permissible for a woman who believes in Allah and the Last Day to travel a journey of three days or more unless with her is her father, or her son, or her husband, or her brother, or a mahram.' (Muslim, Sahih; Bukhari, 1086). Proof (2): Hadith to establish the travel by which rulings change: 'I came to Aisha to ask her about wiping over the khuffs... she said: The Messenger of Allah made three days and their nights for the traveler, and one day and one night for the resident.' (Muslim, 276; Abu Dawud, 187). Proof (3): Saying of a Companion to establish the travel by which rulings change: Ibn Umar and Ibn Abbas used to shorten and break fast in four barid, which is sixteen farsakh. (Bukhari, 1086). Proof (1): Shafi'i's proof: Hadith from Abu Hurairah that the Prophet said: 'It is not permissible for a woman who believes in Allah and the Last Day to travel a distance of one day and one night without a mahram.' (Bukhari, 1088). Proof (1): Hadith to establish the obligation of the traveler with us in every prayer: from Ibn Abbas: 'Allah obligated the prayer on the tongue of your Prophet: in residence, four; in travel, two; in fear, one.' (Muslim, 687). Principle: One who undertakes a legal travel is called a traveler; the traveler in travel shortens, i.e., prays two rakat instead of four. Principle: The traveler in legal travel must shorten his four-rakat prayer; completing (itmam) is not permissible according to Imam Abu Hanifa.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage is a composite of a ruling statement and its proofs. It opens with the chapter on the traveler's prayer. The author, Al-Quduri, first defines the distance of travel that triggers changes in rulings: a journey of three days or more by camel, not counting water travel. This is the Hanafi position. Immediately after, he states the ruling: for a traveler, the fard (obligation) in every four-rakat prayer is two rakat, and it is not permissible to add to them. This is a clear statement that qasr is mandatory, not optional. The author then adduces multiple proofs. First, three proofs for the three-day definition: (1) a hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri restricting women's travel to three days or more without a mahram, which implicitly sets the minimum travel distance; (2) a hadith from Aisha about the duration of wiping over khuffs showing three days for the traveler; (3) the practice of Ibn Umar and Ibn Abbas who shortened in four barid (16 farsakh). The author then records the Shafi'i proof for the definition: a hadith from Abu Hurairah setting the distance at one day and one night. This is the inter-madhhab dispute on the minimum travel distance. After this, the author provides a Hanafi proof for the ruling of qasr itself: Ibn Abbas's hadith stating that Allah made prayer four in residence and two in travel, indicating that qasr is the original obligation for the traveler. Finally, two Urdu usul notes summarize: the traveler must perform qasr, and according to Imam Abu Hanifa, completing the prayer (itmam) in travel is not permissible.

Key Terms
سفر (safar): Legal travel that changes rulings, defined as a journey of three days or more by camel.
قصر (qasr): Shortening the four-rakat fard prayers to two rakats in travel.
رباعیہ (rubā‘iyyah): Any prayer that normally consists of four rakats (Zuhr, Asr, Isha).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the minimum distance for travel (safar) that allows qasr?
A) One day and one night by camel
B) Two days by camel
C) Three days by camel
D) Four barid (16 farsakh)

Key Takeaway
Travel that changes rulings is three days by camel; qasr is fard, not a concession.

Washing the Deceased: Procedure and Proofs
Ruling with proofs for washing the deceased

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the Hanafi procedure for washing the deceased, explain the exception of madmadah and istinshaq, and cite the supporting proofs.

Core Idea
The deceased's wudu excludes mouth and nose rinsing to prevent harm; a cloth wipe suffices.

This passage from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar covers the sunnah method of washing the deceased. It details the physical setup, the special wudu without oral/nasal rinsing, and the pouring of water over the body. Understanding these steps ensures the ritual is performed correctly according to the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the steps of ghusl al-mayyit
List the sequential actions described: placement on a bed, covering private parts, removing clothes, performing wudu, and pouring water.
The order is important for correct practice.
2
Recognize the rule for covering the private parts
The passage states a cloth is placed over the private parts before undressing. This preserves modesty.
This is based on the practice of Ayyub (Musannaf Abd ar-Razzaq).
3
Understand the wudu exception
Note that madmadah and istinshaq are not performed; instead, a clean cloth wipes the mouth and nostrils. The proof from Sa'id ibn Jubayr explicitly excludes these.
The exception is due to the inability of the deceased to expel water, preventing harm.
4
Note the pouring sequence
Water is poured starting from the head, then the rest of the body, beginning with the right side, as per the hadith of Umm 'Atiyyah.
The instruction to start with the right side mirrors wudu for prayer.
5
Locate the hadith proofs for each step
Match each procedural element to its supporting evidence: placing (hadith from Aisha and Ayyub), wudu exception (Sa'id ibn Jubayr), pouring (Umm 'Atiyyah).
This exercise builds proof-based understanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَصل فِي الغُسْل
فَإِذَا أَرَادُوا غُسْلَهُ وَضَعُوهُ عَلَى السَّرِيرِ وَجَعَلُوا عَلَى عَوْرَتِهِ خِرْقَةً وَنَزَعُوا ثِيَابَهُ قَوْلُهُ وَوَضَتُوهُ وَلا يُمضمِضُوهُ وَلا يُنشِقُوهُ ثُمَّ يُفِيضُونَ الْمَاءَ عَلَى رَأْسِهِ وَسَائِرٍ جَسَدِهِ
وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت فَإِذَا أَرَادُوا غُسْلَهُ وَضَعُوهُ عَلَى السَّرِيرِ اسَمِعْتُ عَائِشَةَ تَقُولُ: «لَمَّا أَرَادُوا غَسْلَ النَّي ..... أَنِ اغْسِلُوا النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَعَلَيْهِ ثِيَابُهُ، فَقَامُوا إِلَى رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَعَسَلُوهُ وَعَلَيْهِ قَمِيصُهُ (سنن ابوداؤد: باب في ستر الميت عند غسله،نمبر 3141)
وجه (۲) قول الصحابي لثبوت فَإِذَا أَرَادُوا غُسْلَهُ وَضَعُوهُ عَلَى السَّرِيرِاعَنْ أَيُّوبَ قَالَ: «رَأَيْتُهُ يُغَسِلُ مَيْتًا فَأَلْقَى عَلَى فَرْجِهِ خِرْقَةً وَعَلَى وَجْهِهِ خِرْقَةً أُخْرَى، وَوَضَّأَهُ وُضُوءَ الصَّلَاةِ، ثُمَّ بَدَأَ
بِيَامِنِهِ» (مصنف عبدالرزاق: باب غسل الميت،نمبر 6081)
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَوَضَنُوهُ وَلَا يُضْمِضُوهُ وَلَا يُنَشِقُوهُ \ عَنْ سَعِيدِ بْنِ جُبَيْرٍ، قَالَ: «يُوَضَّأُ الْمَيِّتُ وُضُوءَهُ لِلصَّلَاةِ، إِلَّا أَنَّهُ لَا يُضْمَضُ وَلَا يَسْتَنْشِقُ» (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه: ما أول ما يبدأ به من غسل الميت،نمبر 10897)
وجه (۲) قول التابعي لثبوت وَوَضَتُوهُ وَلا يُمَضْمِضُوهُ وَلا يُنشِقُوهُ \ عَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ، قَالَ: «لَا يُضْمَضُ الْمَيِّتُ، وَلا يَسْتَنْشِقُ، وَلَكِنْ يُؤْخَذُ خِرْقَةٌ نَظِيفَةٌ، فَيُمْسَحُ بِمَا فَمُهُ وَمَنْخِرَاهُ» (مصنف
ابن ابي شيبه ما قالوا في الميت كم يغسل مرة وما يجعل في الماء مما يغسل به، نمبر 10907) وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت ثُمَّ يُفِيضُونَ الْمَاءَ عَلَى رَأْسِهِ \ عَنْ أُمّ عَطِيَّةَ هِي قَالَتْ: «قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فِي غُسْلِ ابْنَتِهِ: ابْدَأْنَ بِمَيَامِنِهَا وَمَوَاضِعِ الْوُضُوءِ مِنْهَا . » (بخاري شريف: باب يبدأ بميامن الميت، نمبر 1255,مسلم شريف: باب في غسل الميت،نمبر 939)
وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت ثُمَّ يُفيضُونَ الْمَاءَ عَلَى رَأْسِهِ \ عَنْ أُمّ عَطِيَّةَ هِي قَالَتْ: «دَخَلَ عَلَيْنَا رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَنَحْنُ نُغَسِلُ ابْنَتَهُ فَقَالَ: اغْسِلْنَهَا ثَلَاثًا، أَوْ خَمْسًا، أَوْأَكْثَرَ مِنْ ذَلِكَ بِمَاءٍ
وَسِدْرٍ، وَاجْعَلْنَ فِي الْآخِرَةِ كَافُورًا، (بخاري شريف : باب ما يستحب أن يغسل وترا، 1254) اصول : جب میت کو غسل دینا ہو تو پہلے دھونی دیے ہوئے تخت پر لٹا دے، اس کے ستر پر کپڑا ڈال دے اور پھر میت کے کپڑے جو پہنے تھے اتار دے۔
Section on Washing. And when they intend to wash him, they place him on the bed, place a cloth over his private parts, and remove his clothes. His statement: and they perform wudu for him and they do not rinse his mouth nor his nose. Then they pour water over his head and the rest of his body. Proof: (1) the hadith for proof of placing him on the bed: I heard Aisha say: When they intended to wash the Prophet ... that they should wash the Prophet while he was wearing his clothes, so they stood to the Messenger of Allah and washed him while he was wearing his shirt. (Sunan Abi Dawud, no. 3141) Proof: (2) the saying of a Companion for proof of placing him on the bed: from Ayyub, he said: I saw him washing a deceased person, so he threw a cloth over his private parts and another cloth over his face, performed wudu for him like wudu for prayer, then began with his right side. (Musannaf Abd ar-Razzaq, no. 6081) Proof: (1) the hadith for proof of performing wudu for him and not rinsing his mouth nor nose: from Sa'id ibn Jubayr, he said: The deceased is given wudu like wudu for prayer, except that he does not rinse his mouth nor does he perform istinshaq. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, no. 10897) Proof: (2) the saying of a tabi'i for proof of performing wudu for him and not rinsing his mouth nor nose: from Ibrahim, he said: The deceased is not rinsed nor does he perform istinshaq, but a clean cloth is taken and wiped over his mouth and nostrils. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, no. 10907) Proof: (1) the hadith for proof of pouring water over his head: from Umm 'Atiyyah, she said: The Messenger of Allah said regarding washing his daughter: Start with her right side and the parts washed in wudu. (Bukhari, no. 1255; Muslim, no. 939) Proof: (2) the hadith for proof of pouring water over his head: from Umm 'Atiyyah, she said: The Messenger of Allah entered upon us while we were washing his daughter and said: Wash her three times, or five, or more than that with water and sidr, and put camphor in the last wash. (Bukhari, no. 1254) Principle: When one intends to wash the deceased, first lay him on a fumigated wooden bed, place a cloth over his private parts, and then remove the clothes he was wearing.
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This section on ghusl (washing the deceased) provides the proper procedure as per the Hanafi school. The rulings are stated concisely by al-Quduri and supported by proofs. The steps are: (1) Place the deceased on a bed (sarir) – the bed should be fumigated (as per the Urdu principle). (2) Cover the private parts with a cloth. (3) Remove the deceased's clothes while maintaining cover. (4) Perform wudu for the deceased, but crucially, do not rinse the mouth or nose. Instead, a clean cloth is used to wipe the mouth and nostrils. This exception is because the deceased cannot expel water, and it may cause harm or leakage. (5) Pour water over the head and then the rest of the body, starting with the right side. The number of washes can be odd (3,5, etc.) with water and sidr, and camphor in the last wash. The proofs include hadith from Aisha (placing on bed, washing with shirt), the practice of Ayyub (covering, wudu, starting right), the explicit exception of mouth/nose rinsing from Sa'id ibn Jubayr and Ibrahim, and the instruction to start with the right side from Umm 'Atiyyah. The Urdu principle reinforces the method.

Key Terms
غسل الميت (ghusl al-mayyit): The ritual washing of a deceased Muslim's body before burial, following specific sunnah procedures.
مضمضة واستنشاق (madmadah wa istinshaq): Rinsing the mouth and drawing water into the nose, respectively. These are excluded from the wudu of the deceased according to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on performing madmadah and istinshaq during the wudu of the deceased?
A) They are obligatory (wajib) just as in living wudu.
B) They are recommended (sunnah) but can be omitted.
C) They are not performed; a cloth is used to wipe the mouth and nose instead.
D) They are allowed but makruh.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uniquely excludes madmadah and istinshaq from the deceased's wudu, based on explicit reports from the Salaf, and substitutes a cloth wipe for purification.

intermediate
8 min
The Washing (Ghusl) of the Deceased: Procedure and Evidences
Explains the rulings for washing the deceased with supporting hadith and athar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the Hanafi procedure for washing the deceased, state the evidence for each step, and distinguish between the ruling categories (fard kifayah vs sunnah).

Core Idea
Washing the deceased is a communal obligation; the sunnah method with sidr water and odd numbers is established by hadith and early practice.

Washing the deceased (ghusl al-mayyit) is a communal obligation (fard kifayah) upon the living. This passage from Al-Quduri outlines the recommended (sunnah) procedure and then provides the evidential basis—hadith and statements of the Companions and early scholars—for each step. Understanding these proofs grounds the practice in the Sunnah and clarifies why certain actions, like rinsing the mouth, are omitted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overall obligation and its category
Recognize that washing the deceased is fard kifayah (communal obligation), while the described method is the sunnah (recommended) way.
The obligation is discharged by some; the method is meritorious.
2
List the procedural steps in order
Extract the sequence: place on bed, cover private parts, remove clothes, perform modified wudu, pour water over head and body, fumigate bed odd times, use sidr in water, wash head and beard with khitmi.
Each step has a proof.
3
Locate the evidence for each step
For each action, identify the supporting hadith (e.g., Umm Atiyya for washing with sidr) or athar (e.g., Sa'id ibn Jubayr for omitting madmadah).
Note the chain: hadith, companion statement, tabi'i statement.
4
Understand why certain actions are omitted
The deceased is not made to rinse the mouth or sniff water because he cannot expel it, and the purpose is symbolic cleansing, not ritual purification of a living person.
This distinguishes from living wudu.
5
Note the hierarchy of cleansing agents and the reasoning
The preferred agent is sidr; if unavailable, khitmi or ushnan may be used. This is based on the practice of early Muslims and the principle of using what is available without causing hardship.
The hadith explicitly mentions sidr; substitutes are from athar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الغسل. فَإِذَا أَرَادُوا غُسْلَهُ وَضَعُوهُ عَلَى السَّرِيرِ وَجَعَلُوا عَلَى عَوْرَتِهِ خِرْقَةً وَنَزَعُوا ثِيَابَهُ. وَيُوَضَّوْنَهُ وَلَا يُمَضْمِضُونَهُ وَلَا يُنَشِّقُونَهُ. ثُمَّ يُفِيضُونَ الْمَاءَ عَلَى رَأْسِهِ وَسَائِرِ جَسَدِهِ. وَيُجَمِّرُ سَرِيرَهُ وِتْرًا. وَيُغْلَى الْمَاءُ بِالسَّدْرِ أَوْ بِالْخَرْضِ فَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ فَالْمَاءُ الْقَرَاحُ. وَيُغْسَلُ رَأْسُهُ وَلِحْيَتُهُ بِالْخِطْمِيِّ.

وجه الحديث لثبوت فإذا أرادوا غسله وضعوه على السرير: سمعت عائشة تقول: لما أرادوا غسل النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: اغسلوا النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وعليه ثيابه، فقاموا إلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فغسلوه وعليه قميصه. (سنن أبي داود: باب ستر الميت عند غسله، رقم 3141)
وجه قول الصحابي لثبوت فإذا أرادوا غسله وضعوه على السرير: عن أيوب قال: رأيته يغسل ميتًا فألقى على فرجه خرقة وعلى وجهه خرقة أخرى، ووضأه وضوء الصلاة، ثم بدأ بيامنه. (مصنف عبدالرزاق: باب غسل الميت، رقم 6081)
وجه الحديث لثبوت ويوضؤونه ولا يضمضونه ولا ينشقونه: عن سعيد بن جبير قال: يوضأ الميت وضوءه للصلاة إلا أنه لا يضمض ولا يستنشق. (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة: ما أول ما يبدأ به من غسل الميت، رقم 10897)
وجه قول التابعي لثبوت ويوضؤونه ولا يضمضونه ولا ينشقونه: عن إبراهيم قال: لا يضمض الميت ولا يستنشق، ولكن يؤخذ خرقة نظيفة، فيمسح بها فمه ومنخاره. (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة: ما قالوا في الميت كم يغسل مرة وما يجعل في الماء مما يغسل به، رقم 10907)
وجه الحديث لثبوت ثم يفيضون الماء على رأسه: عن أم عطية قالت: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في غسل ابنته: ابدأن بميامنها ومواضع الوضوء منها. (البخاري: باب يبدأ بميامن الميت، رقم 1255، مسلم: باب في غسل الميت، رقم 939)
وجه الحديث لثبوت ثم يفيضون الماء على رأسه: عن أم عطية قالت: دخل علينا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ونحن نغسل ابنته فقال: اغسلنها ثلاثًا أو خمسًا أو أكثر من ذلك بماء وسدر، واجعلن في الآخرة كافورًا. (البخاري: باب ما يستحب أن يغسل وترًا، رقم 1254)
وجه قول الصحابية لثبوت ويجمر سريره وترًا: عن أسماء بنت أبي بكر أنها قالت لأهلها: أجمروا ثيابي إذا أنا مت، ثم كفنوني ثم حنطوني، ولا تذروا على كفني حناطًا. (مصنف عبدالرزاق باب الميت لا يتبع بالمجمرة، رقم 6152، مصنف ابن أبي شيبة: في الحنوط، كيف يصنع به؟ وأين يجعل؟، رقم 11020)
وجه الحديث لثبوت ويجمر سريره وترًا: عن جابر قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: إذا أجمرتم الميت فأوتروا. (سنن البيهقي: باب الحنوط للميت، رقم 6702)
وجه الحديث لثبوت ويغلى الماء بالسدر أو بالخرض: عن أم عطية الأنصارية قالت: دخل علينا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم حين توفيت ابنته فقال: اغسلنها ثلاثًا أو خمسًا أو أكثر من ذلك إن رأيتن ذلك بماء وسدر، واجعلن في الآخرة كافورًا أو شيئًا من كافور. (البخاري: باب غسل الميت ووضوئه بالماء والسدر، رقم 1253، مسلم: باب في غسل الميت، 939)
وجه قول التابعي لثبوت ويغلى الماء بالسدر أو بالخرض: عن الحسن أنه قال في الميت: أُغسله بسدر، فإن لم يوجد سدر فخطمي، فإن لم يكن خطمي فبأشنان. (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة: في الميت إذا لم يوجد له سدر يغسل بغيره، خطمي أو أشنان، رقم 10920)
وجه قول التابعي لثبوت ويغلى الماء بالسدر أو بالخرض: عن إبراهيم قال: إن لم يكن سدر فلا يضرك. (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة: في الميت إذا لم يوجد له سدر يغسل بغيره، خطمي أو أشنان، رقم 10918)
وجه قول التابعي لثبوت ويغسل رأسه ولحيته بالخطمي: عن الأسود قال: قلت لعائشة: يغسل رأس الميت بخطمي؟ فقالت: لا تعنتوا ميتكم. (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة: في الميت إذا لم يوجد له سدر يغسل بغيره، خطمي أو أشنان، رقم 10917)

أصول: جب میت کو غسل دینا ہو تو پہلے دھونی دیے ہوئے تخت پر لٹا دے، اس کے ستر پر کپڑا ڈال دے اور پھر میت کے کپڑے جو پہنے تھے اتار دے۔
أصول: غسل کے لیے بغیر مضمضہ و استنشاق کے وضو کرائے اور پھر پورے بدن پر پانی بہائے۔
لغت: سدرة: بیری کا درخت، حرص: ایک قسم کی گھاس ہے جس کو اشنان بھی کہتے ہیں۔
Chapter on washing (the deceased). When they intend to wash him, they place him on the bed, put a cloth over his private parts, and remove his clothes. And they perform wudu for him, but they do not rinse his mouth nor his nose. Then they pour water over his head and the rest of his body. And they fumigate his bed with incense an odd number of times. And water is boiled with sidr (lote-tree leaves) or with khard (a type of herb), and if none is available, then with pure water. And his head and beard are washed with khitmi (marshmallow plant).

Evidence of the hadith for establishing: 'When they intend to wash him, they place him on the bed' – I heard Aisha say: 'When they wanted to wash the Prophet (peace be upon him), he said: Wash the Prophet (peace be upon him) while he is in his clothes, so they stood up to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and washed him while he was in his shirt.' (Sunan Abi Dawud: Chapter on covering the deceased during his washing, no. 3141)
Evidence of the statement of a companion for establishing: 'When they intend to wash him, they place him on the bed' – from Ayyub, he said: 'I saw him washing a deceased person, so he threw a cloth over his private parts and another cloth over his face, and performed wudu for him like the wudu for prayer, then began with his right side.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq: Chapter on washing the deceased, no. 6081)
Evidence of the hadith for establishing: 'And they perform wudu for him, but they do not rinse his mouth nor his nose' – from Sa'id ibn Jubayr, he said: 'The deceased is made to perform wudu like the wudu for prayer, except that he is not made to rinse his mouth nor his nose.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba: What is first begun with in washing the deceased, no. 10897)
Evidence of the statement of a Tabi'i for establishing: 'And they perform wudu for him, but they do not rinse his mouth nor his nose' – from Ibrahim, he said: 'The deceased is not made to rinse his mouth nor his nose, but a clean cloth is taken and his mouth and nostrils are wiped with it.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba: What they said about the deceased: how many times is he washed and what is put in the water for washing, no. 10907)
Evidence of the hadith for establishing: 'Then they pour water over his head' – from Umm Atiyya, she said: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said concerning the washing of his daughter: Begin with her right side and the places of wudu.' (Bukhari: Chapter on beginning with the right side of the deceased, no. 1255; Muslim: Chapter on washing the deceased, no. 939)
Evidence of the hadith for establishing: 'Then they pour water over his head' – from Umm Atiyya, she said: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) entered upon us while we were washing his daughter and said: Wash her three times, or five, or more than that, with water and sidr, and put some camphor in the last (wash).' (Bukhari: Chapter on what is recommended to wash in odd numbers, no. 1254)
Evidence of the statement of a female companion for establishing: 'And they fumigate his bed an odd number of times' – from Asma bint Abi Bakr that she said to her family: 'Fumigate my clothes when I die, then shroud me, then embalm me, and do not put any henna on my shroud.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq: Chapter on the deceased not being followed with a censer, no. 6152; Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba: Concerning the embalming, how it is done and where it is placed, no. 11020)
Evidence of the hadith for establishing: 'And they fumigate his bed an odd number of times' – from Jabir, he said: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: When you fumigate (the place of) the deceased, do it an odd number of times.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi: Chapter on embalming the deceased, no. 6702)
Evidence of the hadith for establishing: 'And water is boiled with sidr or with khard' – from Umm Atiyya al-Ansariyya, she said: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) entered upon us when his daughter had died and said: Wash her three times, or five, or more than that if you see fit, with water and sidr, and put some camphor in the last (wash).' (Bukhari: Chapter on washing the deceased and his wudu with water and sidr, no. 1253; Muslim: Chapter on washing the deceased, 939)
Evidence of the statement of a Tabi'i for establishing: 'And water is boiled with sidr or with khard' – from al-Hasan, that he said concerning the deceased: 'I wash him with sidr, and if sidr is not found, then with khitmi, and if khitmi is not found, then with ushnan.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba: Concerning the deceased if sidr is not available for washing, he is washed with something else, khitmi or ushnan, no. 10920)
Evidence of the statement of a Tabi'i for establishing: 'And water is boiled with sidr or with khard' – from Ibrahim, he said: 'If there is no sidr, it does not harm you.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba: Concerning the deceased if sidr is not available for washing, he is washed with something else, khitmi or ushnan, no. 10918)
Evidence of the statement of a Tabi'i for establishing: 'And his head and beard are washed with khitmi' – from al-Aswad, he said: 'I said to Aisha: Should the head of the deceased be washed with khitmi? She said: Do not cause hardship to your dead.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba: Concerning the deceased if sidr is not available for washing, he is washed with something else, khitmi or ushnan, no. 10917)

Principles: When one wants to wash the deceased, first place him on a fumigated bed, cover his private parts with a cloth, then remove the clothes he was wearing.
Principles: For the washing, perform wudu without rinsing the mouth and nose, then pour water over the entire body.
Lexicon: Sidra: the lote tree, Khard: a type of grass also called ushnan (a plant used as soap).
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage is from a Hanafi fiqh text on the washing (ghusl) of the deceased. It presents the rulings as found in the matn of Al-Quduri and then provides supporting evidence from hadith and the sayings of the Companions and early scholars (Tabi'un). The author first lists the procedural steps: placing the deceased on a bed, covering the private parts, removing clothes, performing a modified wudu (without rinsing mouth or nose), pouring water over the head and entire body, fumigating the bed an odd number of times, boiling water with sidr (lote leaves) or other cleansing agents, and washing the head and beard with khitmi (marshmallow plant). The proofs follow each step, demonstrating that these actions are established by the Sunnah. The hadith of Umm Atiyya is central, showing the Prophet's instruction for washing his daughter with water and sidr. The companion and Tabi'i statements confirm the omission of mouth rinsing and nose sniffing because the deceased cannot expel water. The use of sidr, khitmi, or ushnan as alternatives is based on the practice of early Muslims. The Urdu principles at the end summarize the procedure. As a teacher, note that the overall obligation of washing the deceased is a communal duty (fard kifayah), while the specific method described here is the sunnah (recommended) way, and it is meritorious to follow it.

Key Terms
غسل الميت (ghusl al-mayyit): The ritual washing of a deceased Muslim, which is a communal obligation (fard kifayah) performed by surviving Muslims.
سدر (sidr): Leaves of the lote tree (Ziziphus spina-christi), used in the water for washing the deceased as a cleansing agent, recommended by the Prophet.
وضوء الميت (wudu' al-mayyit): The act of performing wudu on the deceased before the full body wash, but without rinsing the mouth and nose.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith of Umm Atiyya, how many times should the deceased be washed?
A) Once, with camphor
B) Two or four times
C) Three, five, or more (odd number)
D) Only once with plain water

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi procedure for washing the deceased is based on specific hadith and early practice, emphasizing the use of sidr water, odd-numbered fumigation, and omission of mouth rinsing.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
6 min
Washing the Deceased: Water and Head/Beard
Rulings on preparing water and washing the head and beard of the deceased with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended water additives for washing the deceased and identify the proofs from hadith and athar.

Core Idea
Sidr water is sunnah for washing the deceased; pure water suffices when unavailable; head and beard washed with khitmi.

This passage outlines the sunnah procedures for ghusl of the deceased, focusing on the preparation of water and the washing of the head and beard. The imam cites multiple hadith and statements from the Companions and Successors to establish these recommendations. Understanding these proofs shows how the school derives sunnah rulings from primary sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended acts
Notice the three procedures: perfuming the bier with an odd number, boiling water with sidr or khartam, and washing the head and beard with khitmi.
These are not obligatory but strongly recommended (sunnah muakkadah).
2
Locate the proofs for each act
For perfuming, the hadith of Jabir commands an odd number. For water, the hadith of Umm 'Atiyya instructs washing the Prophet's daughter with water and sidr. For khitmi, the athar from al-Hasan and the question to Aisha provide support.
Some proofs are marfu' (Prophetic), others are mawquf (Companion) or athar (Successor).
3
Analyze the legal indication (wajh al-dalalah)
The Prophet's command 'ighsilnaha bi ma'in wa sidr' shows a general recommendation. The imperative form (amr) in a context of instruction indicates sunnah, not obligation, due to other evidence making ghusl fard kifayah.
Hanafi usul: al-amr yufidu al-wujub unless there is a qarina to sunniyat; here the overall obligation is established separately.
4
Note the ikhtilaf and the Hanafi position
Some schools allow pure water as the default; Hanafis prefer sidr but permit pure water when sidr is unavailable. This is reflected in the text: 'fa in lam yakun fa al-mā' al-qurāḥ'.
The Hanafi mufta bihi is as stated in the matn of al-Quduri.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الغسل وَيُجَمِّرُ سَرِيرَهُ وِتْرًا وَيُغْلَى الْمَاءُ بِالسَّدْرِ أَوْ بِالْحَرْضِ فَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ فَالْمَاءُ الْقَرَاحُ وَيُغْسَلُ رَأْسُهُ وَلِحْيَتُهُ بِالْخِطْمِيِّ

عَنْ أَسْمَاءَ بِنْتِ أَبِي بَكْرٍ أَنَّهَا قَالَتْ لِأَهْلِهَا: «أَجْمِرُوا ثِيَابِي إِذَا أَنَا مِتُّ، ثُمَّ كَفِّنُونِي ثُمَّ حَنِّطُونِي، وَلَا تَذَرُوا عَلَى كَفَنِي حِنَاطًا»
عَنْ جَابِرٍ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: "إِذَا أَجْمَرْتُمُ الْمَيِّتَ فَأَوْتِرُوا"
عَنْ أُمِّ عَطِيَّةَ الْأَنْصَارِيَّةِ قَالَتْ: «دَخَلَ عَلَيْنَا رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم حِينَ تُوُفِّيَتِ ابْنَتُهُ فَقَالَ: اغْسِلْنَهَا ثَلَاثًا، أَوْ خَمْسًا، أَوْ أَكْثَرَ مِنْ ذَلِكَ إِنْ رَأَيْتُنَّ ذَلِكَ بِمَاءٍ وَسِدْرٍ، وَاجْعَلْنَ فِي الْآخِرَةِ كَافُورًا، أَوْ شَيْئًا مِنْ كَافُورٍ»
عَنِ الْحَسَنِ، أَنَّهُ قَالَ فِي الْمَيِّتِ: «أُغَسِلُهُ بِسِدْرٍ، فَإِنْ لَمْ يُوجَدْ سِدْرٌ، فَخَطْمِيٌّ، فَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ خَطْمِيٌّ، فَبِأَشْنَانٍ»
عَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ، قَالَ: «إِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ سِدْرٌ، فَلَا يَضُرُّكَ»
عَنِ الْأَسْوَدِ، قَالَ: قُلْتُ لِعَائِشَةَ: يُغْسَلُ رَأْسُ الْمَيِّتِ بِخِطْمِيٍّ؟ فَقَالَتْ: «لَا تَعْتَنِتُوا مَيْتَكُمْ»

اصول: غسل کے لیے بغیر مضمضہ و استنشاق کے وضو کرائے اور پھر پورے بدن پر پانی بہائے۔ لغت: سدرة : بیری کا درخت، حرص : ایک قسم کی گھاس ہے جس کو اشنان بھی کہتے ہیں۔
Section on washing. He perfumes his bier with an odd number. Water is boiled with sidr or khartam; if neither is available, then pure water. He washes his head and beard with khitmi. From Asma bint Abi Bakr: 'Perfume my clothes when I die, then shroud me, then embalm me, and do not leave any hinā' on my shroud.' From Jabir: The Prophet said: 'When you perfume the deceased, do so with an odd number.' From Umm 'Atiyya: The Prophet said about washing his daughter: 'Wash her with water and sidr, and in the last use camphor.' From al-Hasan: 'I wash the deceased with sidr; if not available, with khitmi; if not, with ashnan.' From Ibrahim: 'If there is no sidr, it does not matter.' From al-Aswad: I asked Aisha about washing the deceased's head with khitmi; she said: 'Do not burden your dead.' Principles: Perform wudu without rinsing mouth and nose, then pour water over the whole body. Vocabulary: sidr: lotus tree; khartam: a type of grass also called ashnan.
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage from al-Quduri presents the recommended method for washing the deceased, supported by ahadith and athar. The ruling: the bier is perfumed with an odd number of incense applications. Water is boiled with sidr (lote leaves) or khartam (a cleansing herb); if neither is available, plain water suffices. The head and beard are washed with khitmi (marsh mallow). The proofs cited include the practice of Asma (a Companion), a direct hadith commanding odd-numbered perfuming, the famous hadith of Umm 'Atiyya on washing the Prophet's daughter, and statements from tabi'un (al-Hasan, Ibrahim) and a narration from Aisha. The Urdu note adds that wudu is performed without rinsing the mouth and nose, and then water is poured over the entire body. The vocabulary clarifies that sidr is the lote tree and khartam is also called ashnan.

Key Terms
سدر (sidr): Ziziphus jujuba or lote tree; its leaves are used in washing the deceased.
حرض (khartam): A type of herb used for cleansing; synonymous with ashnan.
خطمي (khitmi): Marsh mallow (Althea officinalis); used for washing the head and beard.
قراح (qurāḥ): Pure, unadulterated water.
تجمير (tajmīr): Perfuming with incense; here, perfuming the bier of the deceased.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the default water used for washing the deceased if sidr or khartam is unavailable?
A) Zamzam water
B) Pure water (al-mā' al-qurāḥ)
C) Rose water
D) Water mixed with camphor

Key Takeaway
The recommended practice for washing the deceased includes using sidr water and perfuming the bier with odd numbers; pure water suffices when sidr is unavailable.
